# 鸣鹤余音

**"The Lingering Cry of the Crane: A Collection of Daoist Songs**
*Original Title: Wūhè Jǐyīn (呜鹤给音)*
*Compiled by Yuan Peng Zhizhong (元彭致中)*
*Nine Volumes*
*Source: *Zhengtong Daozang* (正统道藏), Taixuan Section (太玄部)*

---

**《Xié Hóng》 (解红) – *Untangling the Red***
**By Lǚ Chún Yáng (吕纯阳)**

*Dòng Tiān Shēn Chù* (洞天深处) – *In the depths of the Celestial Cavern,*
The Dao is not distant—yet within arm’s reach, few can awaken.
Like a child lost in inner visions, one must rely on the artisan’s skill and labor.
Waiting eagerly for dawn’s light, when a single ray of yang illuminates the path to the mysterious.
All treasures lie hidden in the fathomless jade-green waves.

At that moment, the master descends—
Earth’s thunder shakes the mountain peaks, rain pours forth.
Gradually, the golden buds are nourished, now emerging from the soil.
Like a babe plucked from the earth, carried in a basket to depart.
Toward the true realm of six yangs, where the cauldron’s fire simmers.
The essence is refined, east and west, south and north—
Laying out the Eight Trigrams and Nine Palaces,
To discern the lineage of the ancestors.
Within the Ten Celestial Stems, left and right are divided,
To reveal the Dragon and the Tiger.
With the Black Tortoise following and the Vermilion Bird leading,
Auspicious clouds spread.
On the River of the Curved Banks,
All deities gather—husbands and wives.
The *Gǔi Mǔ* (癸母) rides the Red Dragon,
Returning to the Cavern’s palace.
Seeking the Golden Old Man,
One must ask through [the proper] means.
The union of yin and yang spans three thousand cycles.

Pointing to heaven, earth, sea, and mountain,
Their shared longevity is unshaken and firm.

---
**《Wú Lì Wǎng Zǐ》 (吴立网子) – *Master Wú’s Net of Illusions***

To become an immortal, one must embrace the *yuán qì* (元炁),
Breathing in the womb, nurturing it endlessly.
Each breath is a refining, each exhalation a distillation.
Yin and yang merge, the Red Dragon coils.
The earthly portal is sealed, the heavenly gate opens—
Rolling the cinnabar elixir into the *níhuàn* (泥丸),
The marrow’s core.
On Kunlun’s heights, the luminous pearl glows,
And the agate shimmers.
One furnace’s fire extinguishes another’s elixir.
The heart’s ashes reveal five colors, radiant and bright.
On the double-gated path, the *qi* flows unbroken.
Clasping the true flower, ascending to the elixir field.
The *Cháng Nǚ Yīng’ér* (姹女婴儿) rejoices in union,
Riding the celestial chariot, earthly fire and thunder shift.
The *Lì Quán Jiǔ* (醴泉酒) is drunk—
At every moment, after sipping, one lies intoxicated in the Peach Blossom Source.
No cares to dissolve.

---
**《Wú Sú Niàn》 (无俗念) – *Without Worldly Thoughts***

The profound Dao of Complete Perfection is boundless,
Wondrously attained by those who grasp the essence of the Perfect Ones.

The Dao of Primal Mystery is spoken through—
Silently intuiting its movements within.
All things fully manifested in essence,
Responding to circumstances, uniquely revealed—
Awakened, life’s completion is achieved.

Though this truth is clear,
The practice demands unbroken, meticulous refinement.
Bow the head to hide the celestial secret.
Without the Master’s guidance,
How could this be known?

Who governs the myriad classes of the Three Realms?
The foundation of Heaven and Earth stands alone.
Endless transformations,
Boundless containment—
Its operations leave no trace.

Piercing the void,
Radiant light pervades the boundless expanse.
The Three Reds dissolve—
For the True Person of Unity,
The Primal Oneness is split asunder.

When does the cycle of the Four Births and Six Paths cease?
Turning the body, changing the shell,
In the boundless void, myriad births and deaths unfold.
All arise from parents,
Yin and Yang paired, their vital *qi* and blood mingling.
Within the amniotic sac,
Feeling takes form, the embryo’s shape is sealed.
Who knows the stench of the birth canal?
Taking it as one’s own fine dwelling.
Burrowing in, one falls into the wheel of transmigration.
The form and bones are sold—
Piled high like mountains.

Seeking the Dao and cultivating the True,
Do not cling to perverse ways.
Speak not of the Dragon and Tiger,
Nor debate the Tortoise and Serpent.
Do not pursue the *Cháng Nǚ Yīng’ér*,
But gather the Four Symbols and Three Vehicles.
*Sword-pill* and *lead-mercury*—
Water, fire, golden sprouts, and white snow.

A hundred methods of breathing,
Yet the *shén* (神) harmonizes with *qi* (氣) in subtle play.
Within nature, let no foreign thing take root,
On the heart, ever sever all attachments.
Alone, the hidden moon shines deep and still.
Free the luminous spirit—
Unobstructed, unbound.
No barriers, no veils.

---
**[Zhengtune Mode] Black Lacquer Bow #1**
**Qiu Changchun**
My home is at the edge of the Parrot State,
A fisherman who does not know his letters.
Amidst the waves, a single leaf of a flat-bottomed boat,
Sleeping through the misty rains of the southern Jiang.
Awakening, my eyes are filled with verses—
Green mountains at dusk, shaking off the green raincoat to depart.
In thought, I recall how I once blamed the Craft of Heaven,
Yet even so, it has arranged my place.

The Celestial Moon #2 sinks in the day’s light,
The sun sets in the west—
Ascending the lofty terrace,
Gazing far, the vast emptiness of heaven and earth unfolds.
Sparse stars flicker faintly,
**[Empty Mode]** A single breath of brightness—
The luminous moon, resplendent and without grasp.
Radiant beyond the Three Realms,
Like a hundred-fold refined bronze mirror, washed clean.
Its grace pervades everywhere,
Illuminating every household,
Casting a dim glow upon halls and doors.

The wind of eternal life sweeps ten thousand leagues,
Aiding the Dao in its boundless sway,
Scattering clouds and mists without effort.
The Hall of Celestial Treasures,
Now bathed in crimson radiance and golden splendor,
Their hues intermingling in splendor.
Oh, the grandeur of the fading night!
It steadies the eternal—
A majestic, unyielding embrace.

If one has resolve to climb the green cassia,
At the Moon Palace’s edge, near the rabbit’s abode,
They watch the elixir being refined.

**Spring Descends from Heaven**
**Feng Zunshi**
The Dao is profound and mysterious.

The Dao appears like the moon full in the cold void,
Its depths like water humbling into the abyss.
Resplendent and clear, it discerns all without bias—
Truly, this principle is beyond speech.

Ask the lofty sage, who points from afar:
"See the falling petals and drifting silk of spring!"
Grass stretches to the sky.
Ah, the yellow blossoms and verdant bamboos—
What difference from true Zen?

Clouds and mountains in ten thousand layers,
Broken and continuous,
Yet deeper still the quiet valleys and ravines,
Cold as stones in deep pools.
Mist enfolds the pine pavilions,
A breeze stirs the orchid halls.
At times, it rests upon a pure table,
Forgetting all explanation.

Before the empty hall’s untrammelled grace,
The heart grows still—
Naturally serene, beyond all taste.
To whom shall it be passed?

There are jars and lamps, their flickering flames,
Kettles and cauldrons, their smoke sunk low.

**The Second Verse**
The sun and moon race heavenward.
This profound and wondrous mechanism—
How rare for dusty mortals to hear!
In the **Taiyi’s** cauldron,
By the mouth of the pure river,
Lingzhi mushrooms bloom, their orchid fragrance rising.
Behold the golden lotus’ splendid scene,
Spouting auspicious clouds,
Unveiling the gate of life.
The Dao alone is revered.
It further nurtures the myriad transformations,
Covering and sustaining the heavens and earth.
How then does one enjoy the four seasons?
Through endless, silent continuity—
Firm roots, unshaken foundation.
Opposing and yielding to yin and yang,
Exhausting and penetrating past and present,
Responding to change like a god.

This is the ultimate Daoist truth,
Transcending names and forms,
Sudden enlightenment of the true essence.
The rare and refined.

Toward **Huaxu’s** gathering,
Together savoring eternal spring.

**The Third Verse**
**Recognizing the rise and fall,**
All things forgotten, dwelling in rustic ease.
Worldly fame and fortune,
Sky-shaking wealth and rank—
None escape the objects’ relentless pull.
Ah, within the **Southern Grove’s** dream,
How many wise and foolish souls were lost!
This humble abode—
Who would count the share of each?
Who would dare return?

Only I, carefree and unbound,
Let nature guide me—
Free as the wind, without constraint.
Straw hats and raincoats stacked idle,
Lutes and books hung high,
Worldly tasks grown cold and distant.
Upon the stone between the pines,
I chant of wind and moon—
Of **clouds and waters**, emotions unconfined.
In the company of **Pure Void**,
Resting on misty peaks,
True joy knows no end.

**Understanding Red**,
I lean upon a staff and walk slowly.

**Crossing the little bridge,**
I wander freely to the Southern Marsh.
The bloom of youth has faded unseen—
Suddenly, the willows turn emerald once more.

The eastern suburbs after the rain’s retreat,
Where does the golden oriole’s languid song drift?
Gazing upon clouds and mountains, veiled and revealed,
Beyond the misty stream, the setting sun grows pale.
As evening’s cool breath lingers,
The bamboo wind carries its fragrant passage.

This idle span of time—
To whom shall I confide its fleeting weight?
A hundred years in this dusty world—
How few can they truly count?
Like bubbles on the water’s surface,
Fading in and out—
The lost may never wake to their true nature.

Returning now, I fear the fields may grow wild,
The garden overrun with neglect.
By the eastern fence,
I laugh at the world’s petty schemes, my heart unbound—
No care for lutes or books.

Within the **green pine’s** shade,
Beneath the thatched eaves,
I tend my frail, remaining frame.
Let the world’s **objects and transformations** churn and rage,
Driving the tides of past and future.
Better I, who drift through life—
Lazy, poor, and plain—
When spirits rise, I sing;
When weary, I sleep;
When wild, I dance.
All worldly affairs, their tangled fuss,
I leave to drift beyond my ken.
Let others call me fool, let them think me crude.
With **clear wind and bright moon** as my companions,
I hide in secluded **hut and marsh**—
A **Second Lord’s** slow gait,
**Dan Yang’s** ease,
And the **Xian**’s aloof grace.

「Then take action—first, dispel lust and desire.
Seek the noble man of jade-like purity and ice-like clarity.
Do not linger, mired in mud and splashed by water.
Once lost, the human body is hard to reclaim.
Do not trifle with your fate—guard your future path with care.

Now I briefly recount:
Five essentials for enduring life and long vision—rely upon these.
First, purify all thoughts and worries.
Second, renounce greed and abstain from wine, meat, and fish.
Third, aid the poor and relieve suffering.
Fourth, always practice benevolence and charity.
Fifth, preserve your vital essence and spirit.

Follow these five principles,
Perform deeds with perfect virtue,
And you shall attain the Daoist path to Penglai.
*Golden Immortals bear alms of dew*—
**Zhenren of Shan Mountain**,
Enjoying the rustic village’s winds and moons, trusting the years to pass in exchange.

All day, sheltering behind the thatched gate,
In quiet chambers, idly browsing ancient texts with languid ease.
Sitting with composure, walking alone—
Sever all ties to fame and name.

Embrace the primordial yang,
Forget the world, dissolve in stillness,
Qi and spirit harmonized—
Ascend and descend without hindrance,
Refine the elixir to its purest treasure,
Cultivate serenity, gentle rebirth.
Silent and unassuming, returning to the source,
Nurture the true essence, restore the uncarved.

Still and clear, tame the restless mind—
No more disturbance from thoughts like wild monkeys.
Free and unrestrained, indulge in boundless joy.
At ease and unshackled,
When deeds are fulfilled and virtue complete,
Attain the state of no-birth—
Let the world’s affairs rush by,
Unconcerned with their rise and fall.
The world’s passions grow distant.

Seekers of the Dao must not delay.
Sweet dew falls on lofty pines,
Time flees swift—
Alas, mortals day by day,
Cling to life without end.

If wealth surpasses Shi Chong’s stone,
Gold and jade piled high,
What gain is there but boundless karma?
Daily deceit and falsehood weigh upon the heart.
Even the Lord of Hell calls—
Your past sins await,
Who will answer for you?

Better to cultivate early,
Join the Daoist immortals beyond the world,
Cast off the mundane.

Silent and profound,
Another realm unfolds—
The boundless expanse of the *Cauldron*’s world.
Manifesting all beings,
Moonlight shines bright—
Behold the Dharma-realm, spirit and light as one.
Return, and the Clear Wind escorts you to the Celestial Emperor.

*Raindrops fall*—
**Song Pi Yun**, high mountains and flowing waters.
Ah, how few are the true kindred in this world—
South of the Zhongnan Range, mist and clouds stretch ten thousand li.
Return, for the years grow old.
Staff, elixir, and scrolls—
Beyond these, what baggage do you carry?
Delight in simplicity, uphold the family Dao of purity,
A single luminous spirit-mirror, clear as washed.

Within its marvels, the teacher points the way—
Strive to banish the specter of impermanence.
Sheathe the three-foot spirit-sword,
Thunderous strikes—
The Fire Dragon takes flight.

When the world knows peace,
Between the white clouds,
Laugh and roam at will.
The worldly seekers of fame and gain,
Do not understand enduring life—
Chasing through the dusty red world.

**Second Poem**
*Seven-petal golden lotus*—
The Gan River’s depths, casually pierced.
Qiu, Liu, Tan, Ma, Sun, and Wang,
Hao Taigu and Xu Lai—
Two true companions wrapped in coarse mats,
Leak not a drop of time,
The teacher’s cause and effect revealed.

Blooming lotus petals,
Ten thousand flowers in unison,
Fragrant mist fills the world—
*Celestial blessings seal it.*
The Jiazi year passes not in vain,
Now the Daoist immortals and heavenly beings rejoice in your awakening.

The *Quanzhen*’s household is profound,
Indeed, within it—
One must forget self and others.
Branches split nineteenfold,
Dwelling on the Dan Platform,
Surname, title, and name all spread.
Deeds and practice lack not a thread,
Yet the upper realms admit me not.

*Playing on the Jade Terrace*—
**Feng Zunshi**,
Directly pointing to the *Xuan Yuan* Path.
Alas, the *苦海*’s delusion blinds mortals.
Before you, smooth and steady,
No peril or obstacle to hinder.

Cast aside all worldly ties—
Awakening arises on its own.
Like cranes breaking free from clouds,
Toward the boundless Daoist skies, stride with faith.
Celebrate the immortal companions.
When thirsty, drink ambrosial peaches,
Fermented in sweet wine.
Entering and exiting star pavilions and moon halls,
Laugh at the world’s birth and death, past and future.

Riding the auspicious phoenix and blessed crane,
Ascend to the *Tai Pei*’s void—
Return to repose in the depths of *Bi Xia*.
This untrammled life is hard to share—
Entrust it to the Penglai companions.

**Third Poem: Ode to Tea**
*One breath exchanged*—
A thunderous shake, one sound—
The yellow sprout emerges.
The *Jade Maiden* picks it,
Seals it in the cauldron,
Refines it without flaw.

The iron wheel turns ten thousand times,
The tea leaves tremble—
A thousand infusions reveal no end.
Like the *Dharma’s* use,
The craft perfected—
Savor it in every moment.

Worthy of praise—
The Daoist child’s skill,
Floating tea leaves like spring snow, beyond compare.
Banish the sleep demon,
Sever the path of the Way,
Expose the superficial.

*Zhaozhou* knows its taste,
*Lu Quan* reaches this truth—
All lead to the immortal realm.
This tea cup—
May all awaken early,
Together bound for mist and clouds.

**Fourth Poem: Yellow Root Dream**
*Yellow Root*—
The dream dissolves.

**First Poem:**

Banish the fleeting vanities before your eyes—
Reflect fiercely, break free from the mundane cage.
Beyond the world, what chains remain?
Follow the *Zhen*’s shadow, befriend the *Xia*’s glow,
Roam where winds are neighbors, moons your companions.
The carefree wanderer—
Bound by no rule.
Skimming green waters, savoring blue mountains,
Dissolving into ease.

Such joy—
No gold could trade.
Let others scramble for fame, wealth, and power.
But I seek only a leftward turn—
Living on simple fare,
Claiming all of life’s languid ease.

Morning to evening, a pillow of deep slumber,
Stretching limbs in boundless ease.
Within the red dust—
Observe well:
Who matches my leisure?
Worthy of envy.

In this idle state, there lies another art—
The *Cloud-Holding* technique.

---

**Second Poem: [Qiu Changchun] #3**
A life of indolence—
Only earning a pillow of carefree repose.
Wild-haired, filthy-faced,
Unmoved by the body’s decay.
Let the *San Guang* rush by—
Sun, moon, and stars—
While the *Four Great Elements* bear the weight of forests and streams.

By the deep ravine, beside the secluded cliff,
Mountains hide, clouds seal the path.
Disaster?
Thunder crashes, lightning strikes—
Yet none dare near me.

At noon, I rise and wander, then sit again.
Shatter every old habit.
In leisure’s embrace, only this remains:
Tired of greed, content in poverty,
Desire severed, drowsy in the smoke of life.
No stored grain, no elixir sold.
Singing with ease, laughing without restraint—
Worthy indeed.

---

**Qiu Changchun #4**
A lone wanderer, stumbling along,
Crosses the Qin Basin—westward into the land of Panshu’s winding streams.
By empty valleys, cliffs, and secluded ravines,
A lofty cave in the clouds shelters his trace.

Smoke and flame are nonexistent,
No provisions stored—what need has he ever amassed?
Hunger met, thirst quenched,
He seeks sustenance in village lanes and byways at each passing hour.
Whatever scraps of cold or hot remain,
Filling his belly, stuffing his gut,
No need for true *cultivation*’s force.

Liking and disliking come and go—just enough to keep him alive,
Avoiding the labor of kitchen and hearth.
His *skin-bag*#5 is mere guise,
As incense fills his *passages*#6—
Seeking only to augment his *vital essence* and *qi*.

His physical form is light and nimble,
His *Dharma-body*#7 rests with ease.

---

**Qiu Changchun #5**
In the thatched hut, we sit together,
Let the *Pure-Void*#8 and cold detachment
Stir the heart’s incense—warm as ever.
He knows the *Primordial True Face*—
All *dharma* dissolves into the same.

Walking like idle clouds,
Sitting as empty valleys,
Motion and stillness both rest.

The *Mystic Profound*’s subtlety—
Indeed, it cannot be split open with words.
Gazing upward, the heights are boundless,
Peering ahead, it vanishes in an instant—
A single point, never lacking.

Whether speech or silence,
All—*immortals*, *sages*, *Buddhas*—
Share its perfect harmony.
*Chan* and *Dao* alike:
Void, still, and utterly extinguished.

Filling every measure, yet forgotten,
Swelling the earth, yet unnoticed—
Wrapped in *Round Perfection*#9, clear and complete.
The *Mystic Sky* reveals itself alone—
A wheel of formless *heart-moon*#10.

---

**Qiu Changchun #6**
Delving into the *Mystic Profound* with toil,
Forcing through the *Dao-law*’s iron firmament.
Cawing crows, howling monkeys—
All speak of the *Non-Dual*#11.
Yet beware of clinging to their divisions.

A single shout—*heart* is illuminated,
A staff’s strike—*nature* is seen.
This truth is fixed, yet hard to say.

The knots of doubt are shattered,
The original face is light—its secrets spill.
Flowers bloom on rootless trees,
Pulsing through ages, ancient and new,
Falling away, returning to the *kalpa*#12.

Wiping the *brush* with tortoise-shell,
Rinsing the *mouth* with spring’s flow—
Long-tongued as the *stone-washing*#13.
Five schools of *dharma*, six lineages of *patriarchal intent*#14,
Yet all erect a waist-high snowdrift—
A hollow display.

Let me liken it to this:
A jade pool, cold, steeped in autumn’s moon.
---

**Manting Huang** #15
*Sinking into the Void*, yet clinging to stillness,
The fool wastes his labor in vain.
Grinding bricks to make a mirror,
Seeking fish by climbing trees.
Why point at the moon when it’s seen?
To gaze upon flowers—
All is *Suchness*#16.

The wise discern things as they arise,
Neither vexed nor pleased.
As *immortal* or *Buddha*—
No gain, no loss,
Neither real nor unreal.

Radiant, open—
A single *divine pearl*#17.
Mingling with the vulgar, yet never stained,
Amid the crowd—
*Dharma* and dust cannot bind him.

The *Everlasting Use*#18 knows no limits—
Stable, vast, and boundless.
What is not *Void* and *Nothingness*?

---

**Zui Jiangyu** #19
*Huangfu the True Person*#20
Pierces the *Chaos*#21—
Behold! The *Qingbi*#22
Southward, the Yangtze’s jade-like grip.

From ancient to modern, poets have sought its scenes—
Who understands its *original source*?

The years pass, one *Geng* month follows another *Jia*—
Why does it show no difference?
Now I reveal the *key*—
To know the origins of heaven and earth.

The *Dao* has a name that may be spoken—
The *Five Phases*#23 shift, overturning,
Arranging the *Heavenly Horse*#24 and *Earthly Tiger*#25’s strategies.

*Kan* water flows backward to the *Bing* door#26,
Following the moon’s waxing and waning, ebbing and swelling.
At *Mid-Autumn*, when *qi* arrives,
Metal can birth water—
Snow surges in layers a thousandfold.
The *immortals’* wondrous workings
Are no different from the tides.

---

**Shui Diao Ge Tou** #27
*Xu Jing, the Heavenly Master*#28
Holds the *secret keys* of the *Highest Truth*#29,
Guides the learned to rescue the lost.
A pure heart, a spotless path—
All *heavenly beings*, *saints*, and *common folk* seek refuge here.
Not in *soaring through the Pole Star* or *treading the Dipper*#30,
Not in *broad hearing* or *much learning*—
A chaotic mind only breeds doubt.

Only banish deceit and falsehood,
Let the heart align with the *divine*#31.
Awaken to the *True Void*#32,
Break free from the world’s snare,
Sever the *passages*#33.

Nurture vast *qi*#34,
Commanding thunder, subduing lightning—
Rescuing the world from peril.
Merge with all *spirits*, returning to the One,
A single thought pierces heaven and earth—
Only then does *non-doing*#35 begin.

With a shout, winds and rains arise,
Upholding the world, aiding the *rightful age*#36.

---
**#2**
No need to hunt for *divine waters*#37,
Nor ask of the *Pool of Flowers*#38.
Yellow sprouts, white snow—
All are but false names.
Just these *Heavenly Ox* and *Earthly Horse*#39,
Are the *High Dragon* and *Kan Tiger*#40—
No need for further guesswork.

Medicines weigh no *jin* or *liang*#41,
*Fire-alchemy*#42 need not be timed.

**偃月炉，朱砂鼎，总皆非。**
The crescent furnace, the cinnabar cauldron—all in vain.

**真铅真汞，遇之不炼要何为。**
True lead and true mercury—if they meet unrefined, what purpose is there?

**自己金翁姹女，渐渐打成一块，胎息象婴儿。**
The Golden Uncle and Crimson Maiden, fused together—
Breathing as one, like an infant in the womb.

**不信张平叔，你更问他谁。**
Do not trust Zhang Ping-shu—who else would you ask?

---

**其三#9**
*(Attributed to Bai Yu-xian)*

**东风卷帘模，时物又新奇。**
The east wind lifts the curtain—spring’s wonders anew.

**桃花院落，小桥流水柳依依。**
Peach blossoms in the courtyard, willows clinging to the bridge,
Where streams flow softly beneath.

**正是清明天气，芳草池塘鲜丽，何处不相宜。**
At Qingming’s gentle season, fragrant grasses brighten the ponds—
Wherever one lingers, all is fitting.

**紫燕添新垒，小雨洒芳菲。**
Swallows build their nests in purple hues,
While fine rain scatters blossoms’ splendor.

**老生涯，沽酒杖，钓鱼矶。**
In my old age, I drink wine with a staff,
Or fish from the rocks where the river bends.

**江湖一样，几声鸥鹭夕阳微。**
Lakes and rivers alike—
A few cries of herons as the sun sinks low.

**百岁光阴石火，万迭云山烟锁，回首顿忘机。**
A hundred years pass like flint and fire,
Endless peaks shrouded in mist—
Turning back, all worldly schemes dissolve.

**蝶梦松窗下，高卧碧云蹊。**
Butterfly dreams beneath the pine window,
Slumbering deep in the path of azure clouds.

---

**孤鹰**
*(Ma Dan-yang)*

**苦海为人，随波逐浪，茫茫甚日休期。**
As a man in the bitter sea, tossed by waves,
When will this endless drifting cease?

**为酒色财气，一向粘惹，瞒心昧己。**
For wine and lust, wealth and arrogance—
Clinging like stains, deceiving the heart and self.

**不算前程，幻躯有限，待作千年之计。**
No reckoning of fate—this mortal form is fleeting,
Yet men scheme for millennia ahead.

**忽一朝阴公来请，看你教谁替。**
Suddenly, the Dark Lord summons—
Who then will you send in your place?

**千间峻宇，金玉满堂，毕竟成何济。**
A thousand rooms of towering halls,
Gold and jade piled high—
What good does it all bring in the end?

**劝诸公省，早把凡笼猛跳出。**
I urge you, gentlemen, to wake—
Break free from the cage of mundane desires!

**向物外飘蓬，放落魄婪耽，鹑居鷇食，昏昏炼己。**
Beyond the world’s clamor, like a drifting leaf,
Cast off greed and folly—
Live like the quail in its nest, eating plain fare,
Refining the self in quietude.

**默默地、怡神养气，丹成既济。**
Silently, nurturing spirit and *qi*,
The elixir perfected—all is fulfilled.

**乘彩云，跨凤归。**
Riding the rainbow clouds, mounting the phoenix—
Returning home.

---

**集贤宾**
*(Wang Chong-chang)*

**仔细曾穷究，想六地众生，强揽闲愁。**
Carefully examining, I see the six realms’ beings—
How they force upon themselves idle sorrows.

**恰才得食饱，又思量、骏马轻裘。**
Scarcely sated, they already scheme for
Fine horses and light furs.

**有骏马，有轻裘，又思量、建节封侯。**
With swift steeds and warm cloaks,
They dream of banners and noble titles.

**假若金银过北斗，置下万顷良田，盖起百尺高楼。**
If gold and silver fill the Dipper’s measure,
If they own vast fields and towering halls—
What then?

**儿孙自有儿孙福，莫与儿孙作马牛。**
Their children will have their own fortunes—
Do not become their ox or horse.

**贪利禄，竞虚名，惹机勾。**
Greed for gain and hollow fame
Stirs the snares of fate.

**岂知身似，水上浮沤。**
Do they not see their bodies as
Floating reeds on the water?

**贪恋气财并酒色，不肯上、钓鱼舟。**
Clinging to *qi*, wealth, wine, and lust,
They refuse to board the fishing boat—
The path to true liberation.

**荒尽丹田三顷，荆棘多稠。**
The *elixir field* lies waste, overgrown with thorns.

**宝藏库、偷盗了明珠，铁灯盏、渗漏了清油。**
The treasure vault is plundered of its pearls,
The iron lamp leaks its pure oil.

**水银迸散难再收，大丹砂甚日成就。**
Mercury scatters, never to be gathered—
When will the Great Elixir be complete?

**杀曾叮咛劝，劝着后，几曾偢。**
Though warnings are whispered again and again,
How few heed them!

**苦海深，波浪流。**
The bitter sea runs deep, its waves endless.

**心闲无事却垂钩。**
With a tranquil heart, the fishing line is cast—
No need for haste.

**呜呼锦鳞终不省，摇头摆尾，恣纵来，来往戏波流。**
Alas, the scaled treasures never awaken—
Shaking their heads, they frolic in the waves,
Unwilling to be caught.

**愚迷子，省贪求。**
Foolish and lost, they cling to desire—
All for a needle’s worth of fame and gain,
While youth fades unnoticed.

---

**齐天乐**
*(Qiu Chang-chun)*

**自离东海上，元本三州，四人同契。**
Since leaving the Eastern Sea,
The Four Worthies of Shu—
Bound by the same Dao.

**异域殊乡，同行并坐，终日相将游戏。**
Though lands and homes were distant,
We walked and sat together,
Playing and conversing all day.

**谈玄论妙，究方外之清闲，道家真味。**
Discussing the Mysterious and the Marvelous,
Probing the leisure of the *outer world*,
Tasting the true essence of the Dao.

**唱和从容，一师#10法眷情何异。**
In harmonious exchange, effortless as water,
The Master’s teachings—
What difference is there in affection?

**于今分显迥然，苦志勤心，磨炼各逃倾逝。**
Now separated by vast distances,
With steadfast resolve and diligent hearts,
Each refines himself, fleeing the world’s decline.

**既是飘零，难为会合，幽僻关山迢递。**
Though scattered like fallen leaves,
Gatherings are rare—
Remote peaks and passes stretch endlessly.

**乾坤间隔，望落落犹如，晓星之势。**
Heaven and Earth divide us,
Like scattered stars at dawn—
Distant, yet visible.

**再遇何年，驾云朝上帝。**
When next we meet, in what year?
Riding the clouds to pay homage to the Celestial.

---

**其二**
**自清都别后，来人间梦中游戏。**
Since parting from Qingdu,
I wander in the world as in a dream.

**性本玄虚，君临社稷，洪福齐天康济。**
By nature, I am boundless and void,
Yet rule the realm with boundless virtue—
My blessings match Heaven’s, bringing peace.

**冬温夏清，任春水秋山，放怀如意。**
In winter, warmth; in summer, cool—
Spring waters and autumn mountains at my will,
My heart unbound.

**外物多情，幻身无奈生憔悴。**
Though the world is full of allure,
This mortal form grows weary in vain.

**深穷仙方道术，固炼形神，内观返调元气。**
I delve deeply into immortal arts,
Cultivating body and spirit,
Turning *qi* inward, restoring its roots.

**四大冲和，三彭遁匿，熟境繁华何忌。**
The Four Elements harmonize,
The Three *Peng*s retreat—
What need to fear the world’s luxuries?

**真空妙有，况千古灵明，自然凋弊。**
True Void, wondrous existence—
How much more so the ancient *Ling-ming*,
Which fades of its own accord.

**梦觉心开，廓然超万岁。**
Awakening from the dream, the heart expands—
Transcending ten thousand years.

---

**永遇乐**
**试问诸公，本来模样，如何形状。**
Gentlemen, let me ask—
What is your original form?
How does it appear?

**纵使丹青，难描这个，旷劫端严相。**
Even the finest brushes cannot capture it—
Its grandeur spans eons.

**无形无影，观之不见，听之又无响。**
Formless, shadowless—
You cannot see it, nor hear its sound.

**露堂堂、不摇不动，目前甚是明朗。**
Yet it stands revealed, unmoving, unshaken—
Bright as day before you.

**人还省悟，回光返照，莫向外边劳攘。**
If only men would awaken,
Turning inward like the sun’s last light—
Do not toil beyond!

**放下诸缘，屏除万事，物物离心上。**
Cast aside all attachments,
Set aside all worldly affairs—
Let all things drift free from the mind.

**迷云消散，性天独露，心月永无遮障。**
The clouds of delusion disperse,
Revealing the true nature—
The heart’s moon, unobstructed forever.

**与三界、一切诸仙，并无两样。**
It shares no difference with the Three Realms,
Or all the immortals.

---

**其二**
**行也无忧，坐也无闷，长安长乐。**
Walking brings no worry, sitting no restlessness—
Eternal peace in Chang’an.

**息息绵绵，朝朝暮暮，保养神珠一颗。**
Breath by breath, day by day,
Nurturing the precious *shen-zhu* within.

**闲是闲非，莫偢莫采，大忌竞争人我。**
Leisure is not leisure—
Do not strive, do not grasp—
The greatest taboo is competing with others.

**灭无明、心似寒灰，便是道人功果。**
Extinguish ignorance—
The heart like cold ashes—
This is the Daoist’s reward.

**猿儿不走，马儿捉住，龙虎定中交媾。**
The monkey does not flee,
The horse is caught—
The union of Dragon and Tiger is sealed.

**阳降阴升，日来月往，炉炼长生药。**
Yang descends, Yin ascends,
Sun and moon pass—
The furnace refines the elixir of longevity.

**抽添鼎内，不须炊爨，自有九阳真火。**
Stirring within the cauldron,
No need for stoking—
The Nine Suns’ true fire burns on its own.

**霜心子、明把天机，与君说破。**
Frosted Heart—
I reveal the Heavenly Mystery to you.

---

**宣静三台**
*(Niu Zhen-ren)*

**自小飘蓬，身心落魄，云游多在山东。**
From youth, a drifting leaf,
Body and heart adrift—
Mostly wandering in Shandong’s mountains.

**世间事，看破浑是假想，荣华犹似梦中。**
The world’s affairs—
All illusions, seen through—
Glory and splendor like a fleeting dream.

**盖个庵儿，隈山靠水，栽松种竹成林。**
I built a humble hut,
Nestled by mountains and water,
Planting pines and bamboo until the grove was thick.

**炕暖窗明，乐清闲、胜竞利名。**
The kang is warm, the windows bright—
Joy in quietude surpasses striving for fame.

**月朗山东，凉风细细，南溪绿水邻邻。**
Under the bright moon in Shandong,
Cool breezes whisper,
Beside the green waters of Nanxi.

**Gradual Refinement**

As the elixir is refined,
The heart’s core grows cold as ash—
Yet one *yang* stirs,
The jade cauldron warms itself.

Ethereal *qi* swirls thick,
Celestial blossoms bloom in splendor,
Fragrance fills the Yellow Court.

Jade Maidens and Golden Boys
Gather them—
Forging the Purple Gold.

Circulating the Three Passes,
Driving back the Four Symbols,
Harmonizing the One Essence of Clarity.

*Qi* condenses, spirit congeals—
Listen to the *sheng* and *xiao*,
A symphony of pure sound.

Fated bonds from past lives,
Encountering the True Teaching now—
The profound, perfect Dao.

Merit fulfilled, the work complete,
Riding *luan* and *he* to the Supreme Clarity.

---
**Ode to Wuyi (No. 11)**
*Bai Yuzhen*

In days of old, at Qin’s time,
On a Mid-Autumn night in Wuyi’s Nine Bends—
Silent mist,
Slanted sun, mere spans in height,
Crows perched on withered branches.

Thirty-six peaks stand in morning verdure,
One stream’s flow births autumn’s green.
Just as the groves fill with cassia’s scent,
Golden millet scatters from the sky.

Divine guests arrive—
The Golden Elixir ripens.
A jade edict descends,
Clouds form beneath my feet.
New bones knit in stone,
Yet still cling to red flesh.

Midnight’s moon shines bright as day,
The Jade Emperor’s palanquin arrives, feasts spread.
Laughing, I recall the pavilion’s past—
Now only pines and bamboo remain.

---
**Ode to the White Lotus**

Last night, Chang’e wandered,
Drunk from the Celestial Palace’s halls.
Why did she drop her jade hairpin?
The Water Spirit stays silent.

She took it to the Crystal Palace—
At dawn, it was returned, chattering.
The wind blew it into fragrant skies—
Who could distinguish?

Soft yet moist,
Cool and pure.
White as jade,
Cold as snow.
Even the Jade Emperor’s gardens
Lack such a bloom.

Only poetry can praise it—
Let none dare pluck or break it.
Laughing at Li’s coarse lotus,
Thin as a willow—
This one surpasses all.

---
**Ten Thousand Springs**
*Qiu Changchun*

Sleeves, autumn’s cloak—
Wearing them now feels just right.
Frost-clear skies.
Unfettered joy in wandering,
No fear of the west wind’s might.

Hundreds of petals, thousands of threads,
Strung together with precision.
Loose yet bound.
Wildness without, inner pearls gleaming.

---
**Playful Leisure**

The moon at heaven’s edge,
At first like a bow.
Now vanished in the *geng* earth.
Dragons seek tigers,
Tigers seek dragons—
They meet.
A golden flower blooms in the wind.

The moon at heaven’s edge,
Now like an overturned furnace.
Lead and mercury dwell in the alchemical tripod.
Fire must refine,
Melting the flowing pearl.
One gourd—
Three hundred eighty-four *zhu*.

---
**Pearl Curtain**
*Bai Yuzhen*

*Yin* and *yang* internally unite,
Lead and mercury arrayed in the Eight Trigrams.
The Golden Cauldron refines the Yellow Sprout,
At the hour when *yang* first ascends.
After the Hour of Child, before noon—
Fire enters the jade furnace,
Boiling into white snow.

Piercing clarity.
This Mysterious Pass is profound—
Not lightly revealed.

**Following the Master’s Subtle Instructions**

Seizing the essence of Tiger and Dragon,
The sun and moon arise naturally.
Heaven’s creative art—how could mortals fathom?
Exchanging mortal bones,
Forever free from demonic snares.

Transcending.

Gazing toward the Celestial Capital’s gate,
Bowing at the Golden Palace of the Primordial.
Drunk on fragrant wine from youthful lone clouds,
Beyond all worldly ties.
Wearing one patch,
Stitching another—
The joy of unbounded ease.

A broken gourd at the waist,
No other baggage.
Others mock me for my lack of care.
Let them point and scold.
In ancient temples and shrines,
I play with mud gods instead.

A cracked sand basin,
A shattered clay pot,
A spoon bent beyond use.
A torn paper quilt,
A mended sack,
Curled up to sleep.

Only waiting—
When my merit is complete, I’ll ascend to the Jade Emperor.
Then shall I prove myself a true man of resolve.

**Gazing at Penglai**
*Qiu Changchun*

Hear my counsel, for small matters you must know:
All striving brings harm in the end—
Profit gained is profit lost.
Cleverness is not as good as simplicity.

True cultivation lies beyond the mind’s grasp.
See only what is before you,
And troubles will not follow.
Step by step, enter the realm of Non-Action.

**Four Pieces of Jade**

Life’s swift as a shuttle, so turn back soon to seek your livelihood.
Do not let gain ensnare you, nor fame drag you—
Let not wine and lust cloud your senses.

Right and wrong, others and I—
Why stir the idle *qi*?

When lead is spent and mercury exhausted,
Then will you rue your hidden treasures—
In vain you’ll weep and wail.

From this day forth, take action now,
Better early than delayed.

Be simple, be foolish—
Profit will come to you naturally.

Even if you feed a thousand mouths at home,
What good does it bring?
In vain you labor body and mind,
Day and night without rest,
Wasting your youthful bloom,
Leaving you gaunt and weary.

Why endure this suffering?
Why not look back and reflect:
Count your own blessings—
Who can replace the impermanence?

**Cranes’ Lingering Echoes**
*Volume II: Daoist Wanderings of Mount Xiangyou, by Monk Peng Zhizhong*

---
#1 This piece, attributed by study to the Yuan-era *zaju* author Bai Pin, was originally mislabeled as by Qiu Changchun.
#2 Also found in *The Canxi Collection*. Below follows its corrected version.
#3 The original lacked a title. This piece, also in *The Canxi Collection*, should be by Qiu Changchun.
#4 The original lacked a title. This piece appears again in *The Canxi Collection*.
#5 True cultivation: *The Canxi Collection* reads 『珍羞』, which also makes sense.
#6 Seminal essence: *The Canxi Collection* reads 『律液』.
#7 Cold control: *The Canxi Collection* reads 『寒控』.
#8 This piece also appears in Lin Ziran’s *The Vital Essence Guide*.
#9 The original lacked a title. By study, this piece should be by Southern Song’s Ge Changeng.
#10 One poem: *The Canxi Collection* reads 『一诗』.
   Below, 『What difference』, *The Canxi Collection* reads 『何义』.
#12 The original tune name is 『满江红』. The next piece follows the same.
   Both were composed by Bai Yuxian.
#14 Joyful wanderings: The original misread as 『畅怀忧』.
   Corrected according to *The Canxi Collection*.
#15 Upper hand: *The Canxi Collection* reads 『上下』.
**Cranes’ Lingering Echoes, Volume II**

**Cranes’ Lingering Echoes, Volume II**
*By Daoist Peng Zhizhong of Mount Xianyou*

**#1**
*By Master Feng Zun*
After the meal, leisurely pacing,
A staff in hand—what support for wild gazing?
Sails return to distant harbors,
Herons stand on riverbanks,
A thousand trees in blossom, softly unfurled.
Fragrant grasses by the pond,
Jade River towers—
Misty clouds conceal the green barriers.
Gazing eastward to the horizon’s end,
No old friends—only melancholy.
Returning homeward, the emerald ridges steep,
Forests and peaks in shadowed embrace,
To while away the evening’s restless mood.
Clever birds in whispered song,
Willows droop like golden threads,
Green shadows echo on the bridge’s span.
Sweeping away serpentine cares,
Savoring the breeze and light—
Like Tao Qian and Xie Lingyun in verse and brush.
What fine scenes these mountains hold,
Beyond the world’s dust—
How few can truly seek them.

**#2**
The sun’s last glow returns,
An end to mortal toil—
Where now shall I rest my weight?
Withered fields of Zheng,
Bamboo groves and pine streams,
Where hidden joys and pleasures dwell.
Cloud-friends and mist-companions,
Water’s hue, mountains’ grace—
Secluded in smoke-wreathed crags and valleys.
Yet here, my spirit soars beyond the sky,
A single breath of boundless vastness.
Worthy of love:
Butterflies dance on blossoming branches,
Moss creeps on stone paths,
Soft winds lift the curtains—daylight high.
With serene breadth of mind,
Chewing the cosmos’ essence,
Lofty above the world’s clamor and feasts.
Loose robes, wide sleeves,
Pale jade dangling—
Laughing, I recline by the eastern hedge, sipping wine.
I would write my true feelings,
Yet dusty paths and absent friends
Leave only desolation.

**#3**
Piercing the world’s delusion,
Free of mortal snares—
Drifting, unbound, no chains to hold.
Floating like water-plants,
Refined in solitude, proud as wild deer,
Like clouds and deer in untamed lands.
Riding waves when struck by fate,
Blending with the world’s light—
What honor or shame in knowing when to stop?
Let the tides of life surge on,
Heedless of youth’s fleeting rush.
From now on, ink and brush gather dust,
Worldly thoughts dissolve—
Content in emerald clouds’ high halls.
All things released,
All cares abandoned—
Quiet before my study’s plum and bamboo.
Pure laziness, ancient virtue’s wind,
Is the true, eternal bliss.
Let the crowd’s frenzy—
Day and night, racing through the world’s paths,
Clashing like wild beasts—
Pass me by.

**#4**
Dreaming of the Hall of Huai,
Leaning against heaven’s heights, a long cry—
Piercing through the world’s illusions, past and present.
Carrying twin mirrors bright as snow,
Hunting tigers, slaying dragons—
Once, I wasted my youth in such folly.
Jin Valley’s splendor,
Han gardens, Qin palaces—
Only fallen petals and drifting silk remain.
Ah, mortal life—
Busy all day, who pauses to reflect before death?
Better than this:
Pure talk with jade dust,
Golden zithers’ refined play—
Sleeping high in the caverns’ threshold.
Roaming fields at ease,
Freeing my heart’s wild flight,
Leisurely with lapwing and heron by the marsh.
Gathering my life anew,
Purple crabs, golden oranges—
A single raincoat on the misty river.
Drunk, I return as always,
To the deep reeds’ embrace,
Moonlight on the quiet shore.

**#5**
Ask the Zen gates—
Endless seeking, often empty at the end.
Grinding bricks to make a mirror,
Piling snow for beams—
How many youths have wandered lost?
Swallowing mountains,
Nestling mustard seeds—
Laughing gold-headed adepts.
When enlightened, transcending the Ten Bhūmis,
Free from doubt in the Four Births and Six Paths.
Who hears the cuckoo’s cry at dawn
Before the cliff’s silent rocks,
Beneath the shade-less tree?
The path to Caoxi is steep,
The Eagle’s Ridge shrouded in clouds—
No trace of old friends here.
A thousand-foot ice cliff,
Five-petaled lotuses bloom,
Ancient halls’ scented curtains sway.
Avoiding the brambles’ tangle,
Old wives and wandering sons—
Dream and reality blur.

**#6**
To transcend and attain the True,
Steel your resolve—
Awaken wisdom suddenly.
Dust dispelled, thoughts still,
Love abandoned, sorrow forgotten—
Tranquil ease knows its own sweetness.
A thunderclap—
Fire ignites the Three Fields,
Midnight crows fly a thousand *li*.
Through the curtains, the furnace glows warm,
Drinking elixir’s rich, fragrant nectar.
Now skilled in hand:
Riding phoenixes, mounting cranes,
Forging gold, refining wood—
Reveling in the caverns’ marvels.
Radiant light, pure essence,
Filling sea and mountain—
True *qi* permeates heaven and earth.
Striding on wind and cloud,
Mounting sun and moon,
No child’s play, this mastery.
Gathering the Mystic Pearl,
Returning to the Great Void—
Saints and sages share this realm.

**#7**
The Dao is profound and hidden—
How can its signs be known?
Speak of it, and even ghosts and gods recoil in dread.

It embraces the cosmos,
Splits the Mysterious Origin,
True joy in the world has no equal.

Before the Spirit Vulture Peak,
A treasure pearl is plucked forth—
Five radiant hues shine clear.

Illuminating heaven and earth,
All beings above and below—
The wise live as long as mountains and seas.

At its utmost height,
Emerald mists dissolve lightly,
Jade flowers fall in disarray,
An empty void weaves into a canopy.

Golden body, jade bones,
Moonly veil, starry crown,
In harmony with crystal and celestial resonance.

Pure and serene abode,
Saints and sages’ bearing—
Through ages, their presence remains.

May those who seek
Grasp this subtle, rare truth,
Together wander beyond the square.

---

**#8**
To avoid the world and dwell in peace,
Mingle with dust yet stay aligned,
Silent depths—who can know the sage?

Dwelling like quails, eating like sparrows,
Moss paths, vine-lined caves,
Nurturing virtue in profound stillness.

Floating stillness has its place,
Emerging and retreating without measure,
Divine responsiveness defies prediction.

Delight in gourd and bowl,
Laugh in scorn of groves and springs,
Yet refuse to bow to servitude.

At this moment,
Pine chairs, bamboo halls—
Lips hum, tongue plucks,
Drinking spring wine from jade cups.

A chestful of moonlight,
Two sleeves of clean wind—
Truly, this is the hidden truth.

The life beyond the square,
Meaning in stillness,
Not to be casually plucked.

Wait for the mist to disperse,
The jade cord to rise pure—
Then know the truth itself.

---

**#9**
Ah, the masses’ delusion,
Lost in the ford’s twists,
When will their drifting cease?

Striving for supremacy,
Clinging to life in vain,
Ever bound to home and gain.

Chains of profit, reins of fame,
Waves of desire, mountains of favor,
Drunk in the wine markets, stumbling through flower-lined streets.

Like ants in endless cycles,
They forget their hair turns white.
Who would choose the Great Simplicity’s grove,
The land of Non-Action,
To idle with Laozi and Zhuangzi?

Pearls lost, elephants trapped in nets,
Dreaming shattered in Hua Xu,
High-pillowed in the celestial caverns of day and moon.

The Three Realms vanish,
The Eight Directions dissolve into emptiness—
Piercing, luminous light shines through.

This effortless freedom beyond kalpas,
Ah, true joy—
Words cannot say it.

---

**#10**
Time flees like a crack in a wheel,
Like dust motes—
Silently shifting all things.

The floating life is restless,
Awareness lost in dust,
Entangled by wine, desire, profit, fame.

Look, through the ages,
Heroes of Chu, Yue, Zhou, Qin, Tang, Han—
Only crumbling graves and ruined steles remain,
Endless strife through the ages.

Yet those who awaken early
Find in the jade cup’s blue-green depths,
White clouds piled—
Another palace of emerald mists.

The Three Heavens’ gathering,
Five-colored lights converge,
Morning attendance at the jade banquet of Purple Micro.

The Celestial Gardens, the Jade Pool,
The Vermilion Gate, the Pure Capital—
Truly, this is effortless wandering.

Laughing at the foolish,
Trapped in the苦海, selling bones without end,
Endlessly turning.

---

**#11**
Awakened at Caoqi,
Cranes soar into the celestial void,
Cloud-water monks’ livelihood.

By the river, raising the oar,
Facing the scene, casting the hook—
Red carp leap from the brocade waves.

Wind carries the fishing boat,
Piercing twin peaks,
Shadows wrapped—startled clarity after rain.

Seeing mist and clouds,
Gazing at the elixir’s gold—
One grain surpasses all treasures.

In its mystery,
The Great One contains the True,
The Mysterious Origin forms its image,
Ascending and descending without obstruction.

Nine years of resolve,
Three years of will,
Five flowers of jade nectar refined.

All from the numinous source,
Piercing the Nine Lights,
The true realm revealed beyond compare.

This eternal life, prolonged vision,
Heaven’s profound mechanism,
The true logic of immortals.

---

**#12**
Establishing the numinous altar,
First refining the elixir furnace,
Nurturing the True Vitality of Great Harmony.

Wind howls, tigers roar,
Fire rises, dragons ascend—
Harmonizing depends on the seasons.

Metal and wood converge,
The Dipper’s axis aligns with Heaven’s Gate,
Swirling to purge the heart’s path.

Witness the Mystic Pearl—
A grain of flowing wine,
Flickering back into the golden cauldron.

The cauldron’s scene—
Creation’s subtle mystery,
Essential patterns must be refined,
Crafting the spirit’s essence, the soul’s sanctity.

From nothingness to function,
From principle to truth—
Awakening to the original nature.

Returning to boundlessness,
Gradually entering Green Yang,
The仙境 fills the void with stillness.

This wheel of moonlight,
A century of obscurity—
Suddenly clear and bright.

---

**#13**
Cultivating qi to swallow the clouds,
Riding the wind to drink the dew—
Align with the Five Phases’ order.

The southern mountain’s crimson phoenix,
The northern sea’s black tortoise—
Steady resolve, focused heart, seek it.

Lead and mercury meet,
In the crucible of creation,
Forging one perfect pill.

Following Yin and Yang’s divine use,
Nurturing the boundless true breath.

At the Mystic Pass’s awakening,
Only now do the blind and deaf see—
Encountering the sage who opens the way.

Using talismans of wondrous Dao,
Silently moving subtle patterns,
Jade nectar flows, increasing.

Cloud-water leisure,
The Great Void’s emptiness—
Vastness has no trace.

This elixir’s secret,
A lifetime’s doubt—
Now dissolved like ice.

---

**#14**
Sun and moon race high,
Golden waves surge—
Seven returns, nine circulations extend life.

True essence responds to things,
The Dao hides its body,
Mysteriously penetrating the path.

Only when Yang arises,
Does creation’s elixir form—
Dragon and Tiger ascend to Purple Void’s heaven.

This jade case,
Celestial seals of fate—
Must be opened by the sage.

The Way of longevity,
Deep-rooted and firm,
The immortals’ craft—
Refining lead and mercury as their duty.

The furnace glows with five colors,
The cauldron radiates the Three Lights—
Recognize the original True Ancestor.

Before the Moonlit Pavilion,
A golden cicada appears,
Dancing on emerald peaks in bright space.

With a lofty resolve,
Sincere cultivation,
The immortal’s examination.

---

**#15**
Original qi fills the cauldron,
Ragged robes conceal the body—
What use are all worldly matters?

Yellow sprouts, white snow,
Black waters, red clouds—
The Yellow Emperor’s transmission is renowned.

Deep thanks to the clear teacher,
Who reveals the subtle mystery—
Profound truths are pure and refined.

Nurturing the仙胎 into a cloudy orb,
Enveloping all spirits completely.

Holding creation’s work,
Each is perfected,
All possess sufficiency—
One breath returns to primordial essence.

「Ranging through the Eight Boundaries,
Wandering in praise of the Three Mountains,
Never straying far—all within arm’s reach.

Lamentable are those lost in error,
How could they know the interplay of Yin and Yang?
The True Ancestor’s teachings are left to false demons.

Refining the Golden Elixir—
All are born of Heaven and Earth’s finest,
Vying in bold and boundless *qi*.

---
**Sixteen**
Withdrawing from grains, halting the kitchen,
Feasting on mist and drinking dew,
Returning to nature’s unforced harmony.

Lead sprouts five colors,
Mercury radiates the Three Lights—
Only then does the Great Elixir’s lineage reveal itself.

Opening the crimson gate,
A golden crow leaps forth,
Soaring into the Jade Rabbit’s palace.

Holding Yin and Yang—
Their union in the divine furnace,
Cooking forth the boundless True Body.

Within the void,
Purple *qi* spirals,
Mysterious pearls gleam,
Piercing the dharmakāya’s primordial wisdom.

Forsaking worldly schemes to cultivate the Dao,
Hiding from traces to seek immortality,
Ever silently preserving the mind from decay.

Clinging to glory and splendor,
Fearing the wrath of the Red One,
The elixir is carelessly cast aside.

---
**Seventeen**
Piercing the depths of hidden mysteries,
Deeply understanding the elixir’s kiln,
Relying on the True Ancestor’s sacred accord.

Dragon plows, tiger sows—
Jade nectar and golden herbs,
What splendid Daoist work!

The elixir’s cauldron glows with light,
Behold a childlike form,
Swiftly vanishing—shocking Heaven and Earth.

Riding the purple clouds,
Emerald phoenixes come to greet,
True offspring of the immortals.

At the dawn of the Three Yang,
Jade medicine’s celestial fragrance,
Qixiang flowers and precious trees,
Enveloped by auspicious clouds.

Heavenly light shimmers,
Moonbeam shadows stretch—
The Great Transformation of the Peng bird follows.

Do not dismiss this as wild talk,
For within it lies clear distinction—
Only the adept recognize its subtleties.

Among the bold and virtuous,
Spirit refined and courageous,
Nature lofty and resolve unyielding.

---
**Eighteen**
With resolve piercing the clouds,
Spirit born of Heaven’s finest,
Escaping the endless search for truth.

Empty space as furnace, self as fire,
True nature encountered—refinement begins.

If the teacher is not enlightened,
Even near at hand, it’s as distant as a thousand miles,
And truth is lost in deception.

These yellow sprouts and red essences—
All mortals possess them,
Yet how many are foolishly blind?

True heroes seize fate’s mechanisms,
Piercing the chaos,
Gaining the luminous Night-Bright Pearl of Joy.

Gleaming with radiant treasures,
Flashing with sacred light,
Shadows vanish into the Great Abyss—no hindrance.

Do not let the mind’s monkey run wild,
Stealing the Golden Cauldron,
Wasting effort in vain elixir-making.

Igniting the Three Yang’s True Fire,
Ever refining, yet fleeing the Nine Returns.

---
**Nineteen**
Piercing frost and snow,
Facing wind and rain,
Meeting the Sage who awakens understanding.

Entering the subtle, penetrating the marvelous,
Reviving the dead, returning life—
This is the true rule of elixir refinement.

Separating from the perilous and uniting,
Returning to Yin and Yang’s cycle,
Requires the aid of the Wood Dragon and Golden Tiger.

Holding the Heaven-Earth cauldron,
The Five Phases arrayed,
Dwelling in the True Soil.

At the profound mysteries—
Sowing the yellow sprouts,
Burning into elixir,
To whom shall this logic be explained?

Phoenix brooding, jade-encased dragon pearls,
Flying forth from the depths of auspicious clouds.

**[Pulling lightning through the void]**
Speaking of the Three Corpses fleeing,
Six Thieves scattering in terror.

Revealing the Daoist embryo’s flight,
Five clouds swirling,
Harmonious sounds rising in chorus.

---**Twenty**---

---

**Nine**
To brave snow and frost, to meet wind and rain,
To greet the breeze and bathe in the mist—
A rare chance to find the Sage and gain enlightenment.
To grasp the subtle, enter the marvelous,
Revive the dead, restore life—
This is the Daoist standard for elixir cultivation.

Yin and Yang in harmony,
Turning the pivot of the cosmos,
The Dragon and Tiger coiling in ceaseless motion.

Who can fathom this celestial mechanism,
Its ebb and flow? Few understand its path.
How could one distinguish its true nature?

The logic of the Immortal’s Way—
Auspicious *qi* surging, blessed clouds ascending,
Purple mists veiling the golden palaces.

Thousands of deities gathered,
Ten thousand transformations complete,
Only then does the Great Elixir ripen.

The *qi*-tree blooms with jade flowers,
Filling the void with their splendor—
The True Landscape, emerald and vivid, stands revealed.

Beholding the Heart’s clarity like a moonlit dawn,
Cool winds sweeping the horizon,
The Celestial Cavern bright and open.

**[The *Peaceful Return* and *Rebirth of the Sage* Suites]**
Laughing at my humble self,
Ordinary passions I’ve cast aside,
Lightly abandoning my old fishing by the cliff’s edge.

Galloping through Chang’an,
Listening to the oriole’s song in the imperial gardens,
Yet in vain did I squander my youth in Luoyang.

At the Jade Hall, summons are issued,
Beside the Golden Throne, I join the feasts,
Repeatedly receiving imperial edicts on elixir refinement.

In what year did I dream beneath the huai tree,
Still clad in my humble raincoat by the Jiang River’s banks?
Heaven bestows upon me
Endless layers of cloud screens, the Five Lakes’ misty waves,
Wild monkeys and sand cranes—
Boundless wilderness, untamed.

At dawn, the Purple Pavilion,
By dusk, the Mysterious Isle,
My hair drying in the crimson mist of the forest’s edge.

The Azure Dragon leaps from the sea,
The White Crane ascends to the heavens—
In a single instant, all is fulfilled.

Gazing toward the Pure Celestial Court,
The crisp autumn winds and dews,
The Celestial Cavern’s first light.

---

**Twenty**
A quiet chamber to cultivate the heart,
Mountains and clouds to nurture the Dao—
Nearly encountering the Sage to receive the secret precepts.

The furnace stacked with the Eight Trigrams,
The cauldron prepared with the Three Talismans,
Building the foundation of Daoist practice.

Yin and Yang aligned,
Turning the cosmic pivot,
The Dragon and Tiger coiling in endless dance.

This celestial mechanism—
Its inverse and direct—
The scholarly currents do not comprehend.
How could one distinguish its true nature?

The logic of the Luminous and the Obscure—
Auspicious *qi* billowing, blessed clouds gathering,
Purple vapors enveloping the golden palaces.

Thousands of deities assembled,
Ten thousand transformations complete,
Then the Great Elixir is ripe.

The *qi*-tree and jade flowers,
Filling the void with their splendor—
The True Vision, emerald and resplendent, stands in array.

Gazing upon the Heart’s clarity like the moon’s bright reflection,
Cool breezes sweeping the eye,
The Celestial Cavern’s light piercing through.

---

**Second Suite**
Sweeping away winds and clouds,
Parting the dust like silk,
I’ve settled upon half a hill to hide my flaws.

A green pine as my shelter,
White stones as my bed—
All worldly cares now rest.

How many times have I visited Penglai,
Wearing a coarse robe, wielding a long sword,
Leisurely facing the waves’ serene clarity?

Whose home is this,
Where the wine is aged in the Immortal’s gourd,
Inviting me to share the bright moon’s gaze?

Returning now—
The Jade Palace vast and empty,
The Silver River stark and cold,
A single iron flute’s note splitting the mountain.

The Three *Hua* [1] encircle me in splendor,
The Nine *Qi* [2] weave like a net—
Lofty and ethereal, the Pure Celestial Gate.

Holding the *Fu Rong* [3] in hand,
Ascending the void in flying steps,
Tonight, how many will pay homage?

Then I turn—
The Northern Dipper as my ladle,
Scattering fragrant wine and snow across the purple cups.

---

**Third Suite**
When the mountain moon arrives,
The sea wind stirs not,
A jade tower and pavilion rise upon the plain.

The cassia’s fragrance drifts,
The dew’s luster like water,
I pluck the Celestial Flute, its notes delicate as silk.

Faint and distant, clear and distinct,
The Green Tortoise [4] transmits its sweet words.

Within the *Tai Wei* [5],
The *luan* [6] and crane seek each other—
All are old companions of the True Dao.

Hear now,
The Leopard’s Gate locked in layers,
The thunderous drums of a thousand officials,
The Celestial Realm’s endless courts.

The Stone Maiden pins her flowers,
The Wooden Man pours the wine—
Let me dwell here for a while.

Singing in lofty verses,
Wielding the brush with boundless strokes,
The dusty world is but trifles of past and present.

Look upon the Spring Mountain,
All in verdant green—
Why does it mock the broken clouds and lingering rain?

---

**Fourth Suite**
The moon’s brilliance, the frost’s chill,
My fishing boat like a leaf—
Leisurely crossing the clear, blue stream.

The Milky Way silent,
The jade rainbow arching over the wilds,
The Dipper’s handle now pointing north.

Half a black hat,
A few strands of white hair,
A single glance at the wild cranes in flight.

Ask of the returning Sage,
The old trees of the southern city—
How many have they seen of past and present?

At the Western Hua’s peak,
A flower ten *zhang* high,
Autumnal dew from the Nine Heavens,
Forming emerald chambers and jade fruits.

To cast off my shoes is no hardship,
Ascending the void—how distant?
Three gulps, and the snow melts into ice *qi*.

The *Divine Method of Abstaining from Grain*,
The *True Precept of Feasting on Clouds*—
Once gone, no trace remains.

Laughing at the world’s dwellers,
Long abiding in the void,
Who compares to a single wheel of red sun?

---

**Fifth Suite**
Loosening my oars in the boundless waves,
The setting sun’s last rays on the fallen clouds,
I lean upon the shore as the mountain turns.

Riding the wild geese, the double ducks,
Cutting through the reeds, drifting on the willows—
My body in a painted autumn scene.

The rain carries the sound of the shallows,
The wind shakes the candle’s shadow,
Midnight still finds me reciting my scroll.

Counting my parting emotions,
Why must they stretch to the heavens?
A mere step’s distance, yet the path is long, and people are far.

Laughing at myself alone,
The scholar from Luoyang,
The aged man of Xiangyang—
How often have they dreamed of me?

Old now at the Floating Mound,
Composing poetry beneath the bright moon,
A thousand *ren* [7] of verdant sky and sharp blade.

After the snow clears, the jade towers,
Spring blooms on the jade mats—
Let me host a grand feast in my old mountain home.

Waiting for the rooster’s crow,
The sun rising over Luo Fu,
Flying across the waves’ shallow, clear depths.

---

**Sixth Suite**
To drink wine while songs are sung,
Without cares to be resolved—
This is the Daoist’s true bearing.

A fine breeze passing through my ears,
The moon’s brilliance filling my chest,
The pure sounds of water and mountain hues.

A thousand years in the world,
Seven days in the mountains—
I’ve grown accustomed to wandering as a guest.

Across the void,
The Northern Dipper and Southern Star—
Who could ever truly grasp this?

Once I recalled,
The blue-eyed barbarian monk,
In a coarse robe by the boundless sea,
Lowering his fishing line a thousand *chi* deep.

Pulling up a whale,
The wind and thunder transforming—
Not a common marvel.

Cold and heat urging each other,
Heaven and Earth no longer needed,
Through countless kalpas, never stale with time.

Alas, my life—
Forgetting my lofty years,
Long accompanying children’s games and plays.

---

**Seventh Suite**
Remembering the Sage of the Slope,
Nightly wandering at the Red Cliff,
A lone crane skimming past my boat to the west.

The heroes have all faded,
My life and fate now obscure—
The moon is small, the waters cold, the stars vast.

How like the fisherman,
Unknowing of past and present,
Drunk beside the water plant and firefly.

In dreams we meet—
Feathers fluttering, robes swaying,
Not necessarily this moment, not I alone.

Who understands the Dao?
At the year’s end, the river is empty—
The wind’s force, the moon’s might,
Crossing spears and composing verse by the Jiang River’s left bank.

The evening dew on my garments,
The late wind at the isles,
How many short poems and long odes have I penned?

The Jade Palace’s lofty chill,
Where are my old friends now?
Vast and distant, my heart knows no rest.

I sigh at the journey,
Sailing the sea in a frail boat,
My followers not knowing who might accompany me.

---

**Eighth Suite**
Returning now—
Yesterday’s folly, today’s truth,
Sadness alone, my words in vain.

My path lost is not far,
Morning light soft and warm—
I command my guide to lead the way.

The wind lifts my light boat,
Children at the gate,
This day I behold my humble home.

Wine fills the cups—
Though the three paths are overgrown,
The pine and chrysanthemum still stand as before.

I’ll leave my arrogance,
Defying the world’s ways,
Old friends all forgotten—
Where else shall I ride my boat to?

---
[1] *Hua* (花) – Refers to the three *Hua* (flower-like formations) of *qi* in Daoist alchemy.
[2] *Qi* (氣) – Refers to the nine types of *qi* or breath in Daoist practice.
[3] *Fu Rong* (芙蓉) – A lotus flower, symbolizing purity and enlightenment.
[4] *Green Tortoise* – Refers to the mythical tortoise associated with the *Tai Wei* constellation, often linked to Daoist immortality and cosmic cycles.
[5] *Tai Wei* (太微) – A constellation in Daoist cosmology, often associated with celestial harmony and the abode of immortals.
[6] *Luan* (鸞) – A mythical bird, often paired with the crane (*he* 鹤) and symbolizing auspiciousness and celestial union.
[7] *Ren* (仞) – A unit of measure (approximately 500 meters or 1600 feet), emphasizing the vastness of the sky.

**其八**
Returning now, ah! What was wrong is now right—
Alone, I sigh in sorrow, speechless with grief.
The lost path is not far; dawn’s light glows bright,
And I command my guide to lead the way ahead.

A breeze lifts my light boat, children at the gate,
Today I gaze upon my humble home once more.
Though wine fills the cup and paths lie wild with time,
The pine and chrysanthemum stand as they were before.

I take my pride in defiance of the world,
Forgot my old friends—where shall I ride my boat to now?

---

**其九**
Strings and books, whispered words, seeking valleys and hills,
The weary crow perches where clouds and mist conspire.
The farmer tells me, “There’s work in the western fields,”
And I set forth alone, penning verse in spring’s rain.

But I take joy in Heaven’s decree—what need to doubt
The unfolding of Nature’s will? Let it come and go.

Ten years on the Jiang, ten years on Yan Mountain,
Accustomed to half a life of wind and snow.
Facing snow without a boat, drifting without snow,
No chance to meet those pure and lofty in spirit.

Broken shores, scattered sands—what night is this?
Like returning to Ke Xi’s stream, bound for Yue.

Yet I lift the sail, and there—
A few feet of plum blossoms, where human traces fade.

Do you not see the Five Elders’ perilous peaks,
Floating Master’s lofty summit, laughing at my early gray?
To reverse age, to refine the coarse into the subtle—
I have only the Nine Returns’ elixir in vain.

The sun breaks through, the sky dazzles the sea,
And all distinctions dissolve in oneness.

Then I can proclaim—
The Six-Yi Immortal Sage, the eternal bright moon of the Void.

---

**其十**
Sixty years returned, now past seventy,
Grateful for the Emperor’s grace and favor.
Early to bed, late to rise,
Drinking when thirsty, eating when hungry—
No cares, no thoughts.

A few volumes of tattered books,
A half-broken inkstone—
Enough for a scholar’s modest life.

Master Dao, write swiftly what I can recite—
Truly, I am far from here.

No more pondering—
Just lean on my green staff,
Wear my double-strapped sandals,
And walk to the ferry to watch the water flow.

The past rushes by, the present comes in waves—
Unmindful, the day grows late, the wind grows fine.

A fisherman calls out suddenly—
“What are you staring at?”

Then he helps me carry fresh fish,
And we drink together, drunk as one.

---

**十一**
A path leads to the depths of mystery,
A painted screen of emerald—
Walking to where white clouds gather.

Peaches of the world beyond, oranges by the well,
A garden of rare mushrooms and elixir plants.

Light taps on the *tan* board, the zither plays softly,
Offering phoenix fat and lynx meat.

Dancing, my white hair drifts like the wind,
Still like the old immortal companions.

Look—
Palaces of the gods, gold and jade in every hall,
This is the daily life of the *médhu* moth.

Five-colored Penglai, the autumnal *diāo* bird,
There is another path to transcendence.

Wine ripens with Ma Gu, clouds rise from Wu Gorge,
I bow to the Celestial Caverns and depart.

Let the sea waves be clear and shallow—
Where is the green window, the cloudy door?

---

**十二**
Light clouds, gentle winds,
Following flowers and willows—
As if youth’s joys were still mine.

High pavilions in the woods,
A small carriage in the city—
Eternal peace in the Western Luo.

Behold the vastness—
Speaking of the virtuous one,
The flowing water seems as it was yesterday.

But leisurely travels meet only light clouds at the sky’s edge,
Uncertain if sorrow or parting awaits.

I remember well—
As a youth, we followed each other,
Bathing in Yi and returning,
Reciting as the swallows flew, the fish leaped.

The past rushes on—
I am aging, yet I adjust my ways.

The *qín* strings hum in the sacred hall,
The old chamber’s bells and stones—
Hidden, I seem to hear them still.

The farmer tells me, “There’s work in the western fields,”
And my books hang from the ox’s horns.

---
**满江红**
*For Master Feng*

Seasons hurry by—
Suddenly, autumn’s message arrives.
Past deeds rise—
So many triumphs and failures,
A hundred years like a fleeting breath.

The scholar’s ambition unfulfilled,
The mountains early claimed my retreat.
I sought the Five Lakes’ leisure, but Xiqi’s joy was rare—
No gain, no loss.

Human affairs—
Full of sorrow and regret.
The world beyond—
A different rhythm, a different grace.

This Penglai is serene and fair,
Jade halls, golden seals.
Bound by mortal cares, yet my heart is pure,
My spirit soars like the gods.

See the phoenix welcome me to the azure sky,
The clouds guide me home.

---
**其二**
Rain passes over the eastern suburbs,
The stream’s trace is shallow—
Spring dawn in the mountain hall.

Worthy of love—
Peach blossoms in flowing water,
Leisurely clouds, quiet crows.

Beyond the world, the sun rises red,
A single green hill at the world’s edge.
Toward the green shade, bamboo shadows roll the gate,
Forever settled.

In this quiet—
Who knows?

The recluse of the world,
Rare in human company.

Let me embrace wind and cup, moon and wine,
Drunk on fragrant grass.

Great purpose contains the heavens and earth,
True feeling stands firm in Xiqi’s depths.
In vain I send news to the forests and streams—
Old in mist and clouds.

---
**其三**
High sentiments through the ages
Lie in forests, streams, and winding rivers.
Knowing this life is but a dream,
Why envy silk robes and grand halls?

I love the moon’s reflection on the carved dock,
The sage does not envy gold mountains or jade.
Joy fills the courtyard as flowers cast golden light,
Moss stains the green.

Forever—
The east hedge’s chrysanthemum.

A hollow-hearted staff,
Southern veranda bamboo.
Pillowed on books and *qín*, I sleep soundly,
Unshamed, at ease.

A thousand years of rise and fall—
A spring dream awakens.
One stream of clouds and water—
Enough for my life.

Look at the Three Wuling Beauties,
Their fragrant breath.
The elixir fields are ripe.

---
**其四**
Master of the Eastern Village,
Where is your home—
Mountain shadows, winding streams?

「其五」
A mind at leisure,
Bright and open—
The Daoist’s heart, straight as heaven’s void.
Though my body cannot yet rise weightless,
I dwell in a humble *Daoist* dwelling.

Within my cup, I gaze and swallow the sun and moon,
Not envying the world’s hoarded gold and jade.
Let the fleeting years shift like *qi*’s illusion,
Scattering crimson and verdant hues.

The cinnabar well’s bloom—
Golden chrysanthemums.
The *lingzhi* mushrooms, the *lángkān* bamboo.

Before the heartless wind’s carefree sway,
What honor or shame remains?

A hundred years of great dream drift beyond,
All worldly matters—
A mind’s content.

Toward mortal realms, three times witness the Yellow River’s clarity,
The peach of immortality ripens.

---
**其六**
A mind at leisure,
The *Hairy Skull Child*—
Endless birth and death.

「被化机，搬弄驰骋，许多颠蹙。」
Mastered by the subtle *qi* of transformation,
Skillfully manipulated and unrestrained—
Endless trials and tribulations.

Buying bones like mountains—what purpose serves?
Lost in passion like the sea—how to transcend?
Grief pierces the primal essence of things long buried in dust and ages.
A *Dharma*’s cycle of suffering.

To seek liberation, one must be fierce.
To find true companions, speak of ice and snow.
With diligent effort and refinement,
The luminous *Dao* shines through.

When winds cease and waves settle, the depths reveal—
Clouds part, the cold moon sinks into heaven’s void.

Asking the mute for honey’s taste—unspeakable.
**Its Seventh: Cloudyang Child**
Raising a void fist,
Unadorned by forms—
Scales and iron are but dust.

Daring to endure the weight of the world,
At times, one must be a man of unyielding resolve.
Ancient Buddhas pluck the flower with a faint smile,
Yet in this age, how few stand waist-high in snow?

Lamenting the cuckoo’s bloodied branches—who understands?
The mute’s dream, hard to discern.
The deaf, who grasp the meaning.

On a lone peak’s summit,
A wooden man speaks eloquently.
Cawing crows and howling monkeys debate the *non-duality* of the *Dao*,
While pine winds and mountain waters reveal its profound truth.

Breaking this mechanism, one sees the cold void—
Every household’s moon.

**Its Eighth: Yuan’s Original Intent**
At the beginning, nothing exists—
All *Dharma*’s roots obscured by the void.
Lamenting those who drift along learning the *Dao*,
Who refuse to sever before death.

Empty gestures and hollow punches—just noise.
Eyebrows raised, glances dart—endless posturing.
Seeing the light of wisdom fall to earth,
The virtuous rise—
Lifting hands and feet.

Abandon false thoughts,
Forget self and others.
Sever fame and gain,
Avoid right and wrong.
Accompany mist and clouds in secluded depths,
Walk freely with ease.

When realms dissolve, the mind forgets all birth—
The sky’s expanse vast and open.
A single wheel of moon reveals itself in the cold pool,
No deception in truth.

**Its Ninth: Mo’s Celestial Tripod**
*Dharma*’s essence lies in the primal void,
Its mysteries—
Beyond words to say.

Its core lies in guarding the *Zhong Zheng* (central rectitude),
The luminous *lingtai* (spiritual platform) clear.
The *Taiyi* (Great Polarity) dwells within the Yellow Valley,
Primal *qi* resides in the *Xuan Guan* (Mysterious Pass) orifice.
Motionless and still, yet responsive—
Relying on unyielding resolve.

Summoning wind and thunder,
Praying for rain and snow.
Commanding spirits and demons,
Driving away malevolent forces.
This is the *incantation of right and wrong*,
Neither talisman nor *geometric magic*.

In stillness and calm, the spirit returns to the Yellow Valley’s domain,
When merit is complete and the *Dao*’s path fulfilled—
Ranked among the celestial immortals.
Riding the auspicious clouds of the *Taiyi*’s void,
Toward the golden gates.

**Its Tenth: Purchasing Green Mountains**
Acquiring green mountains,
Then setting aside—
Straw sandals and a staff of *Ligustrum*.
No need to linger,
Below the *Jian Zhang* (Celestial Building) Palace,
At the *Ba Ling* (Farewell) Bridge’s edge.

The world’s chaos awaits like a snail’s touch,
While fame and gain are but ant-hills of hollow comfort.
In recent years, white hair has grown—
Three thousand spans long.
From now on, I cast off
The crimson dust’s entanglement.
A green stone pillow,
Pine winds echoing.

The *Four Worthies of Shang* (Mountain) come and go at leisure,
Fire dates and autumn dew—
A bargain’s worth.
Exchange pears, nurtured by spring’s warmth.
Counting those who’ve matched my carefree freedom since antiquity—
None but me.

**[The Farewell to Jiangnan] – Spring**
*Chou Changchun* (Spring in the Mountains)
Mountains are good,
Best in spring’s embrace.
Wildflowers red and white in myriad hues,
The *kuang ou* (mourning dove) calls in a hundred tones.
The misty greenery soaks one’s clothes.
Tea plucked fresh,
Bamboo shoots and ferns—
Like wild violet, gathered.

A hundredfold patched robe,
Forgotten worldly cares.
A few cups of rustic wine,
Aligned with heaven’s *Dao*.
Drunken, I let east and west drift.

**Summer**
Mountains are good,
Long summer suits them best.
Towering bamboo, a thousand stalks—
Golden chains shattered.
A thousand-foot cascade—
Jade curtains hanging.
Where is the scorching sun?
Beneath the pine’s shade,
Unrestrained and free.

Deep-fried plums and floating melons,
Serving as pillow and bedding.
Ancient pines and white stones,
Companions to the lute and chessboard.
Drunken, I let the winds carry me.

**Autumn**
Mountains are good,
Autumn’s scene is not desolate.
White wine, yellow fowl, and new rice—
Harvest’s bounty ripe.
Purple *zhu* (chrysanthemum) and golden *ju* (mallow), their fragrance pure.
Tangerines green with frost fill the woods—
Cool moon shines white,
Pines and *gui* (cryptomeria) stand dark and deep.
Only the village elder’s song of joy at the *she* (land deity) festival is heard,
No young men at the gate.
Drunken, what does it matter?

**Winter**
Mountains are good,
Yet the last praise belongs to winter.
Paper curtains and rush mats—
Fragrance faint, like jade’s pale glow.
Bamboo stove and tea kiln—
Flames burn deep red.
Crossed arms in warmth, the *chong* (tea ceremony) shared.
Man is but a dream,
A hundred years pass in an instant’s thought.
When plum blossoms burst, the spring’s pulse stirs,
Where snowflakes fall, the *yang* (sores/ulcers) vanish without trace.
Drunken, I am the slave of spring’s wind.

---
**Moonlight on the Sea-Tang (月上海棠)**
*Simao* (Simao) of the *Lun* (Lun) sect,
Ever mindful, never idle.
In coarse robes and hempen cords,
A satchel slung at my side.
Hair shorn, my head bare,
Unbound, I tread where I will.
With bowl and *dian* (bamboo begging cup),
Each day I alms-beg at the doors.
Bowing low, I take leave—
Then stumble upon a demon who speaks.

“Daoist Master,” he asks,
“Whose household are you from?”
I answer as fate allows:
“My teacher’s name is Qiu Liu Tan Ma.”

---
**Second Poem**
Last night, passing through *Bei Mang* (Northern Mound),
I saw a skull beside the road.
Rain washed it, winds blew—
A herdsman’s staff shattered its rest.
I knew him as Li Si, Zhang San, or Wang Da.
He bowed in silence, pondering me:
When death’s hour comes, how can one flee?
Though he had a thousand in gold,
No fortune could spare this calamity.
Cease your complaints—
All must meet the same end.

---
**Third Poem**
My words have warned countless thousands,
Yet none turn fiercely back.
I teach a thousand ways,
Yet they still cling to *huoyuan* (fire-karmic) bonds.
No reckoning—
Each life only defers the next.
Worried for sons and daughters without food or clothes,
They hope a hundred years’ companionship will last.
The *Yanwang* (King of Hell) arrives to demand,
Ghostly messengers knock at the door.
Dragged away, they do not question
Whether family ties are severed.

---
**Willow Pavilion (山亭柳)**
Worldly affairs are cause for sorrow,
The fleeting light of days cannot be held.
Spring fades, then autumn comes again—
The seasons press one toward old age,
A hundred years like *Zhuang Zhou’s* (Chuang Tzu’s) butterfly dream.
Seeing through the past as illusion,
Why cling to idle cares?
Boldly, I meet the *Xiyi* (Hsi-i, "One-Eyed") teaching,
Worldly passions—
All swept away in a stroke.
I vow to hasten my cultivation.
Yet fools, even when called by *Ma Dan Yang* (Madan Yang),
Still will not turn.
Bound by karmic debts, they become skulls,
Or wailing cranes in *Xu* (Xu)’s voice.

---
**Note on the Following Text:**
Below is the *Su Wu Man* (蘇武慢) composed by **Venerable Feng** (冯尊师) and **Yu Ji** (虞集), collected in thirty-three verses.
The text recorded in *Jiangcun Yezhu* (强村业书) by **Zhu Xiaozang** (朱孝臧) differs greatly from the *Dao藏* (Dao藏) version.
Here, I select several passages to correct and supplement the *Dao藏* text.
No further annotations are provided.

**#2 The following three are tunes.**

**Volume Three: Echoes of the Wandering Crane**
*Collected by Daoist Peng Zhizhong of Xianyou Mountain*

**Manting Fang (Full Court of Blossoms)**
**Wang Chongyang**
You were entrusted with the **Whole Truth of Quanzhen**,
Continuing the lineage of the Five Ancestors,
Briefly extolling the sect’s glory.
The **Laozi’s Golden Mouth** spoke,
Personally entrusting it to the **Western King**.
The **Holy Mother** bestowed teachings upon the **Eastern Master of Donghua**,
Binding the **Hua** and descending—**Zhongli** took the charge.
Transmitting the **Mystic Principle**,
**Liu Xiang of Rich Spring** and **Master Lü** awoke to the **Yellow Grain**.
Ascending to the Dao,
Fulfilling great vows,
Traveling along the **Gan River’s fate**,
And crossing over **Chongyang again**.

Journeying through Shandong and beyond,
Reaching the **Eastern Ocean**.
Witnessing seven golden lotuses rising from the waves—
**Qiu, Liu, Tan, Ma, He, Sun, and Wang**.
My disciples,
Gathered at the **Celestial Primordial Assembly**,
A thousand lotuses blooming in fragrance.

---

**#2 The Second: Master Ma Dan Yang**
My sword is no ordinary blade—
The **Jade Emperor** decreed it given to me.
Who else dares claim it?
A **three-foot green serpent**,
Often emitting auspicious light.
Stirring the **essence of Heaven and Earth**,
Splitting open **Taiyi’s True Yang**.
Who forged it?
**Ou Ye of Yexi**, blending **gold and water**—
Yin and yang in harmony.
Unknown where it is wielded,
Yet it slays demons and cuts through evils,
Bringing peace to all lands.
Turning the **myriad phenomena**,
All dissolved into **Mystic Frost**.
Only those who neglect cultivation
Lightly point—
Their **spirit and qi scatter**.
The sheath resounds,
Thunder shakes the heavens,
Ten thousand miles of ghosts and spirits cower.

---

**#3 The Third: Reflective Grasping**
A hundred years pass like a dream—
Why not live in ease?
Adrift in carefree joy,
Enjoying a tranquil self.
Days and months flee like arrows—
Unnoticed, **time passes**, **hair turns white**, **eyes dim**.
Reflecting on past and present,
Once-bold warriors now lie buried in **Beimang Hill**.
Better to cultivate virtue,
**Free from sorrow**, nurturing youthful vigor.
Fear not the **Limit of Impermanence**,
Taming the **wild horse of desire**.
Let not **spirit and qi decay**—
Lock the **White Ox** within the **Golden Barrier**.
Cultivation is no trifle—
Guard your own life as precious.

---

**#4 The Fourth: The True Person of Sanfeng**
A fallen, idle man,
A carefree vagabond,
Silent to all who pass.
Drifting like dust in the wind,
Coming and going through the streets.
Begging in alleys and lanes,
Dwelling in **ancient temples**, **vacant halls**.
If asked, *"Who are you?"*
**Gentlemen**, do not inquire—
The **Three Pure Ones**, the **Supreme Saints**,
**Zhongli and Lü** as their lineage.
Worshipping **Qiu, Liu, Tan, Ma**,
Turning the **Divine Function**.
