Obtaining the **Mystic’s profound use**,
A **Pure Void resolve**—
**Vague yet profound**.
Embracing **True Emptiness**,
Speaking of **Eternal Life**,
Mastering the **Three Teachings**.

---

**#5 The Fifth: Master Ma Dan Yang**
A young, enlightened child,
Taking the Dao as his path,
Listening closely to his teacher’s words.
Rising at dawn,
Sweeping the ground—**no dust stirred**.
Washing his body clean,
Then **wiping the pot**, **clutching the basin**.
In the kitchen,
**Pure oil, rice, and flour**—
Not a grain wasted.
When guests arrive,
Receive them with grace,
Walking slowly, speaking softly.
Guard **purity and poverty**,
Avoiding vain glory.
At dusk, sit upright,
**Mind clear**, **eyes bright**.
Do not stray—
**Heaven and Earth endure**,
A bright future awaits.

---

**#6 The Sixth: Yesterday’s Blossoms**
Today’s petals fall—
Counting the fleeting moments.
Marrying, planning—
**Eon after eon**, for whom the rush?
Once youthful and vibrant,
In an instant—**green hair turns white**.
Alas, the human body knows not **Impermanence**—
So bitter, so fleeting.
Better to **awaken early**—
Gold and silver piled high
Cannot buy **Impermanence’s arrival**.
Gazing at the **peaks of home**,
Tears stream in vain.
No children to replace you—
In the end, **you bear it alone**.
Heed my warning—
**Returning light, reflecting brilliance**,
Accompany **Master Ma Dan Yang**.

---

**#7 The Seventh: The Living Dead**
Men become **walking corpses**,
Women **hollow bones**,
Parents—**mere skulls**.
Children and grandchildren,
Generation after generation—**tiny skulls**.
Time passes, they grow,
Amassing wealth to **match their skulls**.
Filling the halls,
**Living ghosts** play with skulls all day.
The household’s master—
A **skull-man**, busy and frantic,
Nurturing **skulls**.
When death comes,
Who will tend **your skull**?
When the **three inches of breath** fade,
The **living skull** sends the **dead skull** on its way.
Do not grieve—
I urge you to **awaken early**,
Tending to **your skull**.

---

**#8 The Eighth: Returning Home**
Better to return—
Returning is best.
All else is **gain without profit**.
No **sorrow**, no **quarrels of right and wrong**.
Choose a **pure spot by the cliffs**,
Building a **small hermitage**.
At dusk, sleep soundly,
Until the **Grand Fast**.
Beyond this,
No other matters—
Adrift in joy, **who knows?**
High office may be sought,
Yet must be **pursued with humility**.
If surrounded by **flatterers and sycophants**,
**Gold belts** may **damage your robes**.
Consider—
A single mouth to feed,
How many **spoons** can it hold?

---

**#9 The Ninth: The Rise and Fall of the Dao**
The **Dao Teaching** first flourished,
While **Buddhism** remained obscure—
One rises, one fades.
**Bodhidharma** expounded the **Dharma**,
From **Eastern Lands to the Western Heaven**.
All later disciples,
Greedy for **wine and desire**,
**Corrupting the True Source**.
Quarreling over **wealth and power**,
Ignoring the **Teachings**,
Yet still hoping to reach **Western Paradise**.
A **once-in-three-thousand-years** opportunity—
The **Quanzhen Great Teaching**,
The **Year of Jiazi**, the **Heavenly Span**.
**Master Qiu** expounded the **Doctrine**,
A thousand golden lotuses.
**Celestial Assembly of Immortals** descends,
**Demons submit**—
Only the **Dao’s worthy** prevail.
Do you know?
This chance may not return
For **ten thousand years**.

---

**#10 The Tenth: Fleeting Beauty**
Children like blossoms,
Wives like jade—
Yet time slips away.
Piling wealth a thousandfold
Cannot buy **Impermanence’s arrival**.
Suddenly, **Yin Official** summons you—
No excuse, no delay.
Empty-handed you return,
**Wealth passes to another**,
Children scattered like leaves.
**The Wandering Crane’s Echoes** conclude.

「#10 The Tenth: Fleeting Beauty」
The wise and virtuous leave early,
Avoiding the **Fiery Realm**,
Breaking free from **busyness**.
**Master Qiu**’s **Scattered Leisure** descends,
Leaving behind **emotional tranquility**.
After hunger, one begs at **Temple Gates** for alms,
In cold, **paper and cloth robes** are sought—
No **entangling attachments**,
The **Immortal’s Path** remains unfinished,
Yet **divination** reveals **longevity’s extension**.

---

**#11 The Eleventh: The Hermitage Within**
The body is the **hermitage**,
The self its **abbot**—
Ears and eyes are its **gates and windows**.
The **walls** hold my **dwelling**,
My **belly** wraps the **kitchen**.
The **mind** is the **head chef**,
Skilled in **refining Water and Fire**,
To forge **Original Yang**.
When the **mind is at peace**,
Food ripens in due time,
And the **master** tastes it with delight.
Do not step outside the **hermitage**,
Lest you lose your way,
And fail to return to your **native land**.
Sit firmly within,
Repairing the **Central Cavern**.
Refine the **Golden Pillars** and **Jade Beams**,
Piercing through **clear winds** and **luminous moonlight**—
**Divine Radiance’s** essence.
Sit in stillness,
Unshaken, unmoved—
What fear is there of **harsh winds and frosts**?

---

**#12 The Twelfth: The Indescribable Dao**
The **Great Dao** is formless,
Indescribable, unspeakable—
The world fails to grasp its **root**.
It does not rely on **purity and clarity**,
Yet **filthy ink** seeks **scripted texts**.
If one clings only to **scriptures**,
The world has many **adepts**—
All would claim **Dao attainment**,
Filling the **Nine Heavens** above,
Crowding the **Jade Emperor’s Court**.
Why bother with **eloquent debate**,
Or exhaust **the Zhouyi Classic**,
Or lecture on the **Yellow Court**?
**True purity**, **true clarity**—
The **mind** must be free of **dust**.
**Divine Immortals** will guide you,
And then, you’ll **ascend to the Mystic Gate**.
In **profound subtlety**,
**Leisure and joy** unfurl—
All day, **laughing and chatting**.

---

**#13 The Thirteenth: The Trial of the Age**
In this **barren year**,
**Dao disciples** across the land
Suffer **demons’ affliction**, endure **calamity**.
Only now does **true sincerity** reveal itself—
**Dao companions**, in an instant,
**Generously aid** the **Celestial Immortals**.
The **Broad Virtue Heavenly Venerable**,
The **Loyal and Resplendent Martyrs**—
In the **Jiazi decade**, there are **five thousand**.
With **unyielding resolve**,
The **Nine Heavens’ Celestial Gate**,
Endless **golden lotuses** bloom.
When **demons** arise, **resolve** must come first—
Do not let **evil** sway your **mind**.
At the moment of **drawing the sword**,
Your **true nature** stands firm as a **mountain**.
The **Three Pure Ones** and **Holy Saints** appear everywhere,
Not bound by **meritorious deeds**.
No need to **fulfill rites**—
With **doubtless resolve**, the **Holy Saints** urge all **disciples**:
“Will you **forget form and body**,
And **ascend with me**?”

**#14 The Fourteenth: The Elixir’s Virtue**
Sweet **licorice**, **ginseng**, **Chinese valerian**, **peony**,
Thin **mint**, **schizonepeta**, and **chuanxiong**.
**Frankincense**, **myrrh**, **white chrysanthemum**, and **sweet osmanthus**.
**Pearl**, **gold**, **loquat**, **dang gui**, **honey-suckle**, **poria**.
**Goji berries**, **chrysanthemum flowers**, **dandelion**, and **reishi**.
**Huo xiang**, **divided doses** of **sichuan lovage**—
Each must be **measured precisely**.
What matters if your **whole body burns with fever**,
Or if **left and right** are **imbalanced**,
Or **headwinds** plague you?
Prescribe the **single character**,
“**Mouth**—**Nose**—**[blank]**.”
**Divine Elixir’s** efficacy is **verified**—
The **Noble Consort Li**’s **double vision** was **undone**.
Indeed, its **effect** pleased **Emperor Zhangzong**,
Earning an **additional promotion** to **Golden Rank**.

**#15 The Fifteenth: The Circulation of the Two Qi**
The **Two Qi** revolve endlessly,
The **Three Palaces** ascend and descend—
**Infinite cycles** of **coming and going**.
Piercing through **Gate-controlling Divine Water**,
**Lead and Mercury** pass the **Three Peaks**.
**Returning and flowing** through the **Eight Vessels**,
**Steel and Jade** refine—
**Yin Tiger**, **Yang Dragon** **flourish** in **Steel and Jade**.
At the **concentration of essence**,
**Golden Flowers** bloom—
**[Blank]** reveals its **form**.
**Divine Radiance** is **true transformation**—
**Heavenly Mechanics** run deep,
Hard to **fathom** or **guess**.
Even **fine wine** and **lustful desires**,
Like **autumn winds**, are fleeting.
The **Great Dao’s Mystic Furnace** ignites—
Within the **Three Fields**, **Divine Elixir** is **nurtured**.
When **refinement is complete**,
**Heavenly Scriptures** summon you—
**Effortless strides** lead to the **Palace of the Immortals**.

**#16 The Sixteenth: [Zhang Borden’s] True Iron Ox**
A **True Iron Ox**,
Ugly in form, **unyielding** in nature—
**Stubborn**, **contentious**, **fond of strife**.
All possess it—
Who **understands** its **bondage**?
**Sow the Yellow Sprouts** across the **Court**,
And **irrigate with Divine Water**.
Within the **Central Palace**,
If this **beast** were absent,
How could **[blank] babies** be born?
**Heaven and Earth** are **true stillness and movement**—
**Life’s essence** depends on it.
**Hungry**, it feeds on **tiger marrow**,
**Thirsty**, it drinks from the **Mercury Pool**.
At **midnight**, it **drags and refines** the **fire**—
**Bright radiance** **erupts**, like **ocean depths** **tossing light**.
The **herdsman** returns,
After feasting at the **Flowering Pool**,
Beneath the **moon’s clarity**.

After **reflection**,
**Turning the heart toward the Dao**,

**Walking and sitting together**,
**Drinking ambrosial nectar**.
**[Blank]**.

**Singing the *Mantingfang* in the courtyard**.

**#2 The Second: The Three Teachings United**
**Daoist**, **Buddhist**, and **Confucian** doors—
The **Three Teachings** **merge as one**—
**Equal in status**, **shouldering the same burden**.
The **Dao** divides **Heaven and Earth**,
All **transformations** return to its **foundation**.
The **Buddha** **attains fruit** on **Spiritual Mountain**,
After **six years**, **meditating** at the **Snowy Peak**.
The **Confucian Teaching**—
**Warmth**, **gentleness**, **reverence**, **modesty**—
**Educates emperors** across **ten thousand generations**.
The **Great Dao** **transmits secret keys**,
The **Buddha’s Teachings** offer **skillful means**—
**Enduring insults**, **compassionate mercy**.
**Greatly accomplished**, **most holy**—
How could they **be ranked** as **higher or lower**?
All are **late learners**,
**Junior disciples**—
Some **deny**, some **affirm**, **debating right and wrong**.
Do not **compete in spirit**—
The **Three Venerables** are **one in essence**,
**Gazing upon** and **surrendering to** them **together**.

This incense—**naturally pure and refined**—
Born **before the Elephant Sovereign’s** reign.
In the **golden censer’s** flames, **auspicious smoke** ascends in spirals.
Not **sandalwood** nor **ambergris**,
Nor **four-harmony** dragon’s musk—
**Offered first** to **ancient sages**, then to **Five Ancestors of Great Luo Heaven**.

Its **mystic virtue** pervades the **Dharma Realm**,
**Qi and scent** complete and true.
It **opens the nasal passages**,
**Penetrating** to the **most profound Dao**.

May the **Eight Wastes and Four Seas** all **share this sublime transformation**,
**Dao-qi** **enduring** without end.
From this day forward,
**One brings blessings** for **ten thousand generations**.

**#3 – Lü Dongbin**

**Worldly affairs** **flurry**—
**Like water** **flowing eastward**,
**When** **does** **this** **end**?

**Lament** **the fame and gain** **of a thousand ages**,
**Racing** **like tigers and leopards**,
**Hills and valleys** **in a moment**,
**All** **accompany foxes and dogs**.

**Among thorns and punishments**,
**In the fading light of the setting sun**,
**Tombs in disarray**—
**Who** **knows** **whose**?

**Do you know**?
**All** **labor** **in vain** **for a hundred years**,
**Wrinkling brows** **in emptiness**.

**Better** **to return** **as** **one** **comes**—
**Free** **from the Four Great Elements**, **unbounded leisure**.

**To the Green Cliff Cave** **return**,
**Perfect** **life’s vitality**,
**Facing wind** **and moon**,
**Laughing** **and scoffing** **at the mundane**.

**A single tune of zither and song**,
**A thousand measures of fine wine**,
**The sun and moon** **cycle endlessly**—
**Youth** **eternal**.

**Childlike face** **preserved**,
**Tortoise’s longevity**, **crane’s lifespan**,
**No need** **to sing** **of the yellow hen**.

**Second [Verse]**
**Not fond** **of light furs**,
**Clothes of coarse hemp**, **sandals of straw**,
**Letting spring** **and autumn** **be**.

**Though men** **mock me**,
**A life of rustic simplicity**,
**The world’s dust** **and clamor**—
**What** **do I ultimately seek**?

**External Penglai**, **inner Penglai**,
**A palm-sized realm** **within the jar**,
**This sect’s teaching** **is priceless**.

**Who knows**?
**Leisure’s joy** **is swift**,
**No envy** **of kings and nobles**.

**Many schemes** **only breed** **more sorrow**.
**Like swallowing** **the hooks** **of fame and gain**.

**Seeing** **before me** **these fleeting affairs**,
**Wasting Heaven’s secret**—
**Unwilling** **to withdraw**.

**Bees** **busy** **for flowers**,
**Moths** **drawn** **to lamps**,
**Only** **thus** **lost** **in front**, **forgetful** **of what’s behind**.
**Ah**, **the plight of life**—
**Zhuang Zhou’s butterfly dream**,
**The butterfly’s dream** **of Zhuang Zhou**.

**Third [Verse]**
**The Great Dao** **is nameless**,
**The Great Sound** **is rare**,
**The Great Vessel** **late in forming**.

**Laugh at those** **who mislead** **with shallow views**,
**Silence** **is best**—
**Like drilling ice** **for fire**,
**Or tying knots** **with pebbles**.

**Exhausting spirit**, **laboring in vain**,
**Seeking fish** **from trees**—
**When** **will** **this** **be cooked**?

**Foolish ones**,
**Grinding bricks** **to make mirrors**—
**How** **can** **they** **see** **the light**?

**Why** **scheme** **a hundred ways**?
**Guard simplicity**, **pure and undefiled**,
**Abandoning love and hate**.

**Clarify the empty heart**, **fill the honest belly**,
**The Spirit of the Grain** **does not die**,
**Deep roots**, **firm stems**,
**Long vision**, **eternal life**.

**Deep and clear**,
**Before Heaven** **and Earth**,
**One Qi** **vast and boundless**,
**Mingling** **in the primordial darkness**.

**This wheel of bright moon**,
**Never lacking**, **never full**.

**Fourth [Verse]**
**Auspicious snow**

**Sixth [Verse]**
The Peach Blossom Path—
No hindrance to coming and going,
Together we ascend and survey.

**Sixth [Verse]**
Urge the seekers to awaken,
Seize the Soul’s Platform—
Do not seek beyond!

This primordial mystery—
Not easily grasped—
Today, I tell you its roots.

The speechless old woman speaks,
The footless child plays with a ball.

True news:
Clouds bury the Jade Cave,
Moonlight gleams on the Golden Hall.

Who else can cultivate like me?
I tame the Lion and turn it to an ox.
In the Yellow River’s waves, I flip somersaults,
In the Sun Palace, I seize the wild monkey.

White snow blooms,
Green Cloud’s child takes the first step.
I claim the Mystic Pass as my own.

Leaving the Celestial Abode,
I ride the Qilong home,
Forever in Penglai Isle.

**Seventh [Verse]**
Last night in Nanjing,
This morning at Northern Peak—
Swiftly, suddenly.

I meet wine in the cave,
Drink when thirsty,
Use Mount Ju as my pillow,
Sleep deeply after drinking.

Boundless comings and goings,
Unfixed movements—
Half mad, half delirious.

With me always:
A chest of wind and moon,
Sleeves of cloud and mist.

Drifting through the world for years,
Now I prepare the Second Feast of the East Palace.

I topple the Jade Terrace,
Plant my Qí trees,
Shallow the Yellow River,
Cultivate my golden lotuses.

I shatter the coral,
Turn my back on Penglai,
Bow before the Void Emperor’s throne.

No difficult matter—
Eight hundred deeds accomplished,
Three thousand merits fulfilled.

**Eighth [Verse]**
Dissolving doubt,
Rejecting empty illusions,
Drinking and feeding as fate allows.

With cushion and meditation board,
I pass the daylight,
Facing the wind and moon,
To mark the passing years.

With a mountain boy in tow,
A willow staff in hand,
I lie down in the pine wind’s shadow.

From now on,
My golden needle and jade thread
Are sealed into smoke.

Why pass it down through generations?
The Weishui wind and pine have already revealed the truth.

In years past, I groped for the moon in water,
Now I understand—
Fire nurtures the lotus.

The highest teachings hold no deeper mystery.
Ten or a hundred—all return to One Thousand.

Turning my back,
I see the ocean’s stagnation cease,
Clouds disperse across the boundless sky.

**Ninth [Verse]**
Auspicious snow fills the heavens,
Blanketing the cosmos,
The sky like silver.

What matters wealth or poverty?
No depth or distance—
It falls evenly everywhere.

No speck of dust stains its flakes,
Silent as it falls, unseen.

The rivers and sky grow still,
Revealing the universe’s brilliance—
All things renewed.

It makes one suddenly rejoice,
Like a silver river flowing clear.

When gathered, it spreads like jade across the earth,
When scattered, no trace remains—
No form, no shadow, no sound.

This is the true work of Heaven’s mystery,
Not the hollow craft of mortals.

As the cold fades,
Waiting for the Three Yang’s full measure,
Spring renews itself.

**Tenth [Verse]**
From ancient times, wise and foolish alike—
The wheel of sun and moon drives them all
To sink into the underworld.

「The Han-era Zhang Chen Yi severed his Daoist path,
His mouth for fame and gain,
Indulging in extravagance and luxury,
Only to destroy his own home.

Tombs and ancestral halls by the riverside,
Han graves beside the fields—
All their power fades to nothingness.

Heroes of old,
All speak of leaning against ruined tombs,
Grasses stretching endlessly.

Ah, the past is truly pitiful!
Stained by hollow illusions, fleeting as blossoms carried by the flowing river.

Yet how much better to awaken now—
To abandon worldly toil and vain desires,
To dwell in simplicity and refine the *elixir field* (丹田).

Beyond the wheel of rebirth (輪回),
Ascending the sea of suffering (苦海),
Boarding the ship of *cool wisdom* (般若) straight to its tranquil shore (逍遥岸).

There, one meets the mysterious cloud paths,
Together visiting the *Peach Blossom Source* (桃源).
---

**Eleventh [Verse]**
What joy there is in aimlessness!
Fame and gain are trifles—
When will they ever end?

Counting wealth and splendor,
High rank and noble status,
Beautiful wives and daughters—
Would they ever practice *sustained cultivation* (持修)?

Cold to the *mystic gates* (玄門),
Clear to the *wondrous Dao* (妙道),
Bitter and harsh—who would linger on this path?

The path of cultivation (修行路),
Awakening to rebirth and death (輪回生死),
Shares the fate of the *transcendent ones* (仙流).

Beyond the body, all is idle sorrow.
Sever all grudges and resentments—then rest.

A plain cap of coarse cloth,
Living in harmony with green—
Adrift in clouds and waters,
Roaming the realm beyond things.

Wrapped in leisure, seeking more leisure,
Diminishing loss upon loss,
Extinguishing the fire, dispersing the smoke—no further craving.

When returning home,
This path to the *Netherworld* (酆都) will change,
Into the *Pine Isle* (蓬島) and *Yan Zhou* (瀛洲).
---

**Twelfth [Verse]**
The supreme *Dragon Spring tea* (龍團),
Crafted in subtle refinement,
From *Jianxi’s* distant trails.

Once gathered from the southern mountains,
Moon-brewed fat and crow’s blood,
Blended with the northern seas,
Seven treasures of numinous sprouts.

When spring’s warmth arrives,
It’s stored in hidden chambers,
Ground and pounded into fragrant dust—
Fine water is added.

Within the jade cup,
By the skill of *celestial boys* (仙童),
A golden flower is brewed.

This marvelous tea is fit for the *transcendent* (仙家).
Yet after savoring its aroma,
Only two armpits remain.»

「Fortunate indeed to find the *Daoist* (赵州) of Zhao Zhou,
Yet Lu Zang is nowhere to be seen—
Sweetness in the midst of bitterness,
Whose taste could one boast of?

Purge away all mundane thoughts,
Open the eyes of the *Way* (道),
Returning youth to aged brows—black as crows.

The divine marvels,
May all people understand their drinking,
Together partaking in mist and clouds.

**Thirteenth [Verse]**
From ancient times, the *transcendents* (神仙) have hidden their traces in Zhongnan,
Their teachings passed down through countless generations.
□ said on the *Sutra* (经) platform,
That with a needle, he revived the withered trees,
And beneath the *elixir furnace* (炼丹炉),
He transformed the maiden into the Stone Spring.

The Four Worthies of Shang Mountain,
The Ten Elders of the Ancient Cave,
Yin Xi listened closely to the *Scriptures of Virtue and the Way* (道德篇).

At the hermitage where they dwelled,
A green ox struck the doorpost,
A white deer ascended to the heavens.
The sacred sites of the *Immortal Sage* (栩圣) remain untouched.

The snow-like trinity was fully painted in three days.
There was Yuan Zhen of Wen Jian,
A dream beneath pine shade,
Zhongli coming to enlightenment,
And the *Golden Immortals* (金仙) riding cranes.

The Second Patriarch wore a coarse hide,
Guiding disciples at the *Sweet River* (甘河),
Transmitting the *Seven-Lotus Sutra* (七朵莲) of Chongyang.

The *Complete Perfection School* (全真教),
A *Cave Heaven* (洞天) of blessed land,
The precursor of the *Celestial Sovereign* (象帝).

**Fourteenth [Verse]**
The *Fire Hall* (火院) binds one in endless cycles,
Night departs, day returns—
No respite in the morning or the evening.»

「Today one knows not the morrow’s affairs—
Busy, cycle upon cycle, in endless striving,
Grieving yet still coveting.

Like a wind-lit lamp, man is fleeting,
Grass-tip dewdrops vanish with the dawn—
I see only sorrow’s tears flowing.

Not enduring long, like fire bursting from stone,
Or scum floating on water’s surface.
*"Cease, cease,"* the call to turn back soon.

Hook the past’s frivolities in a single stroke.
Plain robes and simple fare, let life’s currents pass—
Let others laugh, I care not who.

When death’s limit arrives,
Rich or poor, no matter—
What cause remains for endless night-and-day fretting?

Hear the young say:
*"Cast aside family ties, roam the seas like clouds!"*

**Fifteenth [Verse]**
*True Unity* (真一) endures eternally,
*Great Emptiness* (太虚) and essence one—
The wondrous gate opens by itself.

Since the *Mixed Origin* (混元) first began,
The *Two Principles* (两仪) set their stage,
Returning to the root, reclaiming vital breath—
All depends on the *Soul’s Platform* (灵台).

Vast *qi* (浩气) surges open,
*Valley Spirit* (谷神) merges with transformation—
A single spark of luminous essence arises in the boundless void.

Where concentration gathers,
Listen to the dragon’s roar and tiger’s cry,
The earth-shaking winds and thunderous *dharma* (雷).

Ah, the marvel of this wondrous Dao—
Unfathomable, yet it dissolves the foolish into great talent.

*"Now I speak it plain to you—*
Clear as a pearl held in the shell,
Or an autumn hare cradling its moon.

A man of bold resolve,
Once a noble of his age—
Do not let the world’s dust sully your mind and body.

When deeds are done,
Ascend to the *Purple Palace* (紫府),
Ranked among the *Immortal Stages* (仙阶)."

**Sixteenth [Verse]**
To become a *Divine Immortal* (神仙),
The alchemical labor—what difficulty is there?
Where lightning’s voice resounds,
*"[Unclear] [Unclear] [Unclear],"*—
The jade furnace blazes, the clay cauldron smokes cold.

Fair maidens ride dragons,
Golden elders cross tigers—
In a single breath, the Great Return is sealed.

Within the *Elixir Field* (丹田),
There is a white goose, one in number,
Flying into the mud pellet.

The *River Vehicle* (河车) ascends to *Kun Mountain* (昆山),
Not a hair moved—passing this critical juncture.

Seizing tortoise, serpent, and hare,
Alive and bound—
Sudden cloud and rain, one moment’s work,
A single spark yields the elixir.

White snow drifts across the heavens,
Yellow sprouts fill the earth—
Taking this *knife-elixir* (刀圭), one’s youth is ever renewed.

Constantly nourished,
It strips away the old and refines the bones—
The body soars among the clouds.

**Seventeenth [Verse]**
Great Wisdom, boundless ease—
Unfettered, free as the wild.

Housing refined aspirations and quiet joys,
Between pine and stone,
Singing deep until intoxicated,
Beneath moon and wind.

Jade maidens play their *sheng* (笙),
Golden boys dance with sleeves unfurled—
Guiding my *Original Qi* (元炁) into the *Great Mysterious* (太玄).

Within the Mysterious,
All logic drowns in vastness—
Coming and going, endless threads.

Ah, the marvel of these strange scenes—
Beyond mortal ken, a *Cave Heaven* (洞天) in itself.

*"[Unclear], standing firm and thick with virtue—*
Grinding years away,
While others mock my lightness—
The sea shall turn to mulberry fields.*

*Divine Qi* (神炁) surges in harmony,
Yin and Yang rise and fall—
Already I claim the *Free-and-Easy Immortals* (逍遥陆地仙) of earth.

No affliction—
Let my heart open, my brush run wild,
To inscribe these scriptures.»

**Eighteenth [Verse]**
*Venerable Master Feng* (冯尊师)
Boundless *Dharma-Voice* (威音) of ages past,
The moment of sudden enlightenment—
No need for external aid.

Let it rise, wild and unrestrained,
To the farthest reaches of earth and sea,
Idle clouds and forest cranes—
What care for the passing years?

Beneath moon and wind,
Free and easy, self-sufficient—
When inspired, sing high; when weary, sleep.

Where turning back begins,
Falling petals and drifting fluff,
Distant waters and light mist.

Originally, there is no teaching, no transmission.
The Dao is but a forced name—what true *Chan* (禅) is there?

These peach blossoms and willow greens,
Naturally fade and renew—
Why twist and strain,
Or strike bamboo and pluck lotus?

The Great *Dharma-Body* (相) is formless,
True *Emptiness* (空) is not a thing—
What thread of difference between the *Dharma-Realm* (法) and the *Great Thousand* (千)?

The stone lion dares not speak falsehoods,
Or prattle of earth and heaven.
Saying the *Dharma* (地), speaking of the *Heaven* (天).»

**Nineteenth [Verse]**
From ancient times to now,
A single *kshana* (剎那)—
Already a hundred years have passed.

Let *Stone Chong* (石崇) be rich and noble,
Or *Chen Ping* (陈平) poor and lowly,
*Yan Hui* (颜回) die young,
Or *Zhi* (跖) live long.

New paths and old graves,
All filled with countless fools and sages alike.
None see the
Twelve golden hairpins,
Or three thousand jade shoes.

Only because they failed to refine the *Returning Elixir* (还丹).
Each remains an ordinary man, with no predestined fate.

*"[Unclear], before the courtyard’s stubborn stone—*
It still could hear the *Dharma*,
The old tree by the city wall—
It yet understood the way to transcendence.

A jug of wine, a scroll of verse,
A zither played, a sword unsheathed—
All ties with mortal joys dissolved.

When asked, *"How is the Dao?"*
I point to the blue sky.

The candle’s shadow sways red,
Golden chrysanthemums bloom anew,
The jade hare’s glow swells bright in heaven’s clarity.
The *Chongyang* (重阳) feast’s splendor now unfurls—
A round mirror gleams.

At the *Central Upper Realm* (上界中央),
The *Willow of the Nine Boundaries* (桂花鲜) stands tall—
Clouds gather at the eight horizons.

Twisting green branches,
A white moon clusters—
Within, what mysteries unfold.

Countless fragrant herbs,
Hidden blossoms in the *Cave Heaven’s* (洞天) secluded gardens—
How many are there?

The high terrace at midnight,
Most worthy of contemplation—
Encountering *Perfect Clarity* (圆明), one’s insight is complete.

The wind stirs fragrant clouds,
Silvered mist and luminous pools intertwine.
A single cluster of frost,
An ancient wheel of ice—
Who knows their harmonious blend?

---
**Lyrics to *Lingjiang Xian* (临江仙)**
*"A Daoist of Free-and-Easy Ease"* (达道逍遥无事客),
Singing wildly through the day, joyous.
A lone nature, clear and true.

Like the *Three Isles’* (三岛) moon,
Or the *Nine Heavens’* (九霄) idle clouds.
Words and dreams beyond mortal reckoning,
The heart bears no dust of the world.

The four seasons’ flowers, all embraced in play.
A *Heaven in a Jug* (壶中天) knows no night,
The *World Beyond Things* (物外景) blooms eternal spring.

---
**Lyrics to *Yingchui Xu* (莺啼序)**
*"[Unclear]*

---
**Lyrics to *Lü Dongbin* (吕洞宾)**
The *Three Peaks* (三峰) path is treacherous,
Snow covers the cliffs, auspicious vapors rise.
By the ravine, hear
Dragon’s roar and tiger’s cry,
Lightning’s flash and stars’ brilliance—
A sudden crimson glow, ghosts and spirits flee in terror.

Lead condenses, mercury solidifies,
Nurtured in the furnace—
The elixir marks even the rubble.

A treasure supreme,
Yet fools consume but a single grain—
Extending life’s span.

How much more when there are
A million *Divine Pearls* (神珠),
Flowing *Celestial Dew* (霞) dazzling—
All threaded through the palace’s robes.

---
*[Note: The following annotations were inferred from the original text’s context and should be applied where needed in future translations:]*
- *三峰* (Three Peaks) likely refers to a Daoist mountain or sacred site.
- *神珠* (Divine Pearls) and *流霞* (Celestial Dew) are alchemical terms for refined elixirs.
- *壶中天* (Heaven in a Jug) and *物外景* (World Beyond Things) are poetic expressions of Daoist transcendence.
- *莺啼序* (Yingchui Xu) is a word tune name, likely corresponding to a specific *ci* (词) structure.

**First Verse:**
*"Original title misnamed. #4 Unsigned in the original; *Complete Song of the Song Dynasty* attributes it to Ge Changeng. #5 The *ci* title is incorrect, inconsistent with the *qupu* [word-tune structure].
**Wuhè Yúyīn Juàn** [The Echo of the Crane’s Cry, Volume Four]
*Collected by Daoist Peng Zhizhong of Xiányóu Mountain*
**Sūmùzhē** [Veiled Screen]
*By Master Mǎ Dānyáng*

The Upper *Dantian*, the Path of Primordial Void.
Jade seals the Golden Gate—
Eight-Trigram pearls curtain the treasury.
Left, the Azure Dragon; right, the White Tiger.
In emerald robes, the Hu [Barbarian] monk—
This is the soil of the Three Pure Ones.

Tiger subdued, Dragon subdued—
Battle the Three Corpses, claim the River-Chariot’s way.
Tether the wild horse, the monkey-mind—
Lift the elixir to Kunlun’s peak,
Pierce into the *Níwán* [Brain of Perfection].

---
**Second Verse:**
The Middle *Dantian*—
Wondrous depths.
In the Treasure-Gathering Pool,
Five-hued *Celestial Dew* radiant.
The *Zhēnü* [Immortal Maiden] and infant laugh with joy.
Refined into Golden Elixir—
Worth ten thousand myriads.
Ingest but one grain—
Fragrant, wondrous.
Bone-transmutation, embryo-drawing—
All maladies vanish.
Turn back to youth, reborn in vigor.
Adrift in bliss, leaning on dawn’s rocky stream.

---
**Third Verse:**
The Lower *Dantian*—
The Dao of the Illumined Sage.

**Fourth Verse:**
The *Niu* [Ox] does not graze on common grass—
Jade nectar pools, its taste divine.
White snow, yellow sprouts—
Feed the Ox, and it grows fat.
Golden dragon’s head, silver coils entwined,
Luminous, dustless, like snow spread wide.
Wagging tail, shaking head, roaring loud—
Crossing seas, surging rivers, ascending Penglai Isle.

**Fifth Verse:**
Brightly radiant—*zìjīng* [essence], *qì*, and spirit—
Must be cherished, preserved with care.
A single grain of Golden Elixir,
Sold on every street for forty years—
No one buys.
Amidst the blooming flowers, the debt of love is repaid.
The *jiǔsān yáo* [hexagram 93]—*Dìtiān Tài* [Earth-Heaven Harmony].
The Golden Crow ascends, flying into the Silver Hare’s realm.
A hundred-foot pole—just one step more.
These efforts—let others vie in vain.

**Sixth Verse:**
Ah, the human body—like a puppet marionette,
Adorned in five colors, all deceit and illusion.
Arms crossed, standing at the stage’s edge, discussing past and present,
Calling to one another, dancing vainly before the crowd.
When it comes, like wind and rain.
When the breath is spent, the seven *pò* [spirits] and three *hún* [souls] depart.
Though you beat the painted drums before the stage,
You cannot call it back—no return path remains.

---
**[Southern Tune] *Shēng Cházǐ* #1**
Last night, a sudden longing arose—
Behold, a few moths fluttering near the lamps, worthy of lament.
Love, desire, greed, and anger refuse to let go—
Mistaking lamp-light for the sky’s ascent and descent.
Before the flames, they caper wildly,
Yet fear not the burning—
Until they turn to ash within the lamp.
Then—no more. No more. No more.
I urge you, all—heed my warning:
Do not, like moths, cling to love’s illusion.
Love’s embrace ages you—
Wrinkled face, white hair, hunched back, bowed head,
Deaf ears, dim eyes.
Seek no return—sever past pleasures with a single stroke.
While the body thrives, act with clarity and boldness.
Leap free from the mortal cage—
Then all is resolved.

---
**Dissolving Knots of Grudge** *[Chóu Jié]*
North and South—each a day,
East and West—each a day,
Together, the four directions share the sun.
In dreams, deep and drifting,
The passing of days comes and goes.
Await the day when the Dao-heart opens.
A hundred years—brief as a glance—
All are but fleeting days.
Push them aside, this morning and tomorrow.
Unaware of pushing, the day of saintly news arrives.
The Celestial Cavern opens—
That is the day I return.

---
**Second [Section]**
Mountains and rivers now at peace,
No more war—*Tàipíng* times, eight directions harmonized.
Frequent fasts and offerings,
Repaying the boundless heavens and earth.
Thanking the hidden kindness of the *Hong* [Great] Benevolence.
A thousand years—once in a lifetime—
Divine ones descend into the world.
Fortunate to meet them—do not treat lightly.
Strict and precise offerings,
Each year surpassing the last.
On auspicious days, all indulge in joy.
The *yīng* [swallow] flies south—
A joyous migration.

**First [Section]**
Death and life—both are feared.
This wheel of rebirth, selling bones—
How can it ever cease?
Unenlightened to the True Constant,
Forcing growth of branches and nodes,
The nature of life and death remains unpenetrated.
Within existence, yet failing to grasp—
Beyond existence, yet no containment—
Difficult to discern true from false.
Abandoning all dharma.
This original single point—
Where shall it be anchored?
Dare I ask such words?
Cultivating the True, nurturing the nature—
How can one cling to it with fixation?
What is the utmost clarity of mind,
What is the true seeing of nature,
What is the utter detachment from all ties?
What is the clarity of moon and wind,
What is the luminous, unencumbered freedom?
Realizing the True Law.
I beg my revered teacher’s compassion,
To guide and awaken me.

**Second [Section]**
Death and life—no longer feared.
With the fierce wind’s single sweep,
All is done away with.
Revealing only the True Constant,
No growth of branches and nodes,
The nature of life and death has no high or low.
No inner or outer—
Within it is contained—
Originally, no true or false.
Illuminating all dharma.
This True Suchness point—
No need for anchoring.
Awakening to the word of no birth.
Non-doing, non-action—
The Great Dao holds no fixation.
Six-two clarity of mind,
Ever-present seeing of nature,
Only this—detachment from all ties.
Everywhere, moon and wind’s clarity,
Truly luminous, unencumbered freedom.
Realizing the True Law.
True emptiness, self-liberated,
Neither born nor transformed.

---
**Third [Section]**
The Great Dao is formless—
How then does the heart’s measure rely on it?
It lies within all people,
Yet wisdom’s insight is bright and clear.
Able to subdue all desires,
To sever entangled emotions.
Being at ease in the midst of chaos,
Calm in the midst of busyness,
Pure in the midst of filth.
A demeanor like that of an infant,
A heart as cold as ice.
From the very fog of ignorance,
Awakening breaks through the path ahead.
My words are a blessing—
Listen deeply, my friend.
Ten parts of effort,
Ten parts of resolve,
Ten parts of sincerity.

**Second [Section]**
The Great Dao is formless—
How then does the heart’s measure rely on it?
It lies within all people,
Yet wisdom’s insight is bright and clear.
Able to subdue all desires,
To sever entangled emotions.
Being at ease in the midst of chaos,
Calm in the midst of busyness,
Pure in the midst of filth.
A demeanor like that of an infant,
A heart as cold as ice.
From the very fog of ignorance,
Awakening breaks through the path ahead.

The heart’s desires dissolve and vanish,
Detached from the roots of dust and defilement.
Joy in emptiness—
Serene and refined, revering the True.

Form like a wild crane,
Nature akin to lone clouds.
Wherever one arrives, home is found,
Wind as companion, moon as neighbor.

Dwelling in the world without attachment,
Exceeding common customs with transcendence.
Seizing the profound mystery—
Lo, lo, lo!□
A single thought’s reflection,□
Ever fresh in countenance.

Attaining the True’s supreme power,
Perfecting the True’s conduct,
Serving the True Sovereign.□

**Ballad of the Jade Emperor’s Consort**
Sitting in meditation, speaking of Dao and dharma afterward,
Rising, yet not clinging to the slightest trace.
The heart seeks its own musings,
Loves to be dull and foolish.
Daily life’s myriad mechanisms—
How often has one extinguished even a single one?
To crave divinity as an immortal,
How difficult it is by heaven’s decree!

**Second [Section]**
Pursuing the Dao requires a single resolve,
Without resolve, escape from life and death is hard.
Facing all phenomena, resolve stands firm as a mountain,
Naturally at ease.
All dharmas do not depart from purity and stillness,
Only when the mind is settled can one grasp the True Self.
Understanding this profound emptiness,
The Dao must be traversed.

**Autumn Dawn at the Congealing Horn**
Floating life, restless and hurried,
All worldly desires swept away.
In vain do you struggle for livelihood,
Drowned in the ocean of attachment.
Mocking the clever and cunning,
Competing for wealth and honor in dreams.
Even with countless honors and riches,
Who cares for the swift passage of time?

**Second [Section]**
Worldly affairs press on—
Do not weary your heart with ceaseless toil.
Abandoning dust, return early to the forest’s shade,
Covering yourself with a humble thatched hut.
Reflected in the window, sparse bamboo,
A rustling wind stirs jade-like clarity.
Endless green hills as friends,
Heedless of the fields’ rise and fall.
The petals scatter across the path,□

**The Fisherman’s Song [by Lü Dongbin]**
The west wind blows through the Wei River,
Fallen leaves fill Chang’an.
Busy in the dusty world,
Yet alone in serene leisure.

Naturally the furnace and cauldron,
Tigers circle and dragons coil.
Ninefold elixir refined,
A single pill of sharp efficacy—
Feeding it, one becomes a god of mortal lands,
A thousand needles, a priceless belt of marten fur and phoenix feathers.
Riches and glory seek to intoxicate the heavens.
The yellow grains are still unripe,
The dream shatters, leaving only remnants.
In the sea of contention,
Standing firm in the True Dao is hard.
With a sweep of the sleeve, I depart to the south,
White reeds and red willows,
Revisiting the hermitage at Pu Mountain.

**Mountain Stream**
Better to return than to stay,
Becoming a man of tranquil ease.
What need is there to provoke,
Others’ endless troubles and strife?
Heaven’s vast allowance—
Where cannot one take shelter?
Let me just wander,
With a life of means,
Testing thoughts to see.

In the mirror of the lake,
Shallow hills by the forest’s edge.
Dwelling in a small hermitage,
Living by fate’s modest share—
Coarse robes, simple fare.
Mocking the wind, praising the moon,
Carefree beyond all mortal years.
Worldly affairs,
All like hemp—
Who can I blame?

**Wandering Drifter**
Between emerald bamboo, verdant pine,
Layered shadows deep.
The Daoist’s pavilion in clouds of white.
Across the shore, red dust cannot reach,
Water soaks the cold void.
This scene matches that of the **Qiao** hermit,
The sage of the cave’s entrance.
After plucking the zither, he overturns the golden incense burner.
Laughing defiantly at mist and haze, he has no cares,
Beneath the bright moon and pure wind.

**Second [Section]**

---

**The Third [Section]**
**A Master of the Dao**

A lone master dwells within the **Ling Palace**,
Formless, shadowless, and without trace.
Iron eyes and bronze gazes fail to perceive him—
His body seems the very void.

He neither breathes nor lets the wind pass through,
Nor can earth and heaven contain him.
Yet I have captured him within my **medicine tripod**,
Stirring the **Three Heavens Sanhui Fire** to refine his true essence.

**The Fifth [Section] of the Second [Poem]**
**Lu Dongbin**

I have a house of three rooms,
Deep within the mountain’s embrace.
No walls nor gates to bar the four sides,
The myriad forms of the world as my **purlins and brackets**,
The sky my roof of azure tiles.

For decades, it leaks not a drop—
All part of my past destiny.
When my merit and practice reach three thousand,
I shall command the **living dragon** and subdue the **tiger**,
Only then shall I be counted among the **Immortal Ones**.

**Eternal Happiness**

Busy yet stealing leisure,
Amidst the clamor, finding stillness—
Let fame and gain no longer vie.
Limited time, endless dusty affairs—
When shall my cravings cease?

The heartless **crow and hare** hasten my aging,
Stealthily turning my green locks to gray.
This body, this form—
A fleeting union of illusion.
What proof can there be of its permanence?

Living as fate dictates,
Harmonizing with the world’s dust,
What idle sorrow or vexation could I endure?
Wealth and glory come from heaven,
Honor and splendor are my destiny—
Do not trouble your mind with schemes.

When the heart is free of cares,
And all before you is clear,
Then all is joy—this moment’s true landscape.
If you seek such perfect contentment,
Patience will reveal its path.

**Crossing the Golden Crane**

**Niu Zhenren**

At the **Jade Hall of the Dawn**,
The **Daoist Immortals** gather at their **feast of the immortals**.
On auspicious days,
Fragrant incense burns together,
Releasing **auspicious mists** and **lucky vapors**.

Celebrating the **Three True Ones** and the **Five Ancestors of the Double Ninth Festival**,
I pray that the **Holy Sovereign** may endure forever.
In ancient times, there was **Xuanyuan**,
Riding the dragon, soaring aloft,
To the **Jade Emperor’s court**, where he strove to lead.
Then all **Ten Thousand Saints** assembled,
Feasting and lingering in divine revelry.

The **celestial music** resounds,
**Golden Boys** bear the cups,
**Jade Girls** deliver the decrees.
At the **Palace of the Gods** and the **Immortal Gardens**,
Strange and wondrous scenes unfold—
**Cranes and phoenixes descend**, while **cranes dance** in graceful flight.
The **Immortal Boys** announce:
The **Peach of Immortality** is now ripe,
And the **Cinnabar Osmanthus** has blossomed.
For ten thousand years, the **Golden Tortoise** bears witness,
A thousand autumns, the **Jade Hare** remains—
When the **Old Man Star** appears,
All these wonders are celebrated.
The **Caverns of the Immortals** surpass mortal joys—
No coming or going,
Heaven and earth share his lifespan,
Sun and moon his years.

**Treading the Dew**

A **hempen robe** to wear,
A **paper quilt** to sleep.
My **gourd staff** is all the baggage I need.
With three cups and two bowls,
I find pure joy in heaven’s way—
Who could argue with my ease?

All around, the **common folk** scramble for fame and profit,
Each morning scheming to fill their bellies.
Let them eat **earthen dumplings**—
Only then will they know the taste of **plain fare**.

**The Wild Horse Blooms with One Branch of Flowers**
After the rain, the **mountain flowers** burst into bloom.

**Mist Disperses, Clouds Retreat to the Celestial River**
In tranquil seclusion, I wander where peace is pure.
Before the ancient cave’s rocks,
I often refine the **Golden Elixir**.

I care not for riding fat steeds,
Nor wealth and honor’s fleeting fame,
Nor the tangles of right and wrong.
Alone in my thatched study, I pore over ancient texts,
Turning the **Dao Classics** again and again.
Strumming my **horizontal zither** on my knee,
A crane arrives to greet me.

Though **purple sashes** and **golden seals** mark high office,
They are what they are—
Yet even then, at dawn’s fifth watch, the rush to mount,
How could it compare to my **Daoist life**,
When at noon my gate still stands closed?

**Spring Exploration Order**
At the **Grass Hall’s** third watch, I dream of soaring—
To **Penglai’s** halls and **Kunlun’s** gardens.
Where white clouds blanket the earth, untouched by broom,
Truly a hidden grove—
Fragrant winds swirl endlessly.
The **Celestial Worthies** gather in the **Golden Hall**,
Drinking **Liquid Immortality** in revelry.
Suddenly, a wave of cool clarity washes over me,
Like moonlight seen atop a mountain.

**Yellow Crane Cave Immortal (with *Wild Horse*)**
**Master Ma Dan-yang**
All day, I drive the **salt cart**,
Whip and rod striking again and again.
I count my spirit long bent and weary,
Like a sickly horse.
How could I ever find ease?
When **Master Beryle** arrives,
He sighs deeply upon seeing me.
With clever schemes, I redeem my life,
Becoming a **noble steed**.
I must repay my teacher’s kindness.

**Dreamless Order (Two Poems)**
Awakening suddenly, a hundred years pass like a finger-snap—
Tears burst forth like scattered pearls.
I rush to dissolve the sorrow of life and death,
Why fret over **fire in the stone**?
Let the **fire in the stone** rage—
Let all collapse beneath the earth.
Learning the **Dao** is neither hard nor easy—
How dare I stop when I have not yet begun?
I focus on **mortifying the physical self**,
Until I grasp the art of **eternal life**.
**Eternal life’s secret**—
Gathering **qi** and spirit bright.

**Willow Leaf Green**
A **hemp robe**, straw sandals—
I’ve wandered the world’s markets,
Mingling with clouds and morning mists.
Whatever fate brings, I take it in stride,
My staff bearing **Yi Jing** and **Zhuangzi**.
When guests ask of mortal affairs,
I point to falling blossoms in silence.
Refining my **water-and-cloud** nature,
I tread wherever home may be.

**Plucking a Single Plum Blossom**
A **rough linen robe**, loose and wide,
A **carefree bearing**, sleeves fluttering free.
My **water-and-cloud** tasks keep me company with fishermen and woodcutters.
Let tonight pass as it will—
Ask not of tomorrow.

**Nine-Noded Azure Dragon’s Staff**
A single staff—nine joints, the **Daoist Dragon** borne aloft.
**Daoist scriptures** in handfuls, slung across my shoulders.
A tiny **elixir field** dangling at my waist—
In motion, boundless ease; at rest, boundless ease.

**Drunk in the Taoist Paradise**
No need to speak of its origin—no words at all.
Serene and still, profound and tranquil.
Tranquil and still, ever **lethal qi** complete.
Within, I observe the **Mystic Dao**.
Dao’s subtlety, subtlety’s Dao—
No form to grasp, no roundness to seek.
Come and go as I please—
Who can bar my way?
Before **clear winds and bright moons**.

**The Female Daoist’s Song**

**Ma Dan Yang**
Human life is fleeting—see the **blue-green clouds**,
Rain passing over **mountains and waters**.
Youth’s bloom has faded—centuries like a dream,
Like **Xīyī**’s forgotten name.
Cast off all **emotional attachments**, sever all **affections**;
Tame the **wandering thoughts** and **monkey-mind** with iron resolve.
Endless and intricate—
Like breath exhaled, never certain to be inhaled.
Ten years’ effort, yet still the **Daoist Path**’s essence unfolds.
To become a **true immortal**—never a misstep.
Disciples, hold no doubt.
If any lie or deception lingers,
**Ma Wind’s punishment** will make you a **ghost of Yīnshān**.

**Mind and Action Ever Clear**
Through all **Ten Directions**, I perceive **Heaven and Earth**.
With **meritorious deeds** accumulated,
The **Golden Boy** will come to claim you.

**Returning to the Morning’s Joy**
Where did I lodge when **Heaven and Earth** first split?
No **parents of birth**, what name did I bear?
This truth must be made clear—
Probe its depths, let no argument arise.
Transmit the **unutterable** with precision,
And past lives may be fully examined.
Frequent comings and goings—
Lost in confusion, when shall I receive **enlightenment’s grace**?
Suddenly, before the **True Spirit**,
The **formless vision** is joyously revealed.
Awake and aware—what stern **Daoist principle** do I behold?
Radiant and reflected, all is **ease**—*Yìjīng*’s **#6**.
When seen, only the **subtle Dao’s essence** is sought,
A lofty depth that shines with **perfect light**,
Five **auspicious hues**—all signs of **fortune’s return**.

**The Six-Miao Melody**

**Wang Zhongyang**
**True purity, true stillness**—
This is the **harmony of Tiger and Dragon**.
Clear and profound—
**Innocent child** and **maiden** rise naturally.
**Silent meditation** is the **root of the Dao**,
**Fast and abstinence** shift **East and West**.
At the **twelve critical moments** of time,
Ever **mindful and aware**,
Within, refine **qi and spirit**—**jade furnace**’s ** Daoist practice**.
Why seek **branches to pluck** or **leaves to gather**?
What need to discuss the **elixir scriptures**?
My **Dao’s profound subtlety**—
Know **laziness and decline**, yet still **emptiness** prevails.
Banish **sleep, speech, and desire**,
Diminish **food and drink**—**fusion**’s the aim.
**External frugality**, **thin human ties**,
Break **thoughts**—**gradual enlightenment** opens wide.

**The New Cool’s Praise**

**Chen Yizhi**
A full cup—**heart-opening wine**.
Count **life’s discontents**—
Nine out of ten.
**Nature’s child** plays tricks—
Upside down, then right again.
I’ve only **chased dust** in vain.
When **sages are satisfied**, let **fools speak**.

**Red Peony**
**Wang Tongsu**
A hundred years of life—
seventy is rare.
Subtract ten years for childhood’s care,
another ten for age’s decay.
Fifty years remain—
half stolen by slumber’s sway.
Within those twenty-five,
are troubles not to be denied?
Reflect well, then—
pursue joy while time allows.
With wine and friends, laugh boldly,
let jade cups crash and shatter.
Drink deep, drink long—
life’s like dew on morning grass.
Fortunate now, with wine like Mian’s,
to weave songs for ages yet to pass.

**Praise for New Peace**
**Hua Danyang**
**Wang Chongyang**
Limited flesh, boundless fire’s hall—
time’s swift blade presses on.
Man’s life, like a candle in the wind,
all day’s rush, all night’s alarm.
The foolish, lost in endless schemes,
bound by family’s chains.
Loving sons, pitying wives—
tyrants who ensnare the soul.
Awaken, break free—
sever name’s bonds, topple love’s mountain.
Leap from passion’s sea,
unfettered, Dao’s bliss unfolds—
half a sheet, one lute.
Rest on the couch, but tether not the mind,
lest strife disturb the heart.
When wisdom’s sword is drawn,
demons fall, gods stand still.
Qi’s union—dragons race, tigers bound,
golden rooster, jade hare greet the dawn.
Enter the jade furnace, gold cauldron’s glow,
refine the sun-spirit, rise to Heaven’s court.
This lineage’s purity—
ice-clear, jade-white—
nods thanks to kindred souls.
To achieve true harmony’s prize,
worth more than gold.

**The Grand Minister’s Air**
**Tan Zhenren**
Neither monk nor layman, nor immortal sage—
a thatched hut, two or three beams.
White stone, clear spring—
who seeks the Peach Blossom’s hidden realm?
One furnace’s talismans,
one cup of spring’s snow,
to nourish the three pure fields.
Lost in thought on *Gu Shen’s* verse,
unaware the moon rounds the pine.

「其二
Time and tide fly swift, never stay,
Spring fades and autumn comes again.
Unfurling the brows from frowns,
Let’s sing in harmony—
**Daoist songs** to dispel cares.
A hundred years, a fleeting glimpse,
Striving for fame and gain,
Only to stir vain, idle woes.
Cease this bitter craving chase,
For if life’s path is crossed,
Let fate’s wind guide you home.

**其三**
A hundred years’ deeds—
in the mirror’s gaze, how frail!
Lament the ancient traveler’s plight,
For life’s road has ever been hard.
Wind and rain age the face,
Who cares for **An Ren’s** white hair’s spread?
Lofty renown, soaring **qi**,
Yet dreams dissolve like willow’s shade.
Turning back to ask the green hills,
They answer with a single cloud—
free, unbound, at ease.

**Green Jade Tablet**
The **Dao of Non-Action** is hard to grasp,
Yet simpler than you think—
Just lack the effort, and you’ll miss.
A sudden awakening brings back the light,
Ever reflecting in your mind.
Within the **Three Pure Fields**,
Among the **Six Palaces**,
Sweep away the dust again and again.
Where all ties are severed, the heart finds peace.
A spark of **empty luminosity** shines forth,
And you’ll know the **Primordial Dao of Pure Stillness**.
Passing through a hundred gates,
Harmony flows clear,
Your true nature bright and whole—
Then you’ll step forth onto the **Immortal’s Isle**.

**其二#８**
Since parting from the **Eastern Capital’s** road,
I’ve dwelled in the **Panshui Temple** by the west,
Where the **Panshui River** winds.

**南山云寂渺**
Gradually knocking at the southern mountain’s silent clouds,
A thatched hut—cool and detached,
Earthly honors cast aside, carefree.
No officials ever come here.
At night, the lanes are quiet, travelers gone—
Suddenly, the rock’s child-cuckoo calls.
*(Its cry pierces the pine branches till dawn.)*
Each note urges: *"Why not return?"*
Yet—how little effort I’ve made.

**贺圣朝**
The grass hut sleeps beneath the morning’s glow,
Blue-robed attendants seal the door,
The crimson-crested bird returns to its nest.
Clutching my jade zither, I dream of the Immortal’s Isle,
Waiting for leisure to seek the Three Teachings.
Midnight sleep—
A sound like jingling armor,
The wind striking the bamboo mat.
Through sparse trees, I gaze at the fading clouds,
Now clinging to the pine’s highest branch.

**解佩令**
All my life, I’ve been dim-witted,
Unknowing of worldly matters.
Eating tea and rice, I forget hunger or fullness.
Sitting, I take root;
Standing, I’m like a stubborn stone in the path.
Let others laugh at my empty pretensions—
I don’t grasp letters or doctrine.
Speaking of practice, I have no words to split.
Dust clings to my face,
My beard wild, my robe patched.
Yet I’ll live forever—
No calamity will age me.

**粉蝶儿**
To recognize the elixir,
Look to your own ancestral root.
No need to count where you began.
Who shaped this mortal frame?
Who kneaded this soul’s clay?
This spark of life—
Originally, lead refined.
Now that you’re human,
You’ve claimed your own dragon-tiger essence.
Yet you still can’t grasp it.
Swallow that single gold elixir,
And you’ll escape the wheel of suffering.

**武陵春**
All things—let them go.
The familiar world fades naturally.
Snatch back the stolen leisure from the bustle,
Carry nothing on your head.
Motion or stillness—no distinction,
The Dharma-realm cannot be confined.
Free beyond things, my nature like a crystal sphere.

**拾菜娘**
*(Qiu Changchun)*
A stubborn heart must fly like the wind—
Drawn into timelessness, no thought of return.

**幸遇明师因晓了，肯教熟境再相随。**
Fortunate to meet the enlightened Master—
Now willing to guide me through the familiar world once more.

**你待东时我却西。**
When you turn east, I turn west.

**我今省悟即从伊。**
Now that I awaken, I follow only Him.

**万劫轮回皆为汝，百般魔障更因谁。**
All eons of rebirth—all for you.
A thousand obstacles—yet who is their cause?

**二郎神 小张歌，也好把、繁华勘破。**
Oh, Second Son of Heaven, Little Zhang’s song—
Even you must see through the vanity of splendor.

**速认元初真面目，把意马心猿牢锁。**
Swiftly recognize your primordial true form,
And bind the restless mind and wandering thoughts.

**百岁光阴能有几，也不可虚过。**
How few are the hundred years of life—
Do not waste them in vain.

**耳却听嘱付，仙风道骨，莫向红尘埋堕。**
Hear the Master’s instructions well:
With Daoist bearing, do not sink into the dust of the world.

**省呵。把师父亲言记着。**
Reflect—remember the Master’s words.

**你原是蓬莱洞裹仙，为思凡、人间沦落。**
You were once an immortal of Penglai’s cave,
Yet fell to mortal longing, lost in the world below.

**速整仙胎归上会，莫荏苒、俗情系缚。**
Swiftly refine your immortal essence and return to the Celestial Gathering—
Do not linger, bound by worldly affections.

**自思忖，假饶积玉堆金，终久幻化如何。**
Consider this: though you hoard jade and gold,
All will dissolve—what then remains?

**青梅引**
*(I smile at those who deceive me, untrusting.)*
**我笑迷人，不信乖劣。**
I laugh at those who lead others astray—
Unbelieving in their deceit.

**痴心恋，贪名利萦击。**
Foolish love, ensnared by fame and gain.

**落魄狂游，每将术艺养道，用安身己。**
Cast off, wandering wildly—
Daily cultivating arts to nourish the Dao,
To secure my own being.

**道知和息。**
The Dao knows peace.

**藜杖药瓢，蓑衣蛮笠。**
With gourd staff and medicine gourd,
In raincoat and straw hat.

**纵大地有满地真珠，那的直甚闲气。**
Though the earth were paved with pearls,
What use is such idle wealth?

**无限峰峦耸翠。**
Endless peaks rise in emerald splendor.

**略撰个茅庵，用做栖心，幸有灵苗裔。**
A humble thatched hut—my dwelling place,
Fortunate to have such a blessed lineage.

**更兼泉水。**
And the spring’s clear waters.

**饥渴自然无碍。**
Hunger and thirst pose no hindrance.

**独坐深山裹。**
Alone in the mountain’s depths.

**闷看乾坤间隔，望落落如晓星之势。**
Gazing at the vast expanse of Heaven and Earth,
Seeing the scattered stars like dawn’s first light.

**再遇何年，驾云朝上帝。**
When next we meet, I shall ride the clouds
To pay homage to the Celestial Sovereign.

**玉胡蝶**
*(The Butterfly of Jade)*
**捉住玉山赤凤，神舟同泛，激浪漂浮。**
Seizing the Crimson Phoenix of Jade Mountain,
Together we ride the divine boat,
Riding waves that surge and drift.

**便使乌龟开口，出头喜谟，吸洪涛、枯乾北海，使巨波、浇灌西湖。**
Even if the Tortoise speaks,
Its joyful words would drain the Northern Sea’s tides,
Pouring vast waves to flood the Western Lake.

**自舒敷。**
Spreading freely.

**水纹花面，此日是金铺。**
Ripples like floral patterns—
Today, the ground is paved with gold.

**光珠。**
Radiant orbs.

**盈盈照耀，恰如明月，晃晃方隅。**
Glowing full, like the bright moon,
Illuminating every corner.

**普徧腾辉，尽成霞彩环纡。**
Universal radiance ascends—
All becomes swirling clouds of crimson hue.

**见圆珠、深深渐见，结宝丹、空外超踰。**
The round elixir pearl appears ever deeper,
The precious elixir formed—transcending the void.

**得临大罗天上，永永惺苏。**
Ascending to the Great Luo Heaven,
Ever awake, forever.

**玉液泉**
*(The Jade Nectar Spring)*
**这消息，几人知，独我全真好。**
This truth—how few know it,
Only I, the True and Complete.

**大悟来，心地清凉，便分晓。**
With Great Awakening, the heart grows cool—
Then all becomes clear.

**本来面目常照。**
The original face shines eternally.

**最玄妙。**
Most wondrous.

**金关开，玉户闭，来往通关窍。**
The Golden Pass opens, the Jade Gate shuts—
Flowing freely through the vital pathways.

**遍三田，觉上下和冲，降银雪，黄芽遍生芝草。**
Through the Three Fields, the upper and lower align,
Descending silver dew—yellow sprouts grow on the elixir herbs.

**姹婴舞跳。**
The maiden dances, vibrant and lively.

**透引动、龙吟虎啸。**
Stirring the Dragon’s roar and Tiger’s cry.

**般运在，斡旋中，坎离颠倒。**
The revolutions turn,
The interplay of yin and yang—
Kan and Li inverted.

**龟蛇战斗，水火抽添，炉内烧丹，结就明珠晃耀。**
The Tortoise and Serpent contend,
Water and fire blend—
Within the furnace, the elixir burns,
Forming a radiant pearl.

**玉皇深恩宣诏。**
The Jade Emperor’s profound grace is proclaimed.

**祥云攒罩。**
Auspicious clouds gather above.

At that time, steady astride the Azure Crane,
Return to Penglai Isle.

**Refining the elixir sand** *(Waves Winnowing Sand)*
**Master Ma Dan-yang**
To walk the Dao, the heart must be unyielding,
Guard the elixir field with vigilance.
Harmonize the true breath, ever flowing.
Within the twelve hours, ever present—
Do not let worldly dust entangle you.
The secret lies in avoiding clamor,
In quietude, find true repose.
Silent speech must be mastered.
When the divine elixir ripens, the Way is fulfilled,
And one ascends to the Celestial Court.

**Pointing at the Crimson Layer** *(Note: "层" likely refers to a Daoist alchemical stage or layer)*
**Master Quan Zhen**
A humble gourd—
Born naturally, wondrous in its simplicity.
Short of stature,
Yet the gourd has a mouth,
Difficult to open, hard to explain.
Recognizing Heaven and Earth—
Who can truly grasp this truth?
A belt at the waist,
The Daoist cherishes it above all,
Not exchanging it for a golden fish pouch.

**Second Verse**
Alas, all seek fame and gain,
Bound in endless cycles of greed.
When will it end?
Only when the eyes fall to the earth,
Do they finally regret.
Though children and grandchildren may follow,
They cannot bear the burden in your stead.
Tears well up—
This bitter taste,
Shatters the heart before it is known.

**Third Verse**
**Master Qiu Chang-chun**
Last night, drunken and dazed,
In intoxication, I seemed to ride the elixir phoenix.
With music and song,
I soared through the Four Heavens,
Awakening to the Peach Blossom Cavern’s depths.
Facing the deep ravine,
I leisurely played with a radiant pearl.
At dawn’s first stir,
A gust of wind carried me away—
The dream of immortality shattered.
The crane’s cry fades into silence.

**Verse (Continuation of *行香子* / *青莲池上客*)**

**Flower-lined paths and rocky peaks**—
The *Zhōnglí* bell tolls.
The Four Great Elements are void of self,
The Five Aggregates are inherently empty.
Cease to vie with others and with self,
Strutting as heroes.
Noble or base, wise or foolish—
All shall meet in the realm of dreams.
A hundred years of kin and loved ones,
Wrapped in crimson light,
Should each be bound in their own fate.

I urge you to diligently refine your practice,
Ever reflecting on the original essence.
When you come, you bring nothing,
When you go, you are void.
Human life is finite,
Yet greed spins endlessly.
Better to live within your allotted measure,
For even a spark of luminous clarity
Naturally yields moonlit breezes and pure winds.

---
**Second Verse (*Jiāngshénzǐ* / *吕洞宾*)**

Rare is the man who lives to seventy years of age.
Alas, the foolish are lost—
They do not cultivate the Dao.
Time is finite,
Yet triumph and failure hinge on right and wrong.
Worldly glory and renown are all seized,
Yet in vain—
For *karmic bonds* follow them.
Temporarily, they are bewitched by wine, song, and wealth,
Gaining but losing in the same breath.
Darkness veils their youthful bloom,
Gradually draining their *qi* and spirit.
With vigor waning and decline creeping,
Who can they blame but themselves?
How then is the Dao?
**Autumn at Qū River**—

This point, ancient and modern, is sought in confusion.
All have their allotment, yet none lack.
All because of mistaken thoughts—
Where attachment clings, there suffering arises.
If one lets go of each and every thing,
What mysteries remain?
Live in accordance with one’s measure and fate,
Uncover the original face—
This must be made clear.
Cold hearth, cold stove,
Facing tigers and dragons in song and cry.
Right before you—this is it.
No need to seek beyond.

No need to ask of gods or Buddhas,
Only shared awakening awareness.

---
**Melon Blossom Tune** — *Qiu Changchun*
Without toil in walking, without weariness in sitting.
Let me wander or rest as I please.
Morning breeze light, evening sky clear.
The Dao’s path unfettered—
South Creek flows level above and below.
East of the creek, fortunate to forget form in friendship,
Bright moon when night wine is poured.
The cup pauses, moonlight pure.
Unfastening my robe, hair unbound,
Joyfully singing of the Way.

---
**Ascending Flower** — *Wu Zhenren*
The restless mind locked away,
Awakening to dust and time’s swift flight—
A hundred years pass in an instant.
Begin practice now—
The original true spirit must dwell here today.
At home in pits and trenches,
First leap free from the self,
Making solitude your host.
Stillness without disturbance.
Wealth, desire, color, wine—
All must be abandoned.
Cutting off all worldly attachments,
Even father, mother, wife, and kin.
Free and unbound,
Fallen into carefree ease,
Recognize the gold and jade wrapped in rags.
The flower’s heart stirs,
Scent filling the air.
Strange light clusters,
Auspicious radiance gleams,
Forming celestial melodies.

---
**Step of the Moon Palace** — *Lü Dongbin*
Kan, Li, Zhen, Dui, and Zi-Wu aligned—
Recognize your own ancestral roots.
Earth-thunder resounds,
Shaking rain from mountain peaks.
Gradually nourishing,
Yellow sprouts break from the soil.
Seizing golden essence, firmly sealed.
Refining the elixir—
Taming dragons and tigers.
If asked who transmits this,
Only say: *My surname is Lü.*

---
**Double Swallows** — *Qiu Changchun*
Spring mist drifts faintly,
Green hills charming, wandering clouds scattered in the void.
Flower-light and stone-moisture reveal
Strange wonders of the immortal realm.
Windows and doors rise a thousand zhang—
All senses revel in wind’s swift joy.
Lifetimes of suffering and dusty passions,
Now boundless and pure—no trace of the mundane.
Worthy of love.
Free and unbound,
Shedding shackles, free of karmic debt.
Wind as companion, ears attuned,
Dao in harmony with crystal heavens.
Endless towering peaks—
All bestowed upon the mountain hall’s teachings.
Thousand-vehicle pearls—
Who can pay the price?

---
**No Worries to Dissolve** — *San Yu Zhenren*
From ancient times to now,
Many sorrows, few joys—
Pure simplicity and peace are rare.
Fortunate to meet sages in the world.
Proclaiming Dao and discussing the *Luòtiān*,
True immortals descending from above.
Ruling all under heaven without toil,
Inner and outer cease war, embrace culture,
Honor the worthy, cherish virtue,
Bringing clear peace and blessings.
How then repay Heaven’s grace?
Wasting fine moments in triviality.
First uphold frugality,
Ensure warmth and fullness—
No greed for fame or gain.
Seek Dao’s mysteries in the Mysterious Gate.
Abandon desires, preserve harmonious *qi*.
Further, let go—
Each thought, each thing—
Only then escape human burdens.

---
**Wooden Lantern Slow** —
Light and pure, my essence refined,
Alone with Heaven in boundless play.
Yet bound in mortal flesh,
Encircled by the Five Phases,
Trapped by the Four Great Elements.
All years spent in delusion, unaware,
Clinging to illusions of sound and color.
The original immortal realm—
So near, yet distant as heaven and earth.
To seek return to the root, restore the origin,
Only the heart must decide.
Silently focus the essence,
Always probing, seeking—
Surely the work will be complete.
Suddenly, emptiness shatters,
All lifetimes’ karmic barriers vanish.
Shaking sleeves, bound for Penglai and Kunlun,
No fear of weak waters without a boat.
At leisure in intoxication,
Leaning against green mountains.
Awake, plucking the jade zither,
Playing *Hèwū* of the Nine Marshes.
Water clear, mountains near,
Serene and free in joy.
I too return to Kunlun’s halls,
Ascend Penglai’s isle.
Thus, for now, dwelling among mortals,
With Creation, wandering the Great Void,
Nurturing form and spirit—
Both perfectly preserved.

---
**Upper Flat Western Tune**
This *wu-chang* (impermanence),
Two characters—most difficult to guard.
When it comes, no place to hide.
No matter old or young,
Poor or rich, virtuous or base.
No matter wife or child,
How can one cling to parents?
Body returns to earth, blood to water,
Soul and breath scatter with the wind.
Look closely—
How could one not grieve?
Do not covet the fire hall,
Early cultivate the heavenly realm.
Three thousand merits fulfilled, bound for Penglai,
Forever in the immortal land.

---
**Second Verse**
The same.

**First Verse**
Summoning the clear breeze, inviting the bright moon—
Come and go, as one pleases.
Reflecting on how much
Idle chatter is idle folly.
Facing mountains, near waters,
Close to pines and bamboo, near plum blossoms.
In the modest courtyard, few daily tasks—
Poetry, wine, the zither, and chess.
No entanglements, no vexations,
No partings.
Awaiting transformation,
Ever in simple foolishness.
Mosquito’s bite, snail’s horn—
Gains and losses—
What more is there to do?
Better to hear the true essence of early joy,
Lying high on the clouded stairs.

---
**Second Verse**
*(Chou Changchun)*
The sun and moon revolve without end.
Spring departs, autumn arrives—
How many flourishings and decays!
Five Emperors, Three Sovereigns, countless ages—
Each rise and fall is thus.
Death and birth, birth and death again.
Endless cycles of change—
When will they cease?
Only when reaching the heartless resting place
Can one attain true stillness beyond all else.

---
**Third Verse**
*(Bai Yuzhen)*
Green fades, red thins—spring is gone.
Swallows carry mud,
Flying into the weeping willows.
Willow fluff lingers, but the wind won’t stop;
Cuckoos cry endlessly through the mountains.
With bamboo staff and straw sandals, no fixed abode.
Fine groves and streams—
Trusting my feet to guide my path.
How much of this heart’s stirrings?
A river’s wind and moon—who rules them?

---
**Fourth Verse**
*(Chou Changchun)*
The golden rooster turns westward to greet the Jade Emperor.
Eastward, the silver hare glows,
Its radiance veiling the green osmanthus.
Gradually, the South Hua gathering of chrysanthemums begins,
Filled with wine from the Northern Sea—drunk, utterly drunk.
Drunkenly reclining in the Zhongnan Mountains’ hues,
Mountain colors pure and high, night unclouded.
Not a crow’s cry—only the wind grows fine,
Moonlight bright as day, sky like water.

---
**Fifth Verse**
A secluded, rugged peak—pure and clear.
Carving jade for dwelling, embracing the Way without knowing or understanding.
Dao companions look at each other—do not be surprised.
Poverty and simplicity, no pretenses.
Wealth, honor, and fame—rely on them?
Many gains are many losses—
Gradually, excess leads to ruin.
Rich feasts and fragrant meats cannot be endured,
But coarse rice and water bring lasting peace.

---
**Sixth Verse**
When fortune comes, rest while you can—
That is rest.
Winning true ease,
Let the hare lead your mind and body.
How many clever and heroic souls
Busy themselves, squandering their lives’ purpose.
Creation shifts without end.
Yesterday’s joy, today’s sorrow.
Today unknown, tomorrow’s fate—
Why weary the mind over such trifles?

---
**Seventh Verse**
Today, I ponder yesterday’s old self.
Knowing my path ahead,
So distant, so hard to cross.
Fortune does not linger, Heaven offers no aid—
Hastening away, no way to stay.
Now, a walking corpse, I’ve awakened.
My spirit drifts—
For now, dwell by the Pan Stream.
To my neighbors, noble and common alike,
Often I am remembered.

---
**Song of the Incense Offering**
A single fly,
Into a bloody basin.
When it tastes the sweetness,
Straight to the heart it goes,
Forgetting to lift itself.
Stained its feet, stained its wings—
Lost its form.
How I sigh—
How could it not move me?
Sweetness hides bitterness,
Fortune breeds disaster.
Once knowing the taste,
Better to withdraw.
You are so blind,
So foolish—
A great, fat fly.

---
**Peony in the Rain**
*(Wang Chongyang)*
How much wine for the Double-Ninth Feast—
Through it, the Dao’s mysteries unfold.
A coarse hemp robe, a blue cloth cap.
Well-made, truly well-made—
A spirit truly refined.

**Song of the Pillow Screen**
No need for mirrors to reflect—
All things are clear within the mind.
In dreams, one recognizes the dream-self.
This is true freedom—
The one who reaches the other shore.

**Boat on the River**
Traversed famous mountains,
All peaks and ridges passed through.
Climbing high slopes,
Ascending steep ridges—
Why weary the spirit?
The Way is within the body,
Yet the mind clings to things,
Entangled, evading.
Never losing
The original self.

Day and night we walk together,
At dusk, we sleep and rest as one.
Till dawn, we follow as before,
Together walking, together seated.
Suddenly—
In an instant—
It becomes clear:
You are my elder brother.

---

**Divination of Fate**
*(Sun Xiangu)*
Firmly grasping robes, awaiting the hour,
Water and fire intertwine.
A million hues of light rise from the ocean’s depths,
Piercing the Three Passes in a single column.
Celestial music plays without cease,
Ever drinking the nectar of enlightenment.
Wondrous elixirs manifest in an instant—
The Nine-Turn Golden Elixir complete.

---

**Joyous Departure**
*(Qiu Changchun)*
To leave birth and death behind.

**First Verse**
Discard all old habits, grinding them down from the start.
A thousand layers of desire—
Body and mind refined a hundred times,
Forged into an iron will of one inch.

Release the Six Spirits, harmonious and unmoved,
The Three Corpses stumble in confusion.
Act with fierce resolve.
Rely on the boundless void,
Unfeeling and undivided.
The knot is bound—
The shackles are cast off.
Only then does one meet the True Person,
Whose golden mouth transmits the subtle secret.
Instantly, the spirit wind blows away the demonic barrier,
The form becomes like carved wood or molded clay.
Having obtained the Nature-Pearl,
The Heavenly Treasure is pierced through—
Spring flowers, autumn moons.
At that time—
Ghosts cannot call out;
Only the Immortals guide and lift.

**Second Verse**
Disgusted with worldly filth,
One takes delight in emptiness and ease,
Making purity a companion.
The sword gleams with cold light,
Weapons rest beneath cloud-generals,
Victorious over the Five Phases’ marauders.
The Cavernous Mysteries’ treasure is secured,
Escaping the shell of yin and yang.
The Great Elixir is complete.
Refining and plucking the sun and moon,
Caressing stars and constellations—
Outstanding and peerless.
Surpassing past and future,
Responding to myriad affairs with manifest divine power.
An iron gate stands firm,
Golden needles and jade threads—
Piercing through seven and eight layers everywhere.
Summoning the embroidered qilin and lions,
Awakening waterfowl and mountain beasts.
Swiftly turning back,
Toward the Azure Peak’s embrace,
Sleeping high in the pure daylight.

**Third Verse**
Do not seek the arcane mysteries.

I have made clear the keys to cultivation—
Fight the enemy of slumber, forget desire and sever thought—
This is the true teaching of sages.

Eat and drink to still doubt,
Diligently cultivate awareness each day.
Do not err.

Wait until there is neither sleep nor waking,
Then the heart aligns with the Dao.

There are profound harmonies and marvels—
Refining qi into spirit yields a golden radiance.
The Five Qi ascend to the Primordial,
The Three Flowers gather at the crown,
Water and fire circulate in reverse.

The Nine Suns coalesce into the Elixir of Return,
Piercing the Soul’s Platform to its eight extremes.
The work is complete.

On the path to longevity, leisurely wandering the Three Isles.

**Fourth Verse**
To regulate true breath—
Discuss the root source, attaining its living reality.
Qi is the heart’s essence,
Spirit governs qi—when the heart stirs, spirit and qi separate.
When the heart is tranquil, yin and yang embrace,
Mind settled, true essence forms naturally.
Do not mistake it.

This inner breath-regulation
Is not about artificial contortions—
Ignorant of the Embryonic Origin’s principle.
Open eyes, nose, and fingers—
The Spirit Tortoise and Serpent play.
Following the Dao’s ancestral tradition,
Returning light to its source,
Breath naturally returns to its root.
A clean breeze suddenly passes through the door,
Water and fire instantly complete their cycle.

At this stage,
True constancy is within arm’s reach—
A Three-Life Buddha manifests in the world.

**Fifth Verse**
Returning to the dusty world,
Break free from entanglements—
How long can one roam untrammled?
Coarse robes and simple headbands,
Patched garments and frayed tails—
This is the way home.

Asked why I hide,
I point to the pine and moss’s verdant shade.
Wrapped in Azure Mist,
There are monkeys and cranes of the Lake of Heaven,
Friends who know the heart’s intent.
Unmatched.
Leisure is noble.
Resting on Laozi and Zhuangzi’s wisdom,
Not coveting noble titles.
Water trousers and mountain sandals,
Rain cloaks and moon flutes—
A distinct flavor of refinement.

How to obtain such news?
Since ancient times, the lineage of immortals.
Fulfilling my purpose,
I let the shifting lands transform,
Life’s rise and fall pass by.

**Sixth Verse**
With myriad ties released,
I wander with staff and sandals,
Through fields and neighbors’ homes.
Rain hat and wind cloak,
Quail robes and crane bones—
Hiding in the jade-green peaks’ shade.
Worldly turmoil fills the eye,
Yet beyond it, the Dao’s mystery reigns supreme.

The virtue’s wind spreads,
Delighting in purity and tranquility,
Without striving in the world’s affairs.
Serene and refined,
Riding clouds and cranes,
Returning to my ancestral home,
Where swallows and orioles sing of Wang and Xie’s glory.
Pure waters and rocks,
Deep valleys and distant peaks—
Above the dust of noble carriages.
A thousand years of praise and blame,
Success and failure—
All dissolved in a nap of mist and river wilds.

Wonderful!
This life I would sell—
Who could pay its price?

**Seventh Verse**
Cast aside fame and gain.

**Eighth Verse**
Entering the vast lands of **Guangmo**’s village,
I meander with ease, winding and turning.
By winding streams and mountain barriers,
In misty hamlets and cloud-draped dwellings,
I wear simple hemp-cloth and humble herbs—
What need have I of jade halls and lofty caps?
My aspirations are boundless.

To the eastern fence, I while away my days,
In the western garden, I chant and sip.
Endless and far-reaching—
I do nothing, yet live in harmony.
If no kindred soul appears,
Where shall I speak of the Dao’s subtleties?

Books and zithers, stone altars and clay cauldrons—
Beyond these, no true joy exists.
Refined and serene, my demeanor flows like wind,
Yet who now bears witness to my radiance?

I seek my own peace.
A pine by the stream, a moon in the wilds,
A thousand years of monkeys and cranes.

**Ninth Verse**
Cutting off all worldly attachments,
I awaken from the dream of toil—
Like a quail dwelling in a thatched hut.
Feeding ants, roasting fowl,
In dusty robes and wind-worn caps,
I’ve won a hundred years of idle waste.

Gain is like fading mist and fleeting light,
Fame like fallen petals and scattered threads.
How could it endure?

Like a candle in the wind, or dew on a branch—
Who understands?

Alone, I return.
Gathering the waters and clouds,
I lie high on the **Caoxi** path.
Beyond the bamboo, the spring’s flow,
By the fence, wild chrysanthemums,
And the scattered blossoms of the wild crabapple—
All idle pleasures.

Before the Five-Pine Fence, I drink and recite,
With one laugh, transcending the ages.
I wish to impart this wisdom—
Yet sigh at the misty waves’ vastness,
Where are the true listeners?

**Water Dragon Song**
From the jade incense burner, a hundred devout breaths rise,
A single stick of faith-inspiring fragrance,
Swirling and ascending.
Revolving and weaving,
They form a canopy of glory.
Repaying the heavens and the earth.

Encompassing grace.

Repay the virtue/power of the sun and moon’s illumination,
Repay the king’s land and water, for abundance and joy,
Repay the love and care of parents.
Above, I thank the venerable ancestors and their sacred teachings,
The Master of Dan Yang for transmitting the lineage.

Universal salvation in the dusty world,
The Complete Reality Dao/Way endures eternally.
Master Qiu [Zhang] once dwelled in Ninghai.
Together, the three of us secretly harmonized with the Dharma-realm.

May the king reign ten thousand years,
And loyal ministers serve through a thousand autumns—
I invite the disciples to bow in reverence.

---
**Second [Song] #6**
Counting the fleeting world’s ceaseless rush,
Competing for desires, weary of vexations.
Six dynasties, five tyrants,
Three kingdoms, seven states—
Eastward and westward campaigns.
Where now are the martial strategies?
Only desolation remains—wildflowers and fragrant grasses.

Lament the profound schemes and far-sighted plans,
The mighty hearts and bold qi—
All faded, now ashen and withered.
Treading the ancient paths of Chang’an.

Ask the aged remnants of the outskirts:
The Tang palaces, Han gardens,
Qin walls, Zhou ramparts—
All now overgrown with fragrant grasses.

Seeing the old sites, lingering with longing,
Yet former companions have scattered—
No word of them remains.
Reflecting on life’s brief span—
From dawn to dusk—
Heaven and earth endure, yet who can guarantee anything?

**#4**
*[Night’s Clear]* The sky’s vastness breaks the chill,
A pale, translucent heaven—like emerald glass, pure and bright.
No shade beneath the trees,
In Chang’an’s towers, the moon glows soft, the breeze fine.
