A hundred calamities fade unseen,
Ten thousand households share the joy,
All partake in one crisp delight.
Behold the golden—

Stars gleam, clear and bold,
The Milky Way stands firm and wide,
Their light converges, filling earth and heaven.
Flowing through the sapphire expanse like water’s grace.

Unbounded, free to roam,
No pause, no halt—
Crashing mountains, sweeping seas,
Light cascades, radiant and unbounded,
Endless blessings pour forth, pure and bright.

From this moment, all is known:
The Celestial Vessel stands firm,
Jade nectar flows like mud.
My heart’s longing seeks a voice,
Yet who could ever understand?
Let me be lost in blissful intoxication.

---

**#5**
*[Dawn’s Clarity]* The boundless chaos opens in the Southern Peak,
Auspicious clouds emerge from Kunlun’s heights.
Stars shift, lightning flashes,
Shadows rise, light descends—
A crimson glow, faint yet vast.

Cranes dance, phoenixes soar,
Watch the tortoise and dragon coil in harmony.
All of Hongmeng’s breath,
Boiled into Creation’s grand design,
The Dao of immortals—
Instantly revealed.

Ten thousand worlds scatter the Three Isles.
The Celestial Cavern deepens—
Moonlit, winds curl with elegance.
At this hour, I grasp the gate to eternal life,
Long years of vigor, perfect attunement.

Let others sing of change—
Mountains shift, seas transform,
Stones wither, pines age,
While I alone consort with mist and clouds,
Beyond the realm of strife,
Yet grieve for few who truly know.

---

**#6**
I was born to leave the dusty world,
No longer coveting mortal splendor’s fleeting allure.
Disheveled hair, face stained with grime,
All day alone, my inner work refined.
In ancient temples, treasures wrapped in silence,
Let the red wheel sink westward.

The void is known as presence,
White as black—I guard in stillness,
Endless threads of thought unwind,
Silent harmony, my breath attuned.
No cares cling to my heart.

With a satchel at my side,
A staff to lean upon,
Grass sandals, short robes,
Worn legs, sheepskin for cover.
Hunger leads me to beg at doors,
Sated, I hum—*la li la li*—
Let others mock me, fool or sluggard,
Who could ever truly see?

*[Auspicious Crane, Immortal’s Song]*
A hundred years like dreams of butterflies.
Lament the past and present—
How many heroes once aspired to rule,
Yet now are but tales for fishermen and hunters, idle chatter.

Qin palaces, Han gates—
Now only fox trails, rabbit dens.
Remembering splendor’s hollow glow:
Wealth like hot water on snow.
Reflect—

Greed harms the body, profits none,
Empty fame like Wu Yue’s fleeting states.
Follow fate’s guidance, nurture my simplicity.
The gate closed, strife abandoned.
At noon, my knees rest by the window,
A small stream for my fishing line,
Seated before peaks piled in endless layers.

At night, the zither joins me,
With those who truly understand—
Jade sky, silver moon.
The rooster crows, the wooden horse neighs in the wind,
Yet I remain unchanged.

**[The Stone Man Nods, the Mute Speaks]**
A stone man nods in assent,
A mute speaks clearly.
A blue-eyed barbarian monk
Points to the heavens with no hands—
Draws a circle.
No truth to convey.

Let wild passions rage as they will,
Like water spilling from a shattered jar.
In vain do craftsmen toil,
Grinding tiles to polish.
Why contrive such schemes?
To outdo others in rivalry.

Armor laid aside, war’s end—
The Four Quarters in lasting peace.
No need for Zen meditation,
No quest for immortals.
Pure as clarified butter,
I know its natural state.

No step need be moved to reach the Western Paradise.
A wooden man bars the way,
But the iron ox is led along.
Fire wraps a lotus in birth—
The Dao beyond the Dao.

Clouds gather, the moon swells full.
A stone maiden stops her loom,
Her golden needle piercing thread.
Thank you, Third Brother,
Grant me your fishing boat.

Gilded scales gleam in armor,
Red brocade ever more vibrant.
No waves disturb—
I float and sink as nature wills.
Self-satisfied,
I forget the net.

Who dares scatter these tidings?
*[Dreaming of Immortals]*
**Chou Changchun**

*Dreaming of Immortals*
Plainly, I have passed through the Ninefold Heavens.
My **qi** vast and refined,
Piercing white clouds, boundless and ethereal.
Like the **Daode** Assembly at dawn—
Golden boys and jade girls descend to proclaim.

Then all sages gathered,
The Great Bright Light encasing the golden lotus.
Immortal hymns resounded,
Celestial realms rejoiced—
All forgot speech in delight.
Nectar flowed in cups,
Peach clusters feasted upon,
Each lingering in turn.

All wielded **virtue/power** and authority.
Their **spiritual powers** free,
Ages could not displace them.
Before the **Primordial Void**, boundless,
Heaven’s limits nonexistent—
The **Emperor of Forms**’s first emanation.
Piercing the **Ultimate Mysteries**.

My carriage drifts in mist,
My spirit soars through fire,
A million miles in spiraling flight.
The Four Extremes, above and below,
The Eight Directions—
No need to whip the **Luan** and **He** cranes.

When called, I arrive at the hour,
No obstacles—
Roots of my own accord.
I’ve seen all of **Qingdu**’s crimson gates,
Crossed **Yingzhou** and **Zifu** Palace—
No pen can capture it.

At **Youtai** and **Langyuan**’s flowered halls,
Auspicious clouds cast their light,
A hundred harmonies in the fragrant breeze.
Spring’s endless day, eternal warmth—
Everywhere, I feel at ease.

Reflecting on **karma**,
A single spark suffices to perfect it.
Merged with the **Primordial Void**,
Great calamities stretch on forever.
Let the **Jinding** world crumble,
Mountains collapse into caves,
Seas turn to mulberry fields—

*Spring in the Brocade Hall*
Speak of my deepest heart.

Awakening to **Nanguo**’s dream—
A fleeting vision, roots like yellow dust.
Shattering **luxury’s** allure,
Clouds bestow **plainness**,
Recognizing the **lineage’s** truth—
Light returns to its source.
With wisdom’s blade,
I sever the net of attachment,
And with my **li** staff,
I smash the dusty world.

There we meet again,
At **Emamei**’s slopes,
Hiding my radiance, swift as lightning,
Beside **Donghua** Mountain.
Hidden in groves and streams,
Southern **Chen** and Northern **Dou**,
Sun and moon tucked in my sleeves.
My face ageless,
Though heaven shatters and earth collapses—
My true nature remains unchanged.

Dancing in my sleeves,
I scorn the narrowness of **Qiankun**,
Only spreading my hands—
Heaven and earth measured equally.
Drunk with joy,
My sack holds the four seas,
Laughing with delight,
My belly stores the three rivers.

How many times at **Youtai**’s feast,
The **Longevity Peach**’s gatherings—
Immortal banquets, cups raised to the clouds.
**Zhuli** arrives,
The Jade Emperor hosts the feast—
Without me, it cannot proceed.
The **Double-Ninth Festival**,
Seven golden lotuses bloom,
Their divine light radiant as one.

*[The Living Skull]*

The reckoning of life’s vanity—what grand wind flows here?
Clad in robes to shield the form, yet squandering the spirit,
Wasting years in hollow toil.
No thought of impermanence’s approach,
No dread of **Yanlao’s** summons to depart.
Cunningly contriving schemes,
Busy with schemes of greed—
Endless strife, yet bound in suffering.
Empty bustle, fleeting fame, thin gains—
Only more idle sorrow to provoke.
A breath of three inches—
Once severed, lone on barren hills I lie.
Sighing through ages, rise and fall—
Time flees swift, cannot be stayed.
How fine to drift free, refine the nature,
Cast aside past arrogance.
Lay down dusty toil,
Awaken to the heart’s true light—
Soaring on winds, wild clouds gathered in.
Mountains still, the **Taixu** vast and empty,
Stars and moon illuminating **Yingzhou**.
Truly bliss—
Unbounded joy, no envy of kings.

---
*[The Sleep Demon King]*
A hundred harms he brings, a thousand calamities.
By day, he still may lurk—
By night, no place to hide.
He vexes men to stupor, drunk as fools,
Undermines practice, squanders life’s brief span.
Eyes glued shut, head crushed like a mountain’s weight,
A fog of dullness, frail and weak.
He lures the **Three Corpses, Six Bandits**,
Steals **yuanqi** in dreams’ embrace.
Endless his tricks—
Soaring through **Dharmadhatu**, wild and mad.
Thus, without cause, so perverse—
I urge all: guard yourselves with care.
Mind death’s path, the great affair ahead—
Protect the **Three Lights** with earnestness.
No leaning on others—
Awakening alone, fierce as **Guan Yu and Zhang Fei**.
They clash in battle,
Sharp as blades, unyielding—
One mind presses forward.
Chased away, clouds disperse, mists fade,
Cool and clear.

---
**Ma Dan yang** swears this oath,
Burning the vow in solemn pledge.
First, uphold the law of the land.
Seeing men and women, parents alike,
I renounce **qi, wealth, wine, and lust**,
Abandon glory, shun the tainted.
Ever pure, ever humble, reverent,
No factions, no bias.
In coarse robes, I beg my daily bread,
Hunger and cold—then stretch my hand in the street.
No greed for wealth, no boastful lies,
No feigning wisdom as a fraud.
Always mind the end as the beginning,
In peril, stand firm.
Should I stray from the Dao,
May my body split a thousand times,
Forever sunk in **Yellow Springs**.

---
*[For the Practitioner]*
The Daoist does not dwell in mountains,
Nor toil in endless rounds of **kneeling and bowing**.
Why cling to petty comings and goings,
Far journeys to seek the master?
No need for seated meditation,
Nor laboring, planting for food.
No need for bitter herbs,
To trade for robes and rice.
Where do you fix your mind?
Only this: no trace of defilement—
Break free from all such bonds.
Better to beg in the marketplace,
Gathering scraps and leftovers.
Asking after hollow fame and gain—
Sigh, death’s shadow darkens the heart.
Forgotten dust, forgotten thoughts—
Let future ranks among immortals be.
---
*[Shu Kui Flower]*
---
**Wang Chongyang** transmits the secret precepts:
Only when dusty passions fade.
Tame the **horse of desire**, the **monkey-mind**,
Lock them tight—let none escape.
Banish stinginess, strife, delusion—
Cut the roots of **self and others**.
Guard your cleverness, guard your wisdom—
Let them grow dull.
The **Purple Palace’s** Lord rests.
The **Treasure Cauldron’s** cinnabar seals.
No need to speak of **Dragon and Tiger**,
Of **lead and mercury’s** tangled threads.
From the **Misty Clouds’** pile,
A single wheel of moon is lifted.
Now the **Xiyu** lineage stands apart.
---
*[The Five Volumes of the Crane’s Cry]* ends here.

---
*The Daoist Realm: [The Gathering from Panxi]*
*[Shu Kui Flower]* is rendered as *"Fine Grass and Mustard Seed"* in the original.

This poem is likely a **zaju** [散曲 *zǎnqǔ*—a form of Chinese dramatic song, often secular], though its meter requires further study.

The following six **yuefu** [词 *cí*—lyric poems] under the title *"Phoenix Nesting in the Willow"* [凤栖梧 *Fèng Qī Wú*]:
With the exception of the second poem, which appears in *The Poems of Master Yǔchán* [玉蟾先生诗余 *Yùchuán Xiānsheng Shīyú*],
the remaining five are attributed to **Qiu Chúji** [丘处机 *Qiū Chǔjī*—a prominent figure in the **Quanzhen** *全真* **Daoist school**], also found in *The Gathering from Panxi* [磻溪集 *Pánxī Jí*] and *The Journey to the West* [西游记 *Xīyóu Jì*].

The original misattributed the **yuefu** title as *"Nán Xiāngzǐ"* [南香子 *Nán Xiāngzǐ*—a Southern tune], but it should be the **Southern tune double-meter** *"Xíng Xiāngzǐ"* [行香子 *Xíng Xiāngzǐ*—*Walking in Fragrance*].

The original lacks an author’s signature, but this poem also appears in *The Complete Quanzhen Lyrics of Zhòngyáng* [重阳全真集 *Zhòngyáng Quánzhēn Jí*] Volume Five.

The original lacks an author’s signature. The following four poems—all under the title *"Water Dragon’s Roar"* [水龙吟 *Shuǐlóngyín*],—are also found in *The Gathering from Panxi* and are by **Qiu Chúji**.

In *The Gathering from Panxi*, these three lines read:
*"Táng Cháo Hànshì, Qín Guān Zhōu Yuàn, Míngmíng Jiàn Gào"* [唐朝汉市，秦官周苑，明明见告].
---
*[Crane’s Cry Remaining Echoes]* concludes here.
---
*The Sixth Volume of Daoist Play at Xiānyóu Shān*
Collected by **Daoist Master Péng Zhìzhōng** [仙游山道士彭致中 *Xiānyóu Shān Dàoshì Péng Zhìzhōng*] of **Xiānyóu Shān**.

**Eight Modes of *Gānzhōu* [甘州]**
*(Attributed to Hé Xiāngū [何仙姑])*

Thousands of gates and halls—
All toppled seven times eight,
Digging earth to seek the sky.
Truly wondrous, yet reduced to childish babble.
The Daoist of Non-Action walks few paths,
Yet along the way of strange encounters,
A thousand sorrows accumulate.
The dung-beetle’s ball becomes an elixir.
Helpless in grief, yet none know the cause—
In vain, family ties are cast aside.
Time is pure and still—
How could it grasp the alchemy of mercury and lead?
Thoughts and schemes never cease—
Even in sleep, the shadow-demons cling.
The more one turns, the deeper the sorrow—
Revenge becomes the cycle.
Who would believe in the birth of nothingness,
And nothingness giving rise to all?
All streams return to their source.

---
**The Second [Section]**
A cluster of spring snow,
Cast into a jade furnace to boil.
Fires blaze without ceasing—
Burn until it glows red, without flame or smoke.
Mindful not to lose a grain—
The weight remains unchanged.
Thus, three thousand [times].
Only when refined to immobility,
Can it be called Zen.
Nurturing True Life lies here—
Between these very breaths.
The garden holds its own sweet dew.
To nourish the golden sprout,
That the rare lotus may bloom.
In seclusion, await the coming—
To stand shoulder-to-shoulder with the Immortals.

---
**Treading Snow [踏雪行]**
Piercing antiquity, mastering the present,
Clarifying scripture, resolving meaning.
Endless debates make the heavens fall.
Chasing painted bread to sate hunger—
Bamboo shadows cannot sweep the hall’s dust.
Few desires, few thoughts—
Silent joy, beyond words.
All schools struggle to let go—
If one departs from this inch of mind,
Even iron shoes would be trod to no avail.

---
**Willow Leaf Green [柳梢青]**
Faintly, the morning star flickers.
White dew on withered moss,
Ruined walls of an ancient site—
Pale smoke, fading grass,
The Han dynasty’s palaces.
On Chang’an’s thoroughfare, travelers still
Pursue fame and profit as before.
Youth fades, ancient and modern alike—
A sliver of moon over the pass.

---
**The Second [Section]**
Awakening to neither birth nor death—
Not even a flower plucked, a leaf taken.
When inspired, sing aloud,
Drunkenly sleep on fragrant grass,
Dreaming of celestial halls.
Sometimes, bitterly admonishing all—
Do not, I implore you, heed my warnings.
Walking like a hollow corpse,
Greed turns the face ashen—
Wasting years in vain.

---
**Plum Blossom Tune [梅花引]**
Old Master of the Fragrant Peaks,
Grew white-haired early.
In mortal life, both good and evil were wrought.
Poverty and wealth—both known.
Gain and loss, rise and fall—
All like a dream within a dream.
Because of poverty, the body bears no shame;
Because of leisure, the heart knows no burden.
Do not seek high talent,
Do not seek high name.
Talent and fame bring only laborious turns.
Know little of affairs—
Fewer are the vexations.
When the heart forgets and the belly burns—
When will this end?
Do not lift the eyes,
Do not open the mouth.
Endless strife—
How can one escape it?
Coming alone, going alone, no companion.
Pouring alone, drinking alone—
No honor, no disgrace.
Let others slander, let others suspect.
A tranquil heart knows
The clear wind and bright moon.

---
**Gazing at the Plum Blossom [望梅花]**
Life and death are the greatest trials of the self.
From the start, they have harmed me.

**Hunger drives me to seek food,
Thirst compels me to beg for drink,
Cold brings me to search for robes and coverings—
How hard it is to endure!
Day and night they follow me,
Plaguing me beyond measure.

Abandoning my mother-given fleshly vessel,
I entrust myself to the care of the two families of ease.
When I walk, I pierce the clouds;
When weary, I rest beneath the moon,
Playing freely in the boundless void—
How light and swift!

Seizing the wind-wheel,
Straddling the divine tortoise,
I traverse all realms without hindrance.

**Second Stanza:**
Cease debating right and wrong—
The weak will see their truth in time.
Do not blame others,
Nor deceive yourself—
The hidden sage reveals himself.
Hear my counsel:
From ancient times to now,
Not a single thing has been spared.
Sweep away the dust of entanglements—
Pure and unchanging from beginning to end.
Though rooted deep,
Long life and eternal vision
Cannot escape the fleeting beauty of youth.
Refine qi and spirit—
When you meet a kindred soul,
Share the mysteries of the *Xi Yi*—
Reveal all.

**Third Stanza:**
Thick crimson clouds shroud the earth.
A gusting wind from the north arises—
The Great Block breathes,
Yang congeals, yin coalesces,
And jade flowers bloom across the four wilds in omens.
Such intentions—
The sage feels the abundance of the year,
Manifesting the Tang and Yu eras once more,
A world restored to order.
Reverence the Dao, honor Confucius, cultivate righteousness,
Cherish the Three Teachings as one body.
Filial sons and virtuous grandsons,
Loyal ministers and upright courts—
Harmony flows from top to bottom.
Within the sacred cauldron,
Incense burns bright,
Praying for the emperor’s longevity—
May his reign last ten thousand years.

**Fourth Stanza:**
The sun lingers at the southern window,
Still I sleep.

**Fifth Stanza:**
Beyond the sparse bamboo grove, the thatched gate stays shut.
Suddenly, someone arrives—
Lightly knocking at the door,
I barely turn, too lazy to rise.
Just as sweetness deepens—
A taste so dark and intoxicating,
Asking in the world—
What could compare?
Only deep, drunken oblivion
Forgets the startling fear,
Forgets the fall—
Neither rising nor falling known,
Life and death alike,
One with heaven and earth.
Such meaning—
Hard to grasp,
Yet like a mute solving a riddle.

**Sixth Stanza:**
Do not judge others’ flaws.
Search your own faults,
Lest you stir chaos yourself.
The old heart-monkey,
The wild intent-horse—
Now awakened,
Gradually tamed by restraint.
Still the mind within,
Refining to purity and balance,
Transforming the mortal frame.
When matters arise, decide swiftly—
Even immortals have no other method.
Through ages unending,
With an empty heart and full belly,
The wise strategist needs no calculations.
When merit is complete,
Riding a cloud of blessing,
You ascend to the Celestial Court,
Dwelling in the Hall of the Immortal.

**Seventh Stanza:**
A hundred years of youth pass like lightning.
In vain to look back—
Another cycle comes.
Selling bones for return,
Through countless lives and deaths,
Only changing faces.
To escape—
Seize the clear wind,
Turning the void into a single expanse.
No need to chant the *Chuang-tzu* scriptures,
Nor cling to entanglements.
Sever the midstream,
Pierce the heart’s core,
Shooting through jade halls and golden palaces.
Do not falter—
With unwavering resolve,
Watch as the moon rises over the peaks.
The needle stops—
*Sanfeng*’s True Person says the Dao is hard to speak.
To awaken, understand each layer,
Until all is clear.

**Continuation:**

Pierce through with luminous clarity,
Returning radiance to its source—
No need to pluck flowers or leaves.
Movement spawns distinction.
Cease all grasping thoughts,
Lest tangled branches grow.
In its original form,
Pure and unadorned,
What need for words?

Only fierce resolve will suffice.
With wisdom’s blade drawn,
Cut like iron—unrelenting.
Shatter the mountain of affection,
Leap from the sea of love,
Break the void’s false repose.

Qi and spirit rejoice.
Cultivate the Nine Suns,
Refining into crimson snow.
Wrapped in rainbow hues,
A single offering—
A moon of pristine whiteness.

**Acclamation to the Sacred Reign#1**
*(Attributed to Qiu Changchun)*

When the sun sinks low,
The plains gather its last glow,
The willow locks in cold mist.
Facing the southern stream,
Alone I sit, drifting with the wind’s breath,
Listening to the cascading spring.
Through endless night,
Forgetting all affairs,
My idle nature hums—
The zither plays without strings.

Await the time when the Azure Crow descends from the clouds,
To prove the earthly immortal’s truth.

**Second Stanza:**
After the wild monk departs,
The fisherman’s boat ties to shore,
Green pines rise in mist.
Before the cold lamp’s flicker,
I toss aside books and sleep,
Listening to the stones rinse the spring.
The alchemical furnace cools,
The zither hall falls silent—
The wind-tunes the strings.

Await the moment when the lone peak’s moon shines bright,
When the Zhengyi adept dreams of transcendence.

**Song of the Incense Offering**
Silent, boundless, vast—#2

**First Stanza:**
Wine spills in a light drizzle.
A faint life—
One taste of unbounded ease.
Beside the valley’s mouth,
Leaning askew on the mountain’s flank.
A bamboo fence gates the door,
A broom of wild jasmine,
A grass wad for a marker.
A coarse hemp robe, loose and wide,
Its sash long and trailing.
A gnarled staff—
A curved vine’s tip.
Goji berries self-boiled,
Atractylodes brewed by hand.
A clay teapot, a sand-stove hearth,
A gourd ladle, a wooden dipper.

**Second Stanza #3:**
The Celestial Gardens, the Penglai Isles,
Jin Valley’s towering halls—
Yet none compare
To this thatched hut’s quiet grace.
Wildflowers embroider the earth—
No need for artificial charm.
Spring suits it well,
So does summer, so does autumn.
When the wine is ripe, it’s worth toasting.
When guests arrive, they must be kept.
No glory, no shame, no care—
Retreat one step further,
What matter the reasons?
Only when weary, sleep;
When thirsty, drink;
When drunk, sing.

**Third Stanza:**
A low, crooked wall,
A squat, sparse window.
A monk’s boy#4 by a tiny pond.
Layered screens rise high and low,
Beside the green water’s edge.
Yet there are breezes,
There are moons,
There are coolnesses.
Daily life is simple:
A wooden table, a vine bed.
Before my eyes—
Water’s hue, mountain’s light.
Guests come without wine,
Yet words of heart may still flow.
Only then—
Jade-warmed tea steeped,
A steaming cup,
A shallow bowl of broth.

**Fourth Stanza:**
Swept clean of dust,
Spared the creeping moss.
Let red leaves
Pile the threshold before me.
Worthy of a painting—
Truly strange and wondrous.
A few pine trees,
A few bamboo stalks,
A few plum branches.
Nurture the flowers and wood,
Let them bloom in turn.
Tomorrow’s matters—
Let Heaven arrange them.
Who knows when wealth and honor may come?
I but drift, content,
Live as fate allows,
And keep my heart at ease.

---
**Alchemical Pill (Roll of Gold Elixir) – Yang Zhēnrén**

**First Pill (First Watch):**
Wrap in one layer,
Tame the restless mind’s steed.
Monkey-spirit, cease your capers!
When great awakening comes,
The heart grows cool and clear—
All falls away naturally.
The true face ever unbound.
True purity, ever refined,
Ever more serene.
Fewer words, qi preserved whole—
Follow the seasons’ transformations.

**Second Pill (Second Watch):**
Wrap in two layers,
Union of husband and wife.
With child and maiden,
Yin and yang in harmony.
Restore the cosmos,
Let inversion cycle endlessly—
Raise the high, match the low.
Earth Ox, Wood Horse—
Shake the mountains, stir the seas.
With the Ram’s [chariot]#6,
Carry and convey.
Douse the flames,
Roll all into the mud-pill—
Let spirits tremble in awe.

**Third Pill (Third Watch):**
Wrap in three layers,
Root and stem made firm.

**Fourth Pill (Fourth Watch):**
Luminous and hollow—
The sun reaches its zenith.
Must return and invert,
Clay-wrapped, reverse the chariot’s push—
Soil erupts at once.
Wood and metal separated, black tortoise and hare ascend.
The *Dao*’s blade and measuring rod arrive,
Mercury and lead converge.
Descend to fill the earth—
White snow pours into yellow sprouts,
Behold jade flowers, golden lotuses blooming.

**Fourth Pill (Fourth Watch):**
Wrap in four layers,
The Dao’s drum resounds.
Golden rooster, wooden head sings.
Then revolve and rotate,
Ascend and descend through dual gates—
Awaken early, pass through the Hall of Light.
Tiger and dragon move freely,
Can draw and add,
Circulate water and fire.
Refine black to red,
Roll the golden pill within the furnace,
Advance snow-white cinnabar grains.

**Fifth Pill (Fifth Watch):**
Wrap in five layers,
Dawn approaches.
The work is complete,
All is fulfilled.
Then shed the shell,
Come and go without obstruction—
[The] true form revealed.
Ancient and modern immortal families rejoice,
Extend life, forever youthful.
Descend the purple edict,
Report to the Jade Emperor’s decree,
Ascend the auspicious clouds to Penglai Isle.
Two crowns—
**Master Ma Dan-yang**
Wrap in one layer,
Must be focused and pure.

The mind at ease, sit quietly and watch.

Monkeys caper—
Do not let them topple you.
First, reduce sleep’s encroachment.
A scattered mind reveals the azure sky.
Countless grains of sand fulfill the great thousand—
Effort must be made,
To perfect the practice.
This is not contrived—
It is natural.

**Second Watch:**
Wrap in two layers,
Qi flows in pairs.
Lead dissolves, mercury’s flame sears.
Lead becomes mercury,
Mercury becomes lead.
The harmonizing qi fills the Celestial Cavern.
Harmonizing qi, entrusted to the Void’s source.
Nine curves of luminous pearls strung—
Pierce the twin gates,
Shoot through to the azure heights—
Natural, as it ever was.

**Third Watch:**
Wrap in three layers,
Moon at full orb.
Night’s music fades.
Golden Boy rejoices,
Jade Maiden delights.
Ordinary folk are not the same.
The Elixir of Longevity—
Drink it and never reel.
After drinking, return to youth.
On the Curved River’s banks,
Gazing at the hanging clouds.
No need for coin to buy.

**Fourth Watch:**
Wrap in four layers,
Pierce the crystalline depths.
Crystalline depths pierce the azure heights.
Ascend the Other Shore,
Stride over the Phoenix and the Mandarin Duck.
Three years of toil—
Not great words,
But no idle speech.
When spoken, no words remain.

「Monkeys are horses, horses are monkeys—
Do not dismiss them as mere opposites.
**Fifth Watch:**
Wrap in five layers,
Horned melodies blare.
Awakened from pure dreams of Daoist wandering,
Sleep is but a dream, dreams but sleep.
Only now do I know the heart is the Celestial Cavern.
The Dao gives birth to Earth, Earth to the Dao.
*Qi* unites—one breath blends the Primordial Origin.
Add a year, subtract an age,
The True Void remains undisturbed.
Each step is delicate.

**Fan Zhenren** dwells in ancient tombs and cellars.
Moving, sitting, standing—all in song and dance.
Seizing this True Void,
Awakening fiercely.
From ancient times to now, they speak of Dragon and Tiger.
None, not one, truly understands—
Humans awaken.

**The Second:**
Passed down a single phrase of truth,
Teach me to graft and connect.
Since grafting and connecting began,
All separation ends.
Jade buds bloom, golden flowers bear fruit—
Mutes taste molasses honey, speechless.
**The Third:**
Softness and weakness are the family’s virtue.
The Great Dao does not abandon the Void.
Truly, truly there is—
Lead and Mercury.
Water and Fire harmonized, rising and descending in balance.
Civil and Martial forces clash—
Their powers unified.

**The Fourth:**
True practice with true power—
The sword and the elixir swift as wind.
Without meeting a true master-craftsman,
It cannot be made clear.
If you perform this as the first practice,
Every joint in your body,
All flows freely.

**The Fifth**...

**The Sixth:**
The poor child drinks fine wine,
Drinks until he’s drunk and still.
All worldly cares drop from his mind—
Ren’s slanders, blame, all slip away.
A deaf-mute fool—
This is true cultivation.

**The Seventh:**
The Dao of non-action, natural and free,
Pure, nurturing the immortal herb.
Silent understanding—
That is enough.
Darkness veils the furnace sealed.
In an instant of effort—
It is done.

**The Eighth:**
Do not cling to nature as truth.
How then does the yang spirit emerge?
Nine out of ten guard the stubborn void.
If you carry the foundation of life with nature,
White flour baked into bread—
It is certain.

**The Ninth:**
The sacred mushroom grows everywhere,
Yet none recognize it.
When the work is vast and done,
It cannot be matched.
I wish to tell you now—
But fear you’ll disbelieve,
Speak nonsense.

**The Tenth:**
Believe, and you will trust yourself.
Disbelieve, and do not act.
Do not wait until thirst strikes
To dig the well.
Each day you see your labor,
Yet it avails not—
Do not speak of it.

**Appendix:**
I love quiet dwelling,
My heart-mirror ever clear.
When the realm vanishes, emotions forgotten,
Naturally, no distinctions remain.
The lotus scatters across the empty sky,
Revealing the moon in the pure heavens.
This family virtue—
Words cannot fully express it.

**The Second [Appendix]:**
Wrap yourself at the first watch,
Calm the heart, sit upright and steady.

**The Third:**
Drive back the host of demons,
White sheep march in ranks.
Light the lamp within the heart,
Behold the original self.
The mind’s core is pure and bright—
A single pearl hangs suspended.

**The Second [Appendix]:**
At the second watch,
Wrap yourself in silence,
Calm the heart, sit upright and steady.

**The Fourth:**
At the third watch,
The sun arises, parent and child bow toward the golden gate.
The spirit turtle of the sea
Drains the blood of the golden rooster.
*Qi* flows soft and boundless,
Piercing the three passports.
Ten thousand *Dao*’s radiant hues
Lift the moon from the Western River.

**The Fifth:**
At the fourth watch,
All is tranquil on every side.
Within, the heart’s blossom opens,
Enjoying the eternal spring’s scene.
The fifth and sixth gates part—
A true person enters.
A single grain of golden elixir
Is carried to the Kunlun peak.

**The Sixth:**
At the fifth watch,
Dawn returns, fulfilling the vow of practice.
Dragon and tiger entwine,
Rolling up the Yellow River.
Halfway through the sky—
Thunderous voices,
Ghosts and gods cannot fathom the debate.
Recognizing the original self,
The true face is naturally revealed.

**The Seventh:**
After fasting, wandering at leisure,
Singing alone with no one to respond.
Mountain woodcutters
Also sing their *□□□□*[1].
Climbing one slope,
Descending another.
Even as a high official,
None compare to me.

**The Eighth:**
After a year,
Another year is added.
Each day follows fate,
Why strive for idle *heqi*[2]?
Alas, the prime of life
Flees like snapping fingers.
Do not wait until the end—
The thirty-first day of the twelfth month.

**The Ninth:**
I earnestly advise all,
Each to listen and understand.

---
[1] *□□□□* (unclear, possibly a rhyming placeholder)
[2] *heqi* (和氣, harmonious *qi*)

**The Tenth:**
Unversed in *yin-yang*[3],
How could one know the Dao’s path?
At first, one begins—
Refining lead and mercury into form.
Naturally, tortoise and serpent
Guide one along the Caoqi path[4].

**The Eleventh:**
The wise and discerning,
Each must listen and understand.

In the year of *jiǎzǐ*[5], one’s true lifespan—
Day by day, the *zhēnshù*[6] descends.
Breaking free from the mundane cage,
A path to eternal life unfolds.
Avoid the *Yánwáng*’s[7] grasp,
Lest his ghostly messengers drag you away.

At the first watch,
Sitting still, slowly harmonizing *lónghǔ*[8].
Circulating the Three Passes[9],
Piercing into the *níwán*[10].
The Dragon coils in the Golden Cauldron,
The Tiger prowls at the Yellow Court’s gate.
Such efforts—
Do not treat them lightly.

**The Twelfth:**
At the second watch,
The two *yīnyáng* essences merge in subtle *qi*.
Ascending and descending the Three Passes,
Do not let them falter.
The *xiānǚ*[11] and infant,
Both now playfully coquettish.
*Jīngōng* and *Huángpó*[12],
Naturally paired in harmony.

**The Thirteenth:**
At the third watch,
The bright moon illuminates the cosmos.
Daemons flee—
Not a trace within a thousand *lǐ*.
Retreating all *yīnbīng*[13],
No need for elixirs or blades.
The tortoise and serpent of the depths
Naturally entwine.

**The Fourteenth:**
At the fourth watch,
With leisure, study the true scriptures.
Each word profound,
Speaking of Daoist cultivation.
No need for water or fire,
No need for fuel or charcoal.
Refining the elixir—
No gold could match its worth.

**The Fifteenth:**
At the fifth watch,
As dawn breaks, the Golden Rooster crows.
A task at hand—
Clapping hands, laughing aloud.
Feeding the ox fully,
Sleeping joyfully.
When practice is complete,
The *dānshū* decree[14] arrives naturally.

*Yòubóméi*[15] exhorts all to awaken.
Cultivation’s bitterness—
Three layers of suffering.
Yet clearly, one escapes the gate.
*Tán Mǎqiū Liú*[16], *Sūn Wáng Hǎo Tàigǔ*[17],
The *Fǎhǎi*’s[18] boundless compassion—
Universal salvation across the world.

**The Sixteenth:**
Transforming the ignorant and crude.

**The Seventeenth:**
Cast aside the fire-lit halls of sons and daughters.
With the blade of wisdom, sever the three layers of suffering.
Human and self dissolve like mountains collapsing,
Controversies and disputes vanish like dried seas.
Past karmic debts erased,
New calamities not incurred.

**The Eighteenth:**
*Yìng Xiān Jǔ*[19]—respond to the celestial call.
The path of *Xīyí*[20] where mercury and lead blend black and white.
True practice lies below—
The labor of resolute perseverance.
Day and night without sleep,
Coarse robes and plain fare suffice.
Begging alms at street corners,
All beings are my parents.

**The Nineteenth:**
Free from worry.
A lone cloud and wild crane, unbound by constraints.
Within the grass hut,
Leisurely peruse the *Golden Scriptures*.
Outside the window, groves and springs—
Mountains, waters, and bamboo in view.
Bright moon and pure wind,
Worthy companions indeed.

**The Twentieth:**
Nurture the primal essence.
Tame the heart-monkey and mind-horse firmly.
The Six Bandits[21] subdued—
Never coveting their temptations.
Vague and dim, the depths of stillness,
Dull and silent, the realm of emptiness.
Deep and clear, the stillness of nature,
Where essence halts and life abides.

**The Twenty-First:**
Seize the true intent.
Wood and metal, separated yet connected by the *Daoist Path*.
The four limbs as the *Four Symbols*[22],
The five elements as the *Five Phases*[23] gathered whole.
*Qi*[24] coalesces, spirit condenses,
Yin and yang return in natural cycle.
Perfume the body through and through,
The *Microcosmic Fire*[25] burns fully throughout.

**The Twenty-Second:**
Break the path of delusion.

**The Twenty-Third:**
Earth Thunder shakes the mountain peaks with rain.
Yellow sprouts rise, white snowflakes dance.
Dew sprinkles the elixir broth,
Auspicious herbs fill the garden plot.
Jade medicines scatter, golden blossoms unfurl.

**The Twenty-Fourth:**
The realm is worthy of depiction.
Soaring through clouds and waters, steps unbounded.
Over the winding river—
Flying crows, racing hares.
Tigers coil, dragons curl,
Yin and yang converge in high union.
Turning the celestial pass,
Moving the earthly axis.

**The Twenty-Fifth:**
The *Dharma Wheel* resounds.
The *River Chariot* steady with thirty spokes.
Lifting sun and moon,
Rolling them into the golden furnace.
In the jade cauldron, the *Nine Solar Fires* boil.
Ten thousand rays of radiance,
A thousand layers of emerald mist.

**The Twenty-Sixth:**
Enveloping the luminous pearl.
Nurturing the born-again embryo’s dance.
The *True Celebration*—
Fairy maidens gather in circle.
Quenching thirst with *elixir wine*,
The jade zither plays itself.
The melody sets—divine sounds,
Striking metal, striking stone.

**The Twenty-Seventh:**
Being within non-being,
Non-being yet something formed.
Within being and non-being, search and take.
Non-being hides the True,
Being yet seems as non-being.
Forgotten both being and non-being,
Returning to the Great Void.

**The Twenty-Eighth:**
Practices complete.
The Three Isles of Penglai—clusters of immortals gather.
At the *Jade Pool*—
Sages and worthies without number.
All are cultivators of the True,
Daoist companions in the *Path of Perfection*.
Serving the Highest Authentic Ones,
The Western Sovereign, the Holy Mother.

**The Twenty-Ninth:**
Feasting at the Celestial Kitchen,
Immortal robes cling—light as lifting.
Riding *qilin* and phoenix,
Reveling in the Pure Capital.
Jewel halls and *elixir* towers,
Golden nails fill the vermilion gates.
Eternal spring without night,
No coming, no going.

---
**[Song in the Shang Mode – *Wu Ye Er* Tune #6]**
Observing egrets, watching crows,
Fishing for shrimp beneath the waves.
Nightingales weave through willows,
Butterflies dote on flowers.
Scenes of quiet elegance—
None but Cloud Gate’s disciples can praise.

---
**The Thirty-First:**
Reflecting on Lin Ji,
Great compassion as the foundation.
Strike once—
Skin peeled away.
Foolishly dazed,
Unaware of pain or itch.

**The Thirty-Second:**
Brushes of tortoise hair,
Awls of rabbit horn,
Toads leaping to the sky.
Mud ox bellows,
Wooden horses neigh.
Few know—
Bowing and nodding betray celestial secrets.

**The Thirty-Third:**
Wheat has flour,
Millet has grain,
Cloth wraps legs beneath.
Mountains have stone,
Seas have water.
Speak truly—
The *Dao* of the *Cave of the Immortals* stands firm.

**The Thirty-Fourth:**
Taming the mind-horse,
Locking the heart-monkey,
Nurturing *qi* and spirit to fullness.
No forced contortion—
Harmony with nature.
Body in the mysterious,
Law-eyes surpassing the *Great Thousand*.

**The Thirty-Fifth:**
The *Mystic Barrier* sealed,
The *Transformation City*’s gate—
One kick overturns it.
Where flowers bloom red,
Willows turn green.
No obstruction remains—
Everywhere, faces of immortals and Buddhas.

**The Thirty-Sixth:**
Moon at the sky’s edge,
Full and round—
Digging earth to find heaven.
Being and non-being inverted,
Inverted again.
Mysteries profound—
The True *Dao* must be transmitted orally.

**The Thirty-Seventh:**
Moon at the sky’s edge,
Crescent ascending—
The *True Path*’s wonders endless.
Dragons seize tigers,
Tigers seize dragons.
Meeting thus,
They form a golden blossom in the wind.

**The Thirty-Eighth:**
Moon at the sky’s edge,
Directly south—
Three before, three behind.
*Li* is female,
*Kan* is male.
Discussing mysteries—
If not revealed,
How shall one seek?

**The Thirty-Ninth:**

**The Forty-Second:**
Moon at the sky’s edge,
Residing in the furnace—
Lead and mercury in the crucible.
Gold relies on fire,
Refined into a pearl.
One gourd,
Three hundred eighty-four *catty*—
*Mantinghuang* blooms:
Stone and fire’s fleeting light,
Human life too brief—
Death’s arrival cannot be foreseen.
Born or perish—
Like lightning’s fleeting clash.
Piercing the false union of form,
Seeking the *Dao*’s immortal elixir.
Reflecting, then turning toward the Way,
To recognize the sovereign of the *Law*.
Face-to-face, ever-present—
Together walking, sitting,
Drinking the dew of the clouds.
Companions with clear wind and bright moon,
Shared purpose, shared vision of heaven’s light.
Together meeting,
Together seeking the Master’s *Dao*,
Together singing *Mantinghuang*.

---

**The Forty-Third:**
The *Lofty Clouds*’ True Person’s love for mountains
Wears away without end—
Dreaming amid cold forests.
When shall I truly return to the caves,
Sitting on a lotus cushion beneath pine shade?
Wild cranes as companions,
Mountain apes knowing my tune.

**The Forty-Fourth:**
A single pill of marvelous medicine,
A single zither—
All cares sink deep.
Turning, I laugh coldly at worldly travelers,
With whom to barter for gold?

No thought of fading youth,
Yet white hairs creep in unseen.

**The Forty-Fifth:**
North *Yan*’s slopes, grass thick and tangled,
Bones scattered, jumbled.
Tumbled stones, no one recognizes—
Let yellow oxen and white calves till the earth.
What of Qin’s generals and Han’s ministers?

**The Forty-Sixth:**
Better to return, walking with clouds,
Learning eternal life.
The *Dao*-friend by the clear stream,
Picking pine flowers to pair with reishi.
If only the elixir’s sun and moon within,
No need for fame on paper.

**The Forty-Seventh:**
The Southern Expeditionary Protectorate’s horse, *Ru Long*,
Shoulders a carved bow.
With golden seals and purple ribbons late returned,
Called by men a white-haired, failing elder.

A fleeting glance—one brief dream,
Turning away, all things vanish into emptiness.

**The Forty-Eighth:**
Hurrying with a crow’s pickaxe to the cloud-peaked heights,
Leaning alone against a towering pine.
Endless vistas, a thousand poems—
Yet who remains to share my carefree idleness?

Long nights with three cups of murky wine,
Cool evenings with a pillow of clear wind.

**The Forty-Ninth:**
Nine returns, seven transformations—laboring with effort,
Refining in the crimson furnace.
When the Golden Elixir ripens, its light spans a thousand *zhang*,
Rainbow clouds enfold a single dark pearl.
Wrapped in moonlight, I seize the Jade Rabbit,
Within the sun’s heart, I rouse the Golden Crow.

**The Fiftieth:**
The Green Boy delivers the Purple Crane’s scroll,
Inviting me into the *Peng Hu* pavilion.
The Ten Isles bloom with eternal spring,
Drunk on peach wine, fragrance fills the Pure Capital.
A thousand years’ white hair turns black,
A boundless *kalpa*’s pallor remains vermilion.

**The Fifty-First:**
Human wealth and honor—nothing but skulls,
Floating like driftwood on the water.
The dreams of Sui, Tang, Jin, Song, Qi, Liang—
Now only desolate mounds in silence.
Outside the hall, yellow flowers and emerald bamboo,
By the water, white cranes lament the autumn.

**The Fifty-Second:**
Cease, return, and cease—unfurl the brow.
Deep in the white clouds, high repose is fitting,
Like the *Tan Ma Qiu Liu* of Shandong.
Seven golden lotuses bloom resplendent,
Ten thousand branches of jade medicine sway with grace.
A single staff of *lí* wood, let it wander as it will,
Sleeves of coarse cloth trailing long.
Why ask of disputes or worldly gain?
Treading the misty *Yan* slopes, through smoke and vines.
Midday meal beneath twin green pines,
Autumn robes by a pond of blue lotuses.

**The Fifty-Third:**
From the depths of white clouds, songs of purple *zhī* mushrooms,
Laughing coldly, *hēhē*.
On the Long An Road, lingering travelers—
In vain, their dreams enter *Nan Keo*.
Though they boast of fine carriages,
Who knows their temples have turned ashen?

**The Fifty-Fourth:**
North-window poise, jade teeth gleaming,
Midday dreams shattered.
Mountain springs cascade on stone—priceless clarity,
This tower half-sinks into the clouds.
A thousand volumes of poetry, carefree,
A single incense burner, serene and quiet.

**The Fifty-Fifth:**
All ties severed, the heart finds peace,
Returning to youthful vigor.
Within the jar, a single truth revealed—
Who dares now knock at the Mysterious Gate?
Thanks to the thousand-year-old crane,
Silently transmitting the Nine-Turn Elixir.

**The Fifty-Sixth:**
Face like cold iron, bones like withered wood,
Heart like frozen ash.
Dao-emotion does not align with human feeling—
Who then can send or welcome?

Night, listening to the dripping of springs,
Dawn, gazing at the towering mountain hues.

**The Fifty-Seventh:**
A lone, long whistle stirs the cold clouds,
An old crane lingers.
Do not speak of fame in the imperial capital,
Lest it disturb the high recluse on *Tian Tai*.
Prepare a flat-bottomed boat with short oars,
Arrange a bamboo hat and straw sandals.

**The Fifty-Eighth:**
Planting sparse bamboo and towering pines,
To accompany my carefree idleness.
Dense shade covers the cold moss below,
Sitting, I stroke a three-*chi* zither.
Within the cave, crisp and refreshing air,
Between the trees, a rustling clear wind.

**The Fifty-Ninth:**
Long An’s crowned heroes, aged and weary,
Exhausted on the road.
A mere thousand *li* of dusty worldly toil—
White hair like silk, what success remains?
Better the Daoist’s life:
Refining the Nine-Turn Elixir red.

**The Sixtieth:**
Autumn high, I cut *huang jing* with my own hand,
Gradually sensing vitality restored.
A decade’s old ailments worn away—
Yet when meeting others, never speak of longevity.
Thanks to the cow-riding Daoist,
Who last night gifted me *zhī* mushrooms.

---
**The Golden Character Scripture**
*Learning Dao must learn to become a Celestial Daoist.*
Refining the Golden Elixir preserves life entirely.
*Entire*—before *Xi Huang* drew the first trigrams.
*Prenatal qi*, the master’s secret transmission.

**The Second:**
The Great Elixir’s medicine is not hard to seek.

**The Third:**
Every home has its seed—self-cultivation is possible.
Cultivation: rest and depart from the elixir furnace.
From the void arises, the *Kàn* trigram inverted, high and received.
**The Fourth:**
The Golden Elixir’s wondrous Dao is a great divine power.
Descend and gather the White Tiger, subdue the Red Dragon.
The Dragon: simmered and refined in a jade tripod.
In a moment’s use, the *yin-yang* transformative work is done.
**The Fifth:**
The enlightened light penetrates the original school.
Boundless *dharma* realms, one essence unified.
Unified: with Zen mind.
Empty yet not empty.
Thus, the *Tathāgatas* and Laozi share the same *rúhuà* essence.

**The Sixth:**
Cultivate the True Nature, restore the original complete truth.
Free and unbounded, one beyond all things.
Beyond: no greed, no suffering, no anger.
Longevity’s matter—spring blooms on the apricot branch.

**The Seventh:**
Good deeds: eight hundred virtues, three thousand practices.
Roam the Four Seas, guide those with affinity.
Affinity: the Nine-Palace Elixir Decree proclaims.
Riding the *luán* crane and *hè* heron,
Join the ranks before the Celestial Court.

**The Eighth:**
Perception, hearing, and awareness all cease.
Awakening to true emptiness—pass the exam and return.
Return: pierce the *zào huà* mechanism.
Not difficult, yet beyond—eternal *kalpa*, heaven and earth aligned.

**The Ninth:**
Heaven’s secrets leaked—exhort the learned.
Not ordinary *qiánhuì*—Dao wisdom does not pass through.
Through: sweep away and uphold the orthodox school.
Diligently cultivate, and the *rúhuà* essence flows—
Daoist saints and immortals arise.

---
**The [Middle Lǚ] "Welcome the Daoist Guest"**
The *Hùnyuán* Pearl—priceless treasure.
Collected at the Red Water Stream’s edge.
Its hue is blurred, its light clear and bright.
Held firmly in hand, it judges all worldly affairs.

**The Second:**
No schemes, no contrivance.

**The [Middle Lǚ] "Welcome the Daoist Guest" (Continued)**

**The Third:**
Sun and moon vie in urging—never aging.
A boat sails backward, oars turned upside down.
Who knows this one—*qīngjìng jiāfēng* so pure and good.
**The Third:**
Water deep and clear, mountains in fine hue.
All worldly strife and bias—none reach here.
Bamboo windows dim, thatched roof small.
True joy within—do not speak of it to mortals.

**The Fourth:**
Bamboo wind soft, flowers cast heavy shadows.
One cup of wine, three pluckings of the *qín*.
Reveal the *xuàn* of heaven’s workings,
Hide its wondrous uses.
At the *huáitán* of willow and locust,
Ministers and generals see through life’s fleeting dream.

**The Fifth:**
By gnarled willow’s shade, beneath pine’s shadow.
Stand upright—all ties dissolved.
Lock the heart-monkey, seize the mind-horse.
With whom share tales of longevity beneath moon and wind?

**The Sixth:**
Han Zhongli left office, rank and title abandoned.
Awakening from *Nánkē*’s dream, he cast aside the golden seal.
Straw sandals light, millet staff steady.
Laughing with sun and moon, he strides alone in the realm of longevity.

**The Seventh:**
Lü Dongbin transcends the mundane.
Divine light pierces the *sāniàn jiè* of existence.
Discarding fame and fortune—like common weeds.
With a staff of tortoise-shell hair, one strike shatters heaven and earth.

**The Eighth:**
From *Hùnyuán*’s dawn, Zhang Guolao appears.
A white donkey treads the void, inverted in flight.
Purple clouds rise, red mists swirl.
In one night’s gulp, he devours the Penglai Isles.

**The Ninth:**
Lan Caihe departs from worldly ways.
His hand strikes a clapper against cold *jù*.
He shakes the celestial gates, rocks the earthly axis.
With moon and wind, he sings his own hymn of longevity.

**The Tenth:**
Liu Haichan, the Yan Chancellor.
In dreams, he sees through empty red censers—
A single snowflake struck, then released.
Far from mortal paths, he departs the sea’s heights.
A golden statue—his likeness.

**The Eleventh:**
Guangchengzi, a thousand and two hundred.
High on Kongtong, he sleeps in cold white clouds.
The Sage of Emperors, the Dwelling of Heaven and Earth.
Roaming freely, beyond names—
A guest outside all things.

**The Twelfth:**
Fan Li, who once aided Yue.
Alone, he drifts on the Five Lakes in a moonlit skiff.
Forgotten are right and wrong,
Severed are fame and gain.
A lone short flute—
Enjoying the snow on reeds.

**The Thirteenth:**
Zhang Zifang, who upheld the Great Han.

**The Eighteenth:**
Let them wear crimson and jade robes—
My heart is free of care, my body at ease.
Few in the world are so cunning and sly as this one.

**The Nineteenth:**
Worldly affairs are done, how serene and secluded.
The recluse beneath the trees, unbound and unrestrained.
Before the emerald cliffs, friends of wind and moon.
Drunken songs and wild dances—
Gulping down the elixir of eternal life.

**The Twentieth:**
Drunk, I sleep; awake, I rub my head.
Fallen east or west, I know no shame.
No spring, no autumn—
Only boundless vitality, enjoying prolonged years.

**The Twenty-First:**
Returning with herbs, white clouds drift.
Mist locks the green mountains, the immortal path lost.
Black apes cry, green crows tread.
A crane dances ahead, leading me back to the cave.

**The Twenty-Second:**
Inside the cave, the bamboo door is shut.
A youthful immortal awaits, poised for a game of chess.
When bored, I drink from a jade cup.
My straw sandals trip me—
I sleep without removing my clothes.

**The Twenty-Third:**
The cliffs are steep and strange.
Cypress, pine, and green pines encircle me.
Silent, no one passes by.
Loneliness and ease, cold detachment in leisure.

**The Twenty-Fourth:**
My face is sour from stale rice,
A cracked wooden bowl, a broken bamboo strainer.
No divine grace, only pickled greens.
Content with my portion, better than rare delicacies.

**The Twenty-Fifth:**
I wear grass sandals, a hemp rope tied.
A patched raincoat, a gourd hung by my side.
Half fisherman, half woodcutter.
My hair wild, my face grimed—
Let others laugh.

**The Twenty-Sixth:**
They mock me as an exile—I know it well.
My true companions are moon and wind.
Outside, white clouds—
Blowing a jade flute.
Such tastes the world cannot fathom.

*Once, in Water-Bamboo Village,*
*I raged like the wind at Sweet River’s ford.*
*Seven golden lotuses, fresh and bright.*
*Among the hills, Liu, Tan, Ma, Hao, Wang, and Sun.*

**The Second [Poem]:**
*(Note: This appears to be a separate, standalone poem appended to the series.)*

**The Twenty-Seventh:**
I once was born in Ma Half-State.
With my Master, I spoke of fate’s design.
Alone in garden walls, I turned inward to refine.
When virtue and practice reached their peak, I journeyed to Penglai Isle.
*His Third [Poem]:*

**The Twenty-Eighth:**
My true name, in the Four Great’s guise, is Tan.
In past lives, I met my Master and cast off worldly ties.
Roaming clouds, I never stayed in any temple’s shade.
When virtue and practice reached their peak, I ascended to the Celestial Stage.
*His Fourth [Poem]:*

**The Twenty-Ninth:**
My birthplace was Laizhou’s Wuguan.
I met my Master, surnamed Changsheng.
Through alleys and willow lanes, I wandered without hindrance.
Unsoiled by dust, my nature shone as bright as moon.
*His Fifth [Poem]:*

**The Thirtieth:**
By imperial decree, I was granted purple robes in Tianchang.
Now I am Cloudlight Ironfoot Wang.
When I met my Master, I journeyed to Luoyang.
Virtue and practice complete, I reached my Master’s Celestial Homeland.
*His Sixth [Poem]:*

**The Thirty-First:**
At nineteen, I cast off home and worldly fate,
And at Banxi’s ford, I set my resolve and found peace.
I realized the Eternal Spring’s endless day.
The Great Dao’s gate stands open, its teachings passed through ages.
*His Seventh [Poem]:*

**The Thirty-Second:**
From ancient times to now, I speak of fate’s design.
Beneath Zhaozhou’s bridge, I spent my years.
Singing by the bridge, the water does not flow.
When one leaf falls, the autumn comes to all below.
*His Eighth [Poem]:*

---

**The First [Poem] of the *Fangtong Tree* [Series]:**
At the first watch, I wrap myself in meditation.
The wandering mind and restless thoughts are bound and struck.
Do not let idle play distract.
In silent stillness, I refine the Embryonic Breath.
The gates of Heaven and Earth, once sealed, now open wide.
Thus, the truth of Dao’s mysteries is truly revealed.

**The Second [Poem]:**
At the second watch, I share the universe’s essence.
A spark of spirit gradually pierces through.
The Tiger and Dragon first unite, their rigor complete.
The Three Vermin must not flee.
The Wisdom Blade in the void avenges wrongs.

**The Third [Poem]:**
I sever the heads of all demons.
**The Fourth [Poem]:**
At the third watch, I stir the Dynamic Yang.
In gold cauldron I refine, in jade furnace I cook.
True lead and mercury are forged.
The artisan’s hand carves open the jade lotus pod.
Two rays of crimson light illuminate the Kunlun peak.
Ten thousand pearls descend as treasures.

**The Fifth [Poem]:**
At the fourth watch, the clouds disperse completely.
The tortoise and star of the sea’s depths play with the bright moon.
Everywhere, jade flowers bloom.
The fire’s intensity is adjusted with precision, following the seasons’ rhythms.
At the child and wu hours, the qi rises, descending crimson dross.
I boldly reveal the secrets of Heaven.

**The Sixth [Poem]:**
At the fifth watch, in drowsy stillness, I am settled.
My mind nurtures the vast moon—a single mirror of clarity.
It pierces through greed and wrath’s afflictions.
This time, even ghosts and gods must tremble.
Only true purity is true stillness.
When virtue is complete, I ascend to the Celestial Sage.
Step by step, I rise.

**The Seventh [Poem]:**
At the first watch, I sit with a clear heart, sleeves unfurled.
The Monkey and Horse are firmly bound and locked.
The Wisdom Blade is sharpened.
The Six Bandits and Three Vermin all flee in panic.
The host of demons is driven back.
Even in sleep, I rest in my clothes.
Upon waking, the drowsy wind clears and sends me forth.
I awaken to the Peach Blossom Spring’s cave.
At the gate of the Underworld’s realm,
I leisurely visit Master San Mao—my joy knows no end.
The wind through the window stirs.
I awaken from my Wandering Immortal’s dream.

**The Second [Poem]:**
At the second watch, I sleep by the White Ox Brook.
The herdsman drunkenly stumbles, lost in wine.
His rain hat and cloak lie piled.
Beneath the moon, the flute’s tune is just begun—
Joyfully, I return.
Returning to the Land of Hua Xiu,
I embrace its boundless ease.
With leisure, I pluck the jade zither’s strings—
Its notes soar high.
From the fire emerges the tortoise bearing white cranes.
I play the cloud-flute.
Purple mist and crimson light shine bright.

**The Third [Poem]:**
At the third watch, the Milky Way’s stars fade thin.
I step outside, my body searching.
The moon hangs due south.
The Two Eights’ maiden pairs with the youthful boy—
Refining the Three Threes.
I seize the Celestial Pass and shake it.
In the Five Bright Hall, the Primordial Star gathers.
Ascending the Seven Treasure Mountain, I depart.
I pray to the Jade Void.
The Primordial Beginning hangs the millet-pearls aloft.
I inscribe the Golden Script.
The land prospers, the people thrive in wealth.

**The Fourth [Poem]:**
At the fourth watch, the Mysterious Enclosure’s breeze is fine.
Coming and going, no obstruction remains.
I loosen my filthy robes.
The Heart-Moon hangs high, illuminating the Cloudy Brook.
I climb the Heavenly Ladder.
Alone, I pluck the moon’s jade from the Rabbit’s Palace.
In the Three Realms and Ten Directions, I walk unmatched.
I recognize the path to Caoqi.
Nothing remains.
True joy, true delight—drinking the cream of bliss.
No need to buy.
I sing the soundless melody.

**The Fifth [Poem]:**
At the fifth watch, the Golden Rooster crows upon its frame.
The wayfarers below are sprightly in their gait,
As dawn approaches.
I lift the basketless staff to stir the bottomless depths.
A gusting wind I cross—
Together we journey to the Penglai Isle.
Who else knows this family’s wind?
No need to fear decay or old age.
I strike the *Lángbǎn* drum—
In the deep jade waves, I fish for whales and turtles.
Emerging from the billows,
I gather the elixir of longevity.
*"Nánxiāng Zǐ"*:
True mercury with true lead,
Born in the Primordial and Post-Heaven realms.
When the time is known, pluck and gather with diligence—
The Mysterious Mystery.
If the acupoint is lost, why fret?
To become a transcendent, no need.
The fire must be refined and unwavering,
Examining the *qiàn* before and after.
From *Lián* (屯) I draw, and in *Méng* (蒙) I cease—
Hard to teach.
A single hair’s misstep will not yield the elixir.

**The Second [Poem]:**
With both hands, I split the *Hóngméng* [cosmic egg].
The wisdom-sword flies forth to the first peak.
Outer Daoists and *xiūluó* [demonic beings] are startled, their necks drawn tight—
Divine powers.
The transformation was always within my grasp.
I forge the *yù* [jade] and *hú* [fire] in the alchemical furnace—red.
The *qí* [key] and *suǒ* [lock] are blown by the *xùn* [conforming] wind.
In the tenth month, I shed my form and swallow it within—
*Kūn* [Earth] Palace:
Instantly, the Three Pure Ones and the Grandest Ancestor appear.

**The Third [Poem]:**
I nurture the *xiàng* [form] through the *Zhōutiān* [Cosmic Cycle].
The fire must be gentle yet complete.
To cherish the infant, only the mother’s care suffices—
Three years.
I apply and refine the *xiàng* [form], drawing and adding as it wanes and returns.
At the confluence of the *Niúdǒu* [Big Dipper] and the River,
I abandon and take the Mysterious Pearl to sow the Jade Field.
My resolve is steady as I govern the fire’s stages—
Refined and unwavering.
I split the abdomen clearly and explain it to the worthy.

**The Fourth [Poem]:**
Life’s *jiǎ* [first stage] gives way to its *gēng* [second stage].
This is the elixir’s kernel—clearly mark it.
Gather the tender herbs and return them to the earthen pot—
To simmer and refine.
Yield and hardness, strength and softness, proceed in order.
A single dose will yield the elixir.
Bathing and guarding against peril, I hold fast to the city.
Here, no need to govern the fire’s stages—
Hold the fullness.
If fire is added, it will surely topple.

**The Fifth [Poem]:**
Carve and wrap the effort—uniformly applied.
With earnest study, probe the elixir’s every detail,
Not a hair’s breadth overlooked.
Ten months of diligent self-preservation.

**The Sixth [Poem]:**
The Cauldron’s method mirrors Heaven and Earth—
Above, the Celestial Primordium; below, the Terrestrial.
If one can reverse and invert their operation,
Alternating and exchanging,
Opening and closing cycle through the Eight Gates,
Lifting to Kunlun’s heights.
The Tortoise and Serpent brothers spit and swallow.
At the hundred-foot pole’s peak, grip the line tight—
Lift and surge.
From here, the Original Spirit and life endure forever.

**The Seventh [Poem]:**
The Passages lock within the Microcosmic Orbit.
Ascending and descending cycle through the Three-Inch Field.
Not in exhaling, inhaling, or counting breaths—
It is natural.
Nine transformations without loss, fire’s power complete.
Fetal breathing is but idle talk.
The key lies in balancing yin and yang—
No deviation.
All breathing, blowing, and exhaling rely on the Gentle Wind,
Soft and enduring.
The marvel lies in the fore-strand and the after-strand.

**The Eighth [Poem]:**
The *Kàn* [Returning] hexagram rises with the Hidden Dragon.
Stealthily adjust *wu-jǐ* [the fifth and sixth stems]—
Do not yet assault.
At the second line, the Dragon appears, mastering the hexagram,
Divine efficacy.
From here, the furnace’s stages turn crimson in order.
The *Tài* [Peace] hexagram meets again.
Fierce fire burns *qián* [the creative], aided by the Gentle Wind.
Refined, the Yellow Sprout and White Snow emerge—
Extraordinary achievement.
Returning, it follows the *Kūn* [Earth] path to completion.

**The Ninth [Poem]:**
Recognize the Metal within Water.
Smelting and refining deepen its essence.
Advance and retreat, drawing the sacrificial—
Nine transformations, floating and sinking.
Nurture the Hidden Dragon, then let it ascend.
Marvelous operation from the Heavenly Heart.
Relying on the Yellow Nurse—*bǐng-rén* [the third and ninth stems]—
Ferment the cream, descending from the mountain peak,
Pouring again and again.
Slowly plucking the stringless lute’s single note.

**The Tenth [Poem]:**
The eldest son proceeds to the Western Quarter.
The maiden returns to *Kūn* [Earth], transforming into six *yáng* [male/positive] lines.
Then it is time to apply effort and cultivate the *Èr-Bā* [Two-Eight, i.e., the Eight Trigrams].
Fortify the banks.

From the Nine Quarters, the Dao/Way itself flourishes.
The Bull and Dipper constellations deliberate together.
Artistry surpasses Heaven’s craft—wonder beyond compare.
The High *Kàn* [Abyss] and its spouse consummate their union;
Hard to forget.

Only now does one perceive the *Hú* [Caulron]’s eternal sun and moon.

**The Eleventh [Poem]:**
White Snow and Yellow Sprout—
Two refined essences of the same luminous family.
Plucking and selecting, discerning decline and vigor,
Worthy of praise.

Not a hair’s breadth may the fire’s intensity vary.
At the summit, the Three Flowers bloom.
The Ram Chariot and Deer Chariot move in harmony.
The Hare and Tortoise pass between the South and North,
Their interplay ceaseless.

From here, the Heavenly River stirs with steady oars.

**The Twelfth [Poem]:**
Purity complete, revealing Heaven’s design.
Only fear that contemporaries remain lost in delusion.
The pearl beneath the chin must be seized with vigor—
Do not delay.

The Dao/Way lies within the body—
Who else could question it?
Cast off the dust-net swiftly.
A hundred years of life, yet seven [critical] moments are rare.
Do not wait until old age when lead and mercury dwindle—
Worthy of lament.

Karmic retribution’s path is hard to deceive oneself.
An inch of gold—
Worthy of sighing over the multitude of deluded ones,
How few awaken to the dream’s empty blossoms.

「Yet adorned with embroidered brocade curtains and copper peaks,
With crimson shoes and jade hairpins—
What use are they to the body in the end?

Better than the dusty world,
Are secluded bamboo fences and humble cottages.
Beneath the green pines,
A single verse of lofty song—
Laughing defiantly as the years transform into ages.

**The Realm of the Purple Palace,**
Spring’s light pure,
When the refined gather—
Wondrous existence, true delight.
See the natural celestial music,
Star towers and moon palaces,
Cranes soaring, phoenixes dancing.

In the depths of white clouds,
Within the wine cup—
A landscape of divine immortals.
Who would willingly turn back to youth?

**The Realm of Effortless Wandering,**
Only I return,
Then re-enter the boundless void of **Leiyang**.*

**The Second [Poem]:**
**Appreciating Snow**

The evening wild geese cry mournfully,
And the late earthly hums echo—
Cold winds arise together.
Frost forms with severity,
Dark clouds gather uniformly—
The Four Seas display the auspicious jade dragon.

Snowflakes dot a thousand households with pristine beauty,
Ice blossoms unfold in radiant splendor.
The finest moment is when,
Inviting poetic companions,
We surround the brazier with paper screens, lost in intoxication.

Reciting,
We seek exquisite verses—
Outside the bamboo, a fresh fragrance;
Golden threads spurt new buds.

Like scattered silver grains,
Or powdered butterflies,
Flitting high and low in empty embrace.
It is known that this is a sign of great peace,
A premonition of **Yin-Yang** harmony.

This profound truth,
When shared with a kindred spirit like **Zi You**,
Reveals the genuine flavor of the rivers and skies.

**The Seventh Movement of the *Wuling* Series concludes.**
#1 The following nineteen pieces are all **danci** (散曲小令).
#2 The following nine pieces are all **danci** (散曲小令).
#3 The following twenty-five pieces are all **danci** (散曲小令).

**The Eighth Movement of the *Wuling* Series:**
*Siming at Xianyou Mountain by Daoist Priest Peng Zhizhong*

**Western River Moon #1**
**[Attributed to Zhang Boduan]**」

**#1**
Inner elixirs are like outer elixirs—
Inner must harmonize with outer.
The cinnabar essence blends as kindred does.
Nourishing warmth works in myriad ways.
Within lies natural celestial fire,
Flame-red and blazing in the furnace.
The outer furnace’s fuel must be adjusted with diligence.
No art surpasses the true seed.

**#2**
This Dao is most divine and sacred,
Yet its weight for rulers is light—hard to dispel.
Refining lead and mercury takes more than a morning.
Early glimpse the black pearl’s omen.
If worthy men would cultivate,
Why dwell in markets or courtly halls?
The practice is simple, though the elixir is not distant.
Speak of it, and men will laugh in scorn.

**#3**
The White Tiger’s essence is supreme treasure,
The divine pool’s waters—true gold refined.
Thus, the highest virtue’s source runs deep.
Not like common medicines.
To forge the Nine Transformations,
First refine the self and steady the mind.
Take at the proper time—let not float or sink.
Increase the fire, but guard against peril.

**#4**
Seven returns of cinnabar restore its root,
Nine returns of golden liquid restore its truth.
Do not fixate on the hours of *Yin* and *Yang* or *Kun* and *Shen*.
Observe the Five Phases for measure.
It is but mercury in essence,
Circulating through all celestial phases.
When *Yin* and *Yang* qi are full, it naturally becomes numinous.
Its emergence and retreat never leave the Mysterious Female.

**#5**
To retain true lead and bind mercury,
The inner minister never strays from home.
Wood and metal, though separated, meet without cause—
They need the Yellow Matchmaker’s aid.
Wood’s nature loves metal’s righteousness,
Metal’s passion clings to wood’s benevolence.
Devouring, consuming, yet ever close—
Only then does the man bear fruit.

**#6**
Which household’s maiden of twenty-eight,
Which lord of thirty-nine?
They call themselves Wood Elixir and Metal Essence—
Only when they meet the Earth do they form the Three Families.
Further refined by Master Ding’s tempering,
Then husband and wife at last unite in joy.
The River Chariot dares not pause,
Carried to Kunlun’s peak.

**#7**
The love of Ox and Girl aligns with the Dao,
Tortoise and Serpent share their natural kindred.
The Toad and Crow meet at the New Moon’s brilliance,
Their two *qi* intermingle in motion.
All is the wondrous workings of Heaven and Earth—
Who can fathom this profound abyss?
When *Yin* and *Yang* are severed, fault arises.
How could one endure Heaven’s length and Earth’s span?

**#8**
The Male encloses the Female within,
Bearing *Yin* while embracing *Yang* essence.
The two combine—medicine is complete.
Refining soul and spirit to their finest.
Truly, one grain of Golden Elixir—
When the serpent swallows, it becomes a dragon.
Even chicken feed transforms into phoenix and *peng*.
Soaring into the True Realm of Azure Yang.

**#9**
Heaven and Earth have just passed through *Pi* and *Tai*—
Morning and evening, recognize *Lún* and *Méng*.
Radiating wheels converge at the hub, water pays homage to the center.
The marvel lies in adding and subtracting with precision.
Gain one, and all things are accomplished—
No need to distinguish east, west, south, or north.
Diminish again, and guard against undoing past efforts.
Treasure life—do not trifle with it lightly.

**#10**
At Winter Solstice, *Yin* returns to *Yang*’s rebirth,
Three decades add one *Yang* line.
Midmonth, the *Gua* reverses at dawn’s first light.
After the full moon, *Kàn* ends—stains appear.
Days further divide into cold and heat,
*Yang* rises again in midnight’s hour.
At noon, the *Guà* symbol—one *Yin* ascends.
Refining elixir must know dawn and dusk.

**#11**
Virtue cultivated beyond eight hundred,
*Yin* merit accumulated to three thousand.

「The harmonious balance of things unites me with kin and grievance.
At first, the aspiration for immortality and divine beings was kindled.
Tigers and rhinoceroses, blades and armies do not harm,
Yet the fleeting fire of the mortal abode cannot be constrained.

A precious talisman descends—leaving courtly service behind,
Steadily riding the *luan* carriage and *feng* palanquin.

**#12**
Without discerning the Five *Xing* and Four *Xiang*,
One does not distinguish cinnabar (*zhu*), mercury (*gong*), lead, or silver.
The methods of refining the elixir’s fire are unheard of,
Yet early on, one is hailed as a recluse (*juyin*).

Unwilling to reflect on one’s own errors,
One further misleads others with false teachings.
Fearful that others remain lost in the *Mijin* (crossing of delusion) for eternal ages,
One endures deceit with a hardened heart.

**#13**
The elixir is the supreme treasure of the colored body (*seshin*),
Refined, its transformations are boundless.
It can further ascend to explore the true *Zong* (essence),
Unraveling the wondrous use of non-birth (*wusheng*).
No need to rely on another’s merit in future ages—
Divine powers are gained in this very life.

Since the Dragon Maiden (*Longnü*) undertook this labor,
Who afterward could follow in her footsteps?

**#14**
*(Attributed to Xiao Tingzhi)*
With two hands, one cleaves apart the *Hun* (chaos),
Revealing the Dao/Way of refining the elixir plainly.
The *rihun* (solar essence) and *yuepo* (lunar spirit) move from west to east,
Seize them firmly—do not let them slip away.
Outer *Dao/Way* and heretical *mo* (demons) shrink in fear,
All vying to bind treasure within the inner palace (*zhonggong*).
The Nine *Huan* and Seven *Fan* (alchemical cycles) are achieved in an instant,
Yet all depend on the Yellow Woman (*Huangpo*)’s guidance.

**#15**
Silently harnessing the *buqian* (mysterious transformations) of *Yin* and *Yang*,
The marvel lies in the precision of adding and subtracting—
Found in the convergence of *Tun* and *Meng* (trigram symbols).」

**#16**
To recognize the true *qian* (lead) and true *gong* (mercury),
All derived from a single root source.
The alchemical *fire* (huǒ) and timing are profound in their mystery—
Only the true adept can discern them.

When gathering, do not err in season or day,
Still distinguish the *hai* (posterior) from the *xian* (anterior).
In the *jinyu* (jade furnace), a moment’s heat sears the heavens,
The *Dao/Way*’s person (*Zhenren*) appears without rank.

**#17**
Do not ask of the *Nine* (9) and *Three* (3), nor the *Two* (2) and *Eight* (8),
For there is no excess in *Yin*’s even or *Yang*’s odd.
Mostly, high *Kan* (water) and low *Gen* (mountain) form the union.
Recognize *Tun* and *Meng*—they are the key.

If you pass the first *Yang* (male) ascent,
Then you may advance the fire without delay.
For the slightest misstep lies in the hairsbreadth,
And reckless *wild alchemy* (*yèzhàn*) demands precision.

**#18**
The *ding* (cauldron) and *qi* (vessel) follow the *Tian* (Heaven) and *Di* (Earth) symbols,
*Kan* (water) and *Li* (fire) in operation show no deviation.
The *husband* and *wife* meet in the *Huang* (Yellow) household,
Speaking of the *wu sheng* (non-born) marvels.

Rain’s intent and clouds’ emotions are fully understood,
At the *Ling* (peak) head, the *jia* (vehicle) is urged forward.
Returning to the summit, the *Nine* and *Three* bloom—
Seal the *jinyuan* (jade gate) with *golden locks* (*jīnsuǒ*).

**#19**
Stirring the *top* (dǐng) and *gate* (mén) closures,
The tiger roars and dragon hums naturally.
The *Nine* return and *Seven* return—profound in meaning,
Entering and exiting never stray from the *mystic female* (*Xuǎnpìn*).

Using the *jinyu* (jade furnace) at the right *fire* (huǒ) moment,
True *gold* (*zhenjīn*) is refined within the cauldron.
When the *qi* (vital force) is strong and the battle won,
The secret lies in no harm, no loss.

**#20**

**#21**
Returning twice to nourish the *fire* (yǎnghuǒ),
The rabbit and rooster bathe in concealment.
The clear transformations manifest at the center,
The *playing pearl* (xuánzhū) is sealed and refined.

**#22**
Pressing between the *spine* (jiājǐ) and dual *gates*,
Piercing to the *top* (dǐng)—this is the **Great Dao’s Mystic Portal** (*Dàdào Xuánmén*).
The *golden elixir* (jīndān) is but this **School’s Root-Power** (*zōnggēn lìdà yào*).
Know the moment to stir and transport it.
Nurturing warmth, defending the *city* (*shòuchéng*), and wild battles,
Frequently ingesting the *flowering pool’s* (huāchí) *jade nectar* (yùyè).
Always use the *jade furnace* (yùlú) with gentle, warming *fire* (huǒ).
Gather herbs, discerning their maturity—whether aged or tender.

**#23**
The *Nine Oils* (jiǔyóu) surge upward against the tide,
In an instant, they rush past the *Heavenly Heart* (*Tiānxīn*).
On Kunlun’s peak, the waters are pure and clear—
Fermenting the *celestial fluid* (qióngjiāng) for self-nourishment.
At this very moment, begin to gather and refine,
The *River Vehicle* (héchē) transports without pause.
The *One Qi* (*yīqì*) of *Yin-Yang* is naturally captured and sunk.
Seal the *jade gate* (yùguān) with steadfast locks.

**#24**
The *medicine* (yào) is born in the southwest *Kun* (earthly branch) land,
The *golden elixir* (jīndān) is its true root-school.
Students must diligently ponder and exhaust its depths—
Its marvel surpasses all, unmatched by true essence.

**#25**
The Great Dao of *Golden Elixir* (jīnyè huándān) is the ancient path,
Transmitted through eons by the sages of old.
With bared heart and split belly, their scrolls are revealed—
Guiding souls beyond the Dao’s shore.
Do not marvel at the heavens’ secrets being laid bare,
For beyond the *Play of Mysteries* (Xuánxuán), there is no deeper mystery.
Left to the ancients and the worthy of name—
Those with ears shall clearly perceive.

**#26**
A full stomach harms the heart and depletes the *qi*,
Excessive sleep entangles one in dreams, obscuring the True.
When the eyes move, the spirit is lost; when the ears listen, the *Lingtai* (spiritual platform) grows dim.
To behold the Original Face, wield the *wisdom-blade* to sever the red dust.
Unfeeling response to things is the natural truth—
This is the swiftest path of cultivation.

**#27**
Sudden enlightenment reveals the Dao’s principles:
Banish desire, conquer sleep, and subdue the demonic foes.
Avoiding fame and gain, one faces fewer storms.
Laziness and drift pass as one follows fate.
Hunger drives one to beg for scraps in the streets,
While satiety invites aimless wandering.
In leisure, one sings at ancient temples—
Who else roams so freely as I?

**#28**
Wealth and honor cannot enter me, nor does poverty trouble me.
With fate and destiny, disputes arise—
Yet without fortune or misfortune, there is no calamity.
Let them indulge in extravagance, for even a gourd and bowl sustain life.
I counsel you not to labor in vain—
When the Great Limit arrives, how can one flee?

**#29**
First, do not slight the teacher nor disregard the method.
Second, recite the pure *Immortal Scriptures* (xiānjīng).
Third, preserve the True *qi* to nourish the spirit.
Fourth, sweep away all dust and toil.
Fifth, sever the darkness of ignorance’s fire,
Sixth, cast off the shackles of worldly emotions.
Seventh, tame the *monkey* and *horse*—eternal peace follows.
Eighth, drink the *Eight Immortals’ Elixir* (bāxiān zhēng).

*Yǒngyùlè* (Joy of Eternity):
All cultivate, all swallow—who grasps the True Dao?
Crooked paths and minor methods mislead many.
Róngchéng was no immortal—his herb-gathering was in vain.
One day, stripped from the vat’s depths, his nature crumbles.
Better to turn inward, embrace *wuwei* (non-action), and study the original *Zhuāngzi-Laozi*.
Align *Yin-Yang*, refine *lead* and *mercury*—the *Eight Trigrams* mark the foundation.
Life is a dream, years like arrows—turn back while you may.
Clinging to spring flowers and autumn moons—when will it end?

**Part Two**
All *dharma* arises from the heart; observe the *Dharmadhātu* (Law-realm)—all is mind-made.
Buddha and Dao converge; measure not, yet never depart—
The heart itself is the Way.
Since knowing *Kàn* and *Lí* (water and fire),
Mixing and refining elixirs, one dimly grasps dawn and dusk.
See the rooster fly to the *Tianhuang* (Heavenly Palace),
The hare race across the *Danque* (Elixir Gate)—no more affliction.
Within the *qi*, the True Fluid; within the Fluid, the True *qi*—
Harmonized, neither too much nor too little.
Sowing the yellow sprout, refining into red water,
The *Dragon* and *Tiger* entwine in their embrace.
Nine returns, seven refineries—when the work is complete,
I reclaim my youth of old.
Await the three thousand cycles,
When merit is fulfilled and the path is round—
Then it is done.

**Part Three**
Cultivate the Dao, preserve the heart, refine the spirit—
Lightness must be the aim.
Restore the marrow, return the essence—
Flowing water does not rot, the door-hinge never decays.
The *sun-soul* and *moon-shadow* reunite in the furnace—
True *qi* gathers naturally.
Tame the heart-monkey, recall the mind-horse—
No trace of dust remains.
Within stillness, clarity emerges—
When *Yang Dragon* and *Yin Tiger* merge, water and fire blend—this is the measure.
The *Eight Segments of Marvelous Text*, the *Thousand-Mouthed Living Method*—
Above, there is a path.
Lǚ Gōng’s lofty virtue does not abandon the world—
If one has the portion, they must meet.

Across the *Ten Isles* and *Three Mountains*,
Mounting *Luan* and *Hè*, we depart together.

**Part Four**

**Part One**
Nurture water, nurture essence, nurture spirit, nurture blood—
First, one must nurture *qi*.
Sun and moon, yin and yang,
The six lines, the eight *guà*—
Study closely the *Cān Tóng Qì* [参同契].

An empty body, an empty treasure—
A thousand words, ten thousand phrases—
All boil down to two characters: *Kǎn* and *Gāo* [坎高].

Ascending Kunlun’s peak,
Returning to the origin, restoring the root—
One must clarify beginning and end.

Though the body be small,
It mirrors heaven and earth—
Eighty-four thousand *lǐ* vast.

The *Xuān Dàn* gate [玄牝],
Giving birth to myriad transformations—
All lies within *Chōng Hé* [冲和].

This is the true truth beyond;
No other ultimate truth exists—
Only then does one believe in the *One Dao*.

When we meet again with Zhōng Lǚ [钟吕],
If there remain unclear points,
I beg the Master’s guidance.

---
**Song: *Yú Jiā Ào* [渔家傲]**
The Ultimate Dao is not distant—it lies near.
A hair’s breadth misstep is like a thousand *lǐ* apart.

The Dao is hard to seek, yet its source is simple.
If we meet in harmony,
A single leap reaches the Buddha’s realm.

When water and fire merge—*Jì Jì* [既济]—
The *Three Corpses* and *Six Bandits* all retreat.
This alone grants eternal life and keen vision.

Body, speech, mind—
Transformed into one point of *Chōng Hé* *qi*.

---
**Part Two**
Spirit is nature, *qi* is life—
Let not the spirit stray, then the heart will settle.
Fortunate to have Master Cuī’s *Yào Jìng* [药镜].

If one attains ultimate truth,
The Whole Truth steadies, rooted in stillness.
Master and guest—inner clarity, outer response—
The *Líng Tái* [灵台] radiates celestial brilliance.
Two jars, one scene.

Hasten your cultivation—
Do not wait until thirst drives you to dig the well.

---
**Part Three**
Nurture essence to root the spirit, guard *qi*—
Heaven’s child and mother never part.
Keep this in mind day and night, through all six hours.

Within the *Three Fields* [三田],
Warm, harmonious—heaven and earth’s balanced water.
Before the Twelve Towers, white snow clings;
By the Nine Palaces, yellow sprouts rise.
At the Sun-Moon Mountains, we pay homage to the Emperor.

Spirit-light ascends—
The body soars beyond the misty heights.

---
**Part Four**
I possess a luminous pearl with no price—
Its light eternally shines upon the *Zhī Tián* [芝田].
No *zhī* or *hū* [之乎] here.

Few are the true listeners in this world.
A million rays of essence, spirit-guarded—
Four hundred and four ailments vanish.
The Fire Dragon returns to *Zào Huà* [造化].

The immortal chariot departs—
