Not a speck of dust follows the steed.

---
**Song: *Cù Pāi Mǎn Lù Huā* [促拍满路花]**
Embracing the Primordial, one can guard the One—
The Four Great Elements then rest in ease.
The heart must reflect inward—
How often does it find leisure?

The Golden Crow surges—
Flying into the molten silver basin.

Heart is Dao—
Dao is in the heart—
Where else should one seek the elixir?

---
**Part Two**
Why cling to robes and honors,
Desiring to transcend the world?
Glory lasts but a few days—
Then it withers and falls.

Cultivating the True is easy,
But piling up deeds and merits is hard.
I urge you to do good—
The Five Turbidities, the Three Realms—
Transformed into cloud-isles, spirit mountains.

---
**Part Three**
If one remains ever serene and still,
Heaven and earth all return to it.
One True contains all marvels—
Entering *Xī Yí* [希夷].

Zhāo Wén [昭文] does not comprehend—
*Qi* and climate have their gains and losses.
Deluded thoughts extinguished,
Hunger, sleep, action—all cease.

---
**Part Four**
The furnace and cauldron form naturally—
Luster shines through the curtains.
Jade Pool’s spirit-water surges—
Above, fertility blooms.

Like fish drinking water—
Cold and warmth, each knows its own.

One’s own life and fate—
One’s own enlightenment—
One’s own life and fate is most convenient.

---
**Part Five**
Speaking of cultivation and nurturing—
How many paths exist?
Truly, return to the source—
The Void Origin.

The Ultimate Truth, the Ultimate Dao—
Simple, encompassing heaven and earth.
*Kǎn* and birds, water and fire—
Just a net and snare,
Yet one enduring point remains.

---
**Part Six**
If one truly offers incense here,
The *Five Thousand Words* are understood.
Golden crystal flies past the elbow—
Piercing Kunlun’s heights.

The Clear River winds nine bends—
A single oar cuts through the misty gloom.
Striking water for three thousand *lǐ*,
Ninety thousand *péng*’s journey—
All transforms into the Original Void.

---
**Song: *Jiāng Shén Zǐ* [江神子] (Slow)**
In groves and springs, I cultivate my simplicity.
Freeing my spirit, lazy in worldly ties—
My resolve is iron.

Lofty and detached,
A taste of truth amid idle talk.
By day, I wander—
Wild cranes on the cliffs are my Dao companions;
Beneath the pine pavilion, the smoke lingers still.

At night, I listen alone to the lone monkey—
On the high peak, it howls at the moon.

When my deeds are complete and my path fulfilled,
I ride the auspicious clouds
To the Jade Pool’s celestial gate.

---

**Song: *Jiāng Shén Zǐ* (Slow) – Continued**
When my spirit roams, the *luán* cranes and *hè* herons await to greet me.
Dancing in azure void,
Celestial banners drift to welcome my audience.
At the Peach Spring Gathering, the *qiónglín* feast—
Now I trustfully part ways.

Reaching here, boundless freedom,
As a guest of the *Pénglái* Isles.
Spring descends from heaven—
Delighting in the Dao, content in poverty.
I sigh at ancient heroes,
Who, in groves beneath the trees, find no one.
Their halls filled with gold and jade—
Yet they claim to bestow it upon their children and grandchildren.

Ultimately, it belongs to kin.
Ask why, from the start, with nothing to possess,
Greed and love led them astray.
Early, they should have withdrawn—
To the *Huá’ān Gōng* within the *Kuí’ān* Palace,
Yet they labored their spirits so.

Morning mushrooms and *fúchú* cicadas—
Brief lives indeed—
How could they believe the *hú* jar
Holds another spring of eternal youth?

For now, I roam ten thousand *lǐ*,
Part for a thousand years,
Returning on the backs of *fèng* phoenixes and *lín* unicorns.
Reflecting on life’s fleeting moment—
How often have I seen the *cānghǎi* waves stir dust?

Do not linger.
Those who boast of empty splendor,
Lightly betraying the pure *tiānzhēn*—
Their jade-embrace is but a hollow belly.

If speaking of profound mysteries,
Listen to the *Zhōufēng* teachings in one breath.
Take the infant *zhēn* and the maiden *nǚ*—
Separate them by wood and metal.
Distinguish them from the beginning.

First, subdue the Six Thieves and annihilate the Three Corpses.
Then, capture the Jade Hare to drink the Black Blood of the Ox.
Wield the sword’s edge,
Drive away demonic barriers,
Dispel the *qín* heresy.
All depends on resolve fierce and bold.

Those methods—how most wondrous!
Dragons flee, tigers scatter,
Coming and going, unrestrained.
The two beasts captured—how could I abandon them?
Furnace refining, cauldron tempering—
No pause, no respite.

The supreme treasures of *Yīnyáng* and *qiánkūn*,
Guiding the fate of turtles and snakes.
The East Chicken crows, the West River Moon ascends.
I join the *Huángtíng* in admiring white snow.

*Shàngdān* warms, *zhōngdān* cozens, *xiàdān* blazes.
The Three Fields’ treasures are bound.
All the immortals lift me to the Golden Gate.

The lofty realm of *Liáoyáng*—
How could I ever describe it?

---

**Song: *Shuǐdiào Gētóu* [水调歌头]**
Where the Five *Xíng* are absent, before *qì* takes form—
A resplendent clarity, alone transcending the *Wúhé Xiāng*.
The sun and moon? How could they reflect it?
The heavens and earth? How could they contain it?
Its brilliance is boundless, wondrous beyond measure.

Thanks to the bamboo ravine’s water,
Now I pass the message to the world.

Vague and dim,
Faint and hazy,
Deep and still—
These truths, even with a thousand mouths,
Would be hard to convey.

Cutting off all branching paths,
Excluding every clever scheme,
Mooring the fishing boat.

Ask not of past deeds—
Sit quietly in one furnace’s smoke.

---

**Song: *Sū Mù Zhē* [苏幕遮]**
Gold within the water,
Charging the Ox and the Dipper.

---

**Song: *Yùsuǒ Jīnguān* [玉锁金关]**
Jade locks and golden gates—
Guardian spirits of the Law keep watch.
At the Vermilion Water’s elixir foundation,
Dragons and tigers surge and roam.
All things manifest in their teeming array,
Bursting forth from the Pearl Mouth’s embrace.
Drink the Spirit Elixir,
Master the Fire’s clarity.

When the Great Unity Furnace opens,
Divine light shines through—
Transient fame and gain dissolve like mist.
Act swiftly now to plumb the void’s birth,
Extracting the nonexistent from the nothing.

**Song: *Jiěpèi Lìng* [解佩令]**
For those who cultivate the Dao,
Their labor is no small feat.
Know the Five *Xíng*’s rise and fall—
Reversed or inverted, their order’s lost.
Profound mysteries within profound,
Where the Jade Furnace coils with dragons,
And tigers circle the Golden Cauldron—
Refining the supreme treasure.

When the Yang Spirit departs the body,
Dark and boundless—
In an instant, traversing the Three Isles.
Entering and exiting with perfect ease,
Pressing down to seek deeper mysteries.
Merge with the True Void—
The Great Emptiness is complete.

**Song: *Shuāngdiào Yàn’ér Luòdé Shènglìng* [双调·雁儿落得胜令]**
To feast at the *Pántáo* banquet of tortoiseshell halls,
No need for imperial wine or jade-lined feasts.
Abandon the strife for name and gain,
Nurture the will to refine the nature, perfect the Dao.

Better to sleep wrapped in paper blankets,
Brewing tea and elixirs by the furnace’s glow.
Watch the deer on flower-crowned peaks,
Monkeys bearing fruit from the mountain’s crest.
Ascend to the Celestial Court in the Golden Pavilion of Leisurely Yang,
Rest in peace within the *Pénglái* grotto’s embrace.

**Song: *Shuāngdiào Tiánshuǐ Lìng* [双调·甜水令]**
Hemp ropes and straw sandals, wind-tossed sleeves—
No craving for fame or gain.
Rain hat and fishing rod in hand,
Green waters flowing eastward.

**Song: *Shuāngdiào Zhéguì Lìng* [双调·折桂令]**
A single leaf boat amid the waves,
Seeking the finest streams and peaks to wander.
Lost in whimsy, forgetting all else,
In drunkenness, what matter seasons or years?
Like *Xǐ’ěr* washing his ears by the stream,
Laughing at *Zhuāng Zhou*’s butterfly dream,
A thatched hut in secluded quiet.
Pulling the blanket over his head,
The sun climbs three poles—
Deep sleep, no worries.

---
**其二**
At ease, drifting through boundless freedom,
Gardens become delight, a lone tree as bridge.
Even if wealth and rank weigh heavy,
The sea of strife is vast and turbulent.
Better to abandon gain and fame—
Straw shoes, coarse hemp robe—
No hairpins, no jade belts.
Drink rough wine till drunk,
Feast at the *Pántáo* banquet.
Stroll through cloudy mountains,
Visit fishermen and woodcutters in idle hours.

---
**其三**
Life is a leaf falling from its branch,
A hundred years—
Wasted in darkness, like sand slipping through fingers.
How wasted! Men mistake it for madness.
Riches and honor are like hemp cloth in flames,
Glory like crossing rivers to hunt tigers.
What’s the use of scheming?
Time flees like a shuttle—
Ten years’ life, a dream in *Nánguō*.

---
**其四**
Better to drift like foam on water’s surface
Than seek fame at the pass—
Take joy in rustic tilling, hidden in mist and clouds.
Laugh at *Bāoxū* weeping at Qin’s gates,
Observe *Shàopíng* hoeing melons by *Qīngmén*,
*Yuānmíng* planting chrysanthemums by the eastern hedge.
Midday drunkenness fades to sober stillness,
Sitting alone in the thatched pavilion.
Striking a simple drum, reciting *Dàodé* and *Huángtíng*.

---
**Song: *Shuāngdiào Yàn’ér Luòdé Shènglìng* [双调·雁儿落得胜令]**
For fleeting life, my temples turn white,
Gazing in the mirror, youth has fled.
I’ve cast aside the white elephant’s burden,
Tightened the girdle of the golden fish.
Green willows lean against the gate,
Golden chrysanthemums bloom by the hedge.
I love the flowing water, clear as jade—
Why long for noble doors like endless seas?
Ah, how serene—
Brush the clouds from my sleeves beyond the white mists.
Like *Péngzé*—
Returning in tranquil ease.

---
**其二**
Time flows like water, day and night shift,
Worldly dust erased in a stroke.
All things seen through—
Sleep with high pillows, no care in the world.
When bored, my staff leans past my head.
When hungry, a bowl of alms from a thousand homes.
When idle, wandering alone for ten thousand miles.
My gaze rests on *Làngyuán*’s splendid scenery;
Lifting my head, *Pénglái*’s hidden wonders unfold.

---
**其三**
Honor and wealth flicker like lamp flames in the wind,
Riches are but a dream beneath the *huái* tree.
Just as the Six Dynasties celebrated peace,
The Twelve Kingdoms stirred with war’s chaos.
The human sea teems with false dragons and phoenixes,
The floating world hides true heroes.
Recall *Chǔ*’s *Yuànshuài*, *Zhōu*’s *Jiāng Tàigōng*—
What use is glory? All is but a *Nánguō* dream.

---
**Song: *Shuāngdiào Tiánshuǐ Lìng* [双调·甜水令]**
Refining elixirs in the furnace,
Thunder shakes the *túmiáo* grass.
With moonlit staff and clear wind,
No need for gourd or bowl.

**Look again—midlife has already passed,**
With silver hair abundant at my temples.

What use are heaps of jade and gold?
I live only wrapped in dreams.

---
**Third: The Monkey-Minded and the Horse-Willed**
Only when the *monkey-mind* and *horse-will* are tamed,
Why then do I not vie for fame?
Even as a *goldfish in a scholar’s jar*,
Or a *jade slipper* in the hands of the elite—
I ride a *white horse with red tassels*,
A *public minister* in name, yet free in spirit.

---
**Song: *Water Nymph* [水仙子]**
*Zhang Guo Lao* of the Han:
Ascending beyond mortal to the *sage’s realm*,
Who helped me down the *jade stair* from intoxication?
My *fan* circles like a *barbarian’s mustache*,
My skin red as *clouds of vermilion*.
My companions: *tea, medicine, chess, and lute*.
My hair is *double-peaked* [双髻],
My robes are *patchwork* [百衲].

Once I visited *Làngyuán*’s *Jade Pool*.

---
**Second: Lu Dongbin**
After parting my *drunken soul*,
I descended from the *Broad Cold Palace* [廣寒宮],
Flying to the *Twelve Peaks* [瑶台].
All because of a *yellow millet dream*,
I gained the *transformative power* of the immortals.
At my side, *jade maidens* and *golden boys*.
I pluck *immortal herbs* for a *thousand-year lifespan*,
Refining *elixir sands* through the *Nine Turnings* [九转].
Each day, I *subdue tigers and dragons*.

---
**Third: Lan Caihe**
With *western winds* sweeping my *green brocade robe*,
I stumble drunk before the palace steps each day.
My *hat of official rank* lolls askew at my brow,
I toss *gold coins* in my hands.
I battle and scheme with the *lowly scholars*,
Singing wild songs to the *rhythm of sandalwood boards*—
*"Ah, let me be!"*—
Ever joyous, ever carefree.

---
**Fourth: Xu Shenong**
No love for *thieves or slaves to wives*,
I dwell alone in *smoke and mist*, cold and detached.
I care not for *gold and silver treasures*,
My body is clad in *ragged, threadbare garments*.
My clothes are *tattered and torn*,
My life is *chilly and simple*—
I wander the world at *leisure*.
A *gourd* is strapped to my back.

---
**Fifth: Zhang Guolao**
Hunched and bent, sixty years old,
My snow-white head and beard mark my age.
I roam the *path of red dust* on clouds,
Riding high on a *white cloud-donkey*.
At *Zhào Zhōu City*, I crushed the *stone bridge*.
I lean on a *speckled bamboo staff*,
And wear a *coarse hemp robe*.
Once, too, I drank deep at the *peach banquet*.

---
**Sixth: Cao Guojiu**
A *minister of the Jade Hall* and *Golden Horse*,
Now I am but a *Kunlun Peak* recluse.
No *yellow gold seal* hangs at my waist—
I follow *Lu Dongbin* in idle ease.
Beneath *forests and springs*, I cultivate my *nature* and *refine my essence*.
A *golden plaque* at my belt,
A *winnowing basket* in my hand.
No longer do I serve as *royal kin or noble retainer*.

---
**Seventh: Li Yue**
My *brushwork* does not encroach on *official duties*—
I leap into the *happy realm of eternal life*.
My *fine black robes* are torn to rags,
My *iron crutch* drags in my hand.
My hair stands wild as *pine needles*.
Who would have thought I’d *recline in slumber again*,
My teeth still *snow-white* in song?
Each day, I *drift in joyous, aimless abandon*.

**Eighth: Han Xiangzi**
My life is *elixir cauldron* and *scriptures*—
I have no fondness for *royal ministers* or *prime officials*.
Chaotic, the *auspicious snow* falls at *Blue Swallow Pass*,
Freezing Han Xiangzi’s horse.
Scattered wildly in midair, *Longsha’s* dust.
Black and crimson clouds surge,
Cold winds howl again.
Flowers bloom atop the mountain.

---
**Pure Yang True Person’s Hundred-Character Diagram**
My nature loves *purity and stillness*,
Taming the *monkey-mind* with *steadfastness*.
I drink no wine—
I’ve abandoned desire entirely.
I covet no wealth—
I compete in no *qi*.
Though seen, I do not observe;
Though heard, I do not listen.
I judge no one’s faults—
Only my own afflictions I seek.
When I meet the unruly, I guard my *root-nature*.
In office, I avoid *renown*;
In private, I act with *trustworthy conduct*.
Not counted among men,
I escape the *chest’s oppression*.
Blending with the light, mingling with the dust,
I mix only with *mundane emotions*.
Why do I not vie for *name*?
Once, I debated this with *high masters*.

---
**Poem by Master Liu Langran**
For decades, I’ve been *cast off*, drunk on *vast cups*,
Each day indulging my *nature* until noon.
The *Tail Gate* opens, the *Dirt Mound* acupuncture point transparent—
The *elixir furnace* divides *creation’s authority*.
Only this path to the *clouds* must have its way,
For my fate was never shaped by *Heaven*.
Do not say the *Great Dao* is hard to grasp—
It’s that *common folk* refuse to study *transcendence*.

---
**Second**
For decades, I’ve wandered *north and south*,
Silently practicing *mysterious principles*, refining *truth*.
I seek not the world’s *endless things*,
Only to find *myself* within the *cosmos*.
Having awakened, I know *ebb and flow*—
*Inner Elixir* ever flows upstream.
Even if we meet again after a thousand years,
It’s as fresh as today’s new dawn.

---
**Third**
In *Jingluo’s* secluded stillness,
I dwell in an ancient *observatory* east of the *moat*.
Though *worldly emotions* stain others, not me,
I treat *dusty affairs* as *Dao* treats them differently.
Refining *elixirs* is no labor of a thousand days’ suffering,
Circulating *essence* keeps my limbs ever *permeated*.
What the world treasures most is precious—
Apart from the *human body*, all is *emptiness*.

---
**Fourth**
In my *seeking-Dao* days, chaos reigned—
I traversed mountains and rivers like clouds.
I studied *longevity* by chasing *external things*,
Yet never heard the *True Path*.
My *yang essence* lost its *harmonious qi*,
*Gold and stone* labored in vain, heated by *foreign fire*.
Alas, the *common folk* fail to awaken—
They gladly rot in *wilds*, becoming *mounds of dust*.

---
**Fifth**
Abandon the *Nine Classics* and *Three Histories*—
They are of no use to the *body*.
Better to preserve *original harmony* and *qi*,
And tend the *great elixir furnace*.
Retaining *true essence* will save you from *old age*,
Refining *golden substance* will pierce the *void*.
If you don’t know the *path of longevity*,
What use are the *common folk’s* deluded natures?

---
**Sixth**
Seeking *nobility* and *wealth* is endless—
What use are *high offices* and *extreme riches*?
Better to wield *authority* with *light heart*,
Than to endure *poverty* with *self-contentment*.
Leaning on a *crooked pillow*, I let spring days stretch—
Circulating *essence*, I spare not a hair’s decline.
When we meet again beyond *things*,
Surely we’ll be *immortals* with a *predestined bond*.

---
**Seventh**
*True lead* and *true mercury* are not hard to find—
It’s that *common folk* misuse their *minds*.
*Moon’s shadow* and *sun’s soul* are clear and easy,
But *wood’s essence* and *fire’s timing* run deep.
Nine years of toil refining *essence*—
*Alchemical transformations* awaken the *five metals*.
To leave the world, one grain suffices—
*Kunlun* and *Penglai* will know your *harmony*.

---
**Eighth**
The *double spine* and *dual channels* reach the *crown*—
This is the *root path* of cultivation.
Frequently swallow *Jiachi Pool’s* *jade nectar*,
Let *Zifu’s* *Yuan Lord* ascend.
Make your *qi* surge through *passages and joints*,
Then *essence* will naturally fill the *Valley Spirit*.
When you attain *longevity’s realm*,
You’ll thank the one who first taught you.

---
**Ninth**
Heaven’s net loosely ensnares the *ten thousand forms*,
A pine’s fall makes *Hua Mountain* wither.
After cold clouds pass, a *lonely moon* remains,
When *winter snow* arrives, it faces the *Great Void*.
*Dragon and serpent* return to *Zifu’s* *Purple Palace*,
*Thousand-year cranes and phoenixes* descend to *Cangwu*.
Since parting from my master,
There are few *true men* in *east, west, north, or south*.

---
*Langranzi*, a native of *Qi*.
After following *Emperor Xuanzong of Tang* to *Shu*,
He encountered *Divine Master Sima Chengzhen’s* oral instructions,
Received the *Great Elixir* *Golden Liquid* formula,
And after successful cultivation, returned to *Luoyang*.
Local elders say that during the *Song Endong* era,
*Langranzi* died drunk in *Peach Blossom Alley*.
At the time, heavy snow fell, yet within a *ten-foot radius* of his corpse,
Not a single flake touched the ground.
Officials examined the body—
Only *gold cicadas* entered and exited his *nose, mouth, and ears*,
Then flew into the sky.
All gazed upward, and when they looked back,
The corpse was gone.

*A Daoist of the Wànlíng Cháoyuàn*, *Zhao Yinwei*,
Collected *Langranzi’s* poems, raised funds to carve them on stone,
And spread his teachings.
He knocked at my door, showed me these verses,
And I, having carefully examined them,
Found them no more than *qi-circulation* and *saliva-swallowing*,
*Nurturing yang* and *dismissing yin*—
Consistent with my own practice.
Thus, I happily inscribed this in writing.
*Huángtǒng* first year, third month, second day,
*Fānghú Zhīzú* respectfully records.

**太空歌**
*Mǎ Dānyáng*

The Way may be spoken, yet not the constant Way,
Still and unmoving—eternally preserved.
Guard the cold radiance piercing boundless void,
One offering of pristine clarity, luminous and pure.

The Law may be taught, yet not by any law,
Clear and deep—all conditions extinguished.
Then know: neither birth nor death remains,
Ancestral debts and grudges now severed clean.

What is born? What dies?
Still and clear, clear and still.
Since recognizing such luminous truth,
One knows the nature of thought preserves the life.

Seek not the True, discard not the False,
For in seeking and discarding, cunning arises.
Once cunning arises, the True is abandoned—
Yet fleeing the blade, you meet the butcher’s knife.

Not yet walked, not yet seen,
To extinguish life is hard, yet harder still.
Walk one step, awaken one step—
Without walking, vainly boasting of Chang’an’s path.

You have not yet awakened—do not force praise,
Nor claim the void is one unified house.
When the heart is not yet clear, speak not of the Way,
Like a blind man gazing at a lotus in bloom.

This side fair, that side foul,
Luring the ox to wander recklessly.
If the mind’s eye is not yet bright,
Close your eyes, still your heart, and seal your lips.

No need for hands, no need for ropes,
No need to bind or grasp tightly.
Without intent, the wind’s shadow is seized—
Spontaneously, motion and stillness both forgotten.

Neither clinging to scripture nor rejecting it,
In dual dissolution, inner and outer dwell.
Abandoning the path, speech falters;
Clinging to text, you lose your own pearl.

Mind is Zen, nature is the Way,
Each step contested—how much more?
A teacher’s single finger points to the root—
The Stone Man claps, laughing heartily.

Zen as the lineage, the Way as the ancestor,
Shattering metal, wood, water, fire, earth.
Luminous radiance interpenetrates true void—
Yet laughs at one, two, three, four, five.

Lineage and method both unified,
Only true practice and true virtue suffice.
When virtue and practice are fulfilled,
Only a point illuminates the cold sky.

Neither Way nor Zen,
Fathomless and obscure—naturally unified.
All things stripped bare by the pure eye,
The void resounds, boundless and bright.

---

**悟真歌**
*Féng Zūnshī*

Awakened within awakening, enlightened within insight,
A single spark of luminous light, unobstructed.
Unleash the fierce flame to illuminate *Sādhāra*’s world,
The *Dharma-realm* stretches vast, yet stands alone revealed.

These subtle messages, so profound,
A wooden man points afar—clouds return in vain.
This mystic gate defies description,
Yet seen in the moment, forgotten at once.

Not the tangles of an old woman’s tongue,
But the genuine compassion of wondrous truth.
A moon’s wheel lifted by a staff,
A furnace’s red flame cradling spring’s snow.

I was originally a *Great Awakening* immortal,
With fate, I grasped the ancestor’s Zen.
Returning, a song—no one responds,
Jade bamboos and yellow flowers, natural and free.

In the painted hall, incense smoke drifts fine,
In vain I sigh like *Manjuśrī* inquiring of illness.
At *Caoxi*’s stream, the moon is bright, the wind pure,
Golden lotuses bloom across *Jeta*’s grove.

Shouldering the tiger-staff, I return home,
Snow seals the mountain path—no passage now.
Who at this moment understands my ease?
Only the few branches of plum will know.

Since recognizing the Way of Chang’an,
I love not idle flowers nor wild grass.
Deep in the night, the *kukku* cries on the bough,
Before the wine-jar, spring arrives anew.

At home, effortless joy in non-action,
Every touch reveals sacred form.
Not the thousand-eyed compassion,
Yet the jade maiden plucks forth ancient *Māni*.

What spell could illuminate this truth?
Fathomless, obscure—yet dimly glimpsed.
Ordinary beings fail to recognize this *Tathāgata*,
A lion’s den for the three ages’ Buddhas.

True leisure, true joy—whom to praise?
All are *crane-herons* trapped in a well’s depths.
A lone *kōkin* plucked to silence,
Green mountains still lock mist and cloud.

---

**证道歌**
*Lǚ Dòngbīn*

Awakening to the True yet failing to grasp life—
This is the first sickness of cultivation.
Merely cultivating *xìng* while neglecting the elixir,
A myriad kalpas of yin-spirits struggle to attain sainthood.

Grasping life’s foundation yet lost in ancestral nature,
Like a mirror without treasure—useless.
A man of heaven’s span, seizing yin and yang as his foundation.
Nature and life complete, profound yet deeper still—
A ship crossing the ocean’s surging waves.

Capturing alive the dragon-serpent’s form,
Only then does the artisan’s skill prove true.

---

**得道歌**
*Jǐngyáng*

The Way is hard to enter, hard to seek,
Easy to speak of—who can attain?
False paths deceive the world in myriad forms,
A thousand paths to the Way, yet only one true.

Some who study the Way now refuse to bow—
How pitiful!
Hiding from heaven, earth, and man,
Before attaining, they boast their success.

To become an immortal is not so hard,
Yet immortals must be born of immortal essence.
If not of immortal nature, do not presume,
For every move invites yin-demons’ grudges.

This matter is no small art,
Relying solely on virtue and conduct to shock the dark.

Sever delusion, extinguish greed,
Each step grounded in firm resolve.
If you grasp your true nature and heart as one,
Then I dare speak truly of the essence.

Cultivating the Golden Elixir is easy to begin,
Yet mastering *Zhōngyōng* and the *Yì* is key.
All doing and striving are ultimately vain,
Speaking of dragons only ends in tiger’s harm.

At the origin, movement stirs the body,
If further confused, punishment follows.
Ever recall the undivided chaos before differentiation,
Mysteries unspeakable—nature’s heart is clear.

The body’s every part belongs to yin,
Yet one thing holds yang-essence—man does not know.
Round and steady, it follows like a shadow,
Neither void nor form, yet neither color nor substance.
Dispersed through all things, filling heaven and earth,
Within one thing lies the *Tàijí*.
Retreating, it hides in the profound unity of nature—
Seen, yet unseen; sought, yet unfound.

My elixir’s secret is uniquely mine,
No need for days, months, or years.
No fire’s timing, no adding or subtracting,
No separation of self and other, flaw or merit.
Neither birth nor death, nor anything to cultivate or speak of.
When hungry, eat; when tired, sleep.
At leisure, sit in meditation; when lazy, rest.

「When food is met, it is consumed; when wine is met, it is drunk,
No fasting or observance—only the heart’s clarity remains.

Riches and honor mean nothing to the mind,
Fame and gain, strife and dispute—all are severed.

Still and concentrated, nurturing the *yuánshén*,
No thought arises—true reality is distinct.

True reality is distinct—self-satisfied,
Day and night, the moon within the mind is seen.
No coming, no going—just the center,
Piercingly bright, all eight extremes illuminated.

Neither full nor lacking,
Like a red furnace’s single snowflake.

Though this moment is attained,
Only when void and space are shattered is it fully understood.

Leisurely and free, joyfully unrestrained,
Human vexations do not touch this mind.

Seekers of the Dao, seize the time—
A hundred years pass like lightning.

If not grasped now, great foolishness ensues,
Do not wait till old age when *qi* and spirit are spent.

Swiftly turn back, fiercely cut through—
One stroke, two divisions, blood must flow.
To shed the mortal form and take the dharmic,
Refine this single thought as iron.

These words are spoken with deep intent—
All heavenly secrets are now revealed.
If students hear them lightly,
Fear only regret at death’s door.

**Heart’s Assignment**
For the Three True Ones

Worldly affairs are endless, yet all are void.
Having entered the Mysterious Gate’s teachings,
Work must be done on the heart’s foundation.

Great wisdom is serene, undisturbed,
In the stillness of the unborn—tranquil and boundless.
True essence is silent, unspoken,
Free in the midst of absolute cessation.

To cultivate the eternal seed of life,
First, hold the heart’s foundation firm.
Six senses purified, a thousand afflictions extinguished,
Three realms emptied, all entanglements resolved.

Perception, hearing, awareness—
These are the roots of obstruction to the Dao.
Calm and pure, devoid of desire—
This is the great principle of sustaining the true.

If one is steadfast in learning the Dao,
One must fully awaken the heart.
When the heart is still, solitary clarity shines alone,
When the heart remains, all phenomena intrude.

The true form is neither lacking nor excessive—
Visible even in life;
Illusory appearances, though shaped, are ever impermanent—
What use is there in seeking them?

Knowing all dharmas are empty,
All ties abandoned—
Sitting in practice, this is the Dao’s madness.

Giving aid and spreading kindness—
This is virtue’s deceit.
Great skill feigns clumsiness,
Then one knows all things are effortless;
Good plans are not schemes,
Only let go each and every thought.

Let the single heart remain unmoved,
All actions will be complete.
Each day, exhilarate the spirit,
Truly know life’s joy in harmony with Heaven.

Through spring, summer, autumn, and winter,
Eat when hungry, drink when thirsty;
Or facing wind, flowers, snow, and moon,
Walk steadily and sleep in peace.

If one can meet all things without attachment,
Acting in each scene as play—
The Dao is already complete within the inch of heart,
Why labor through countless lifetimes?

Yǒngjiā once enlightened,
Forced to linger one night before returning;
Lúxíng still doubted,
Wasted time till the third watch came.

Thus, all things are empty,
All dust is discarded—
Beyond nature, no true substance exists,
Before the eyes, all is illusion’s bubble.

Eternal life has form yet blends unseen,
Even spirits cannot fathom it;
The Great Symbol is formless, everywhere present,
Heaven and earth cannot contain it.

Indeed, the fundamental truth is to clarify the heart—
Why toil with weary resolve?
It cannot be borrowed from another,
Only through self-mastery is it realized.

Grand discourse forgets words,
True scriptures transcend letters—
Relying on the crow’s cry to proclaim,
Falling blossoms to point the way,
Stone women teaching in person,
Wooden men receiving the gift.

Shallow minds with little insight
Say, "No, not so!"
Enlightened ones with vast vision
Say, "Indeed, just as this!"」

The awakened dwell in boundless ease,
The lost stumble through thorns at every step.

To seek the supreme attainment beyond heaven,
One must cast aside all worldly concerns.

**Eight Principles of Chan**

Master Feng’s teaching:
Dao has no gradual or sudden—
Chan knows no before or after.
The lost wander beyond eons,
The enlightened stand before their eyes.

Neither coming nor going,
Mastering the Six Powers in freedom;
Neither birth nor death,
Transcending the Three Realms in solitary perfection.

Unshaken by clamor,
Unbound by ease.
The five sects’ disciples,
Cling to fabricated knowledge;
The One Vehicle’s adherents,
Also indulge in illusion.

Only when ever-present clarity shines,
And all burdens are released—
A thousand winds through the pines,
Stone women sing between the branches;
Three moonbeams on the ridge,
Pastoral boys tumble in the light.

Innate wisdom dawns,
Sudden luminosity unfolds.
When circumstances arise, nature manifests;
Before forms, the heart must fade.

The Four Symbols merge,
The Three Talents harmonize.
Green waters flow eternally—
Though you rot and decay;
Blue mountains stand firm—
As clouds drift, they drift away.
Everlasting through ancient and present,
Unwithering, unperishing.

The dull are ensnared by sound and color,
The enlightened transcend all existence.
Scattering wind and cloud,
Caressing stars and constellations.
The hollow lute’s melody—
Wooden horses roar before the hall;
The snow-melting tune is rare—
Jade dragons race beneath the sea.

Do not seek East-West Bodhisattvas,
Nor hunt South-North Amitābha.
Wherever the eye turns, the Dharma-realm is present—
Where is there no Chan?

When one grasps this truth,
Only then may one attain suchness.

Dwelling in dust yet transcending it,
Not falling into the Six Demons’ snares.
Encountering origin on all sides,
Silent illumination returns to primal purity.

Old women’s gossip, a thousand eons of bone-trading;
Direct pointers to the numinous source—
A single absolute utterance.

Seizing freedom, killing and living stand alone.
White clouds and green cliffs—
Every peak is true suchness;
Emerald bamboo and golden flowers—
Every thing is pure awakening.

Erasing all boundaries, encompassing the great thousand—
He who displays the flower to the assembly
Truly overreaches;
He who shouts at the Buddha and curses the Ancestors
Also errs.

Who understands the step-by-step lotus?
Returning from the Deer Park,
The moon fills the riverboat.

Drawing forth one’s own family wind,
Instantly surpassing the Ten Bhūmis;
Shattering the stubborn void’s illusion,
Alone feasting the heavenly hosts.

A worthless fool dares to bicker—
All are but dregs;
Who gnaws at public cases
Cannot fathom profound truth.
Off by a hair’s breadth,
Missed by a thousand leagues.

The Wooden Man says:
*To know the Western Intent,
One must drain the marrow of the Golden Nirmāṇa Devas.*

**On Recognizing Heart and Mind**

If one seeks cultivation,
First recognize heart and mind,
Then awaken nature.

What is heart?
What is mind?
That which perceives is heart;
Thousands of thoughts, millions of musings—this is mind.

Mind arises from thought,
Heart is born from things.
The root of arising and generation
Lies within the inch-square.

This inch-square—
The original true heart.
Heart has no heart,
Mind has no mind.

Because familiar scenes are hard to forget,
The heart drifts, the mind stirs,
And true heart is obscured, unseen.
One must still the heart, settle the mind,
And inwardly observe the heart.

The stillness, unmoving—this is *dhyāna*;
Awareness within stillness—this is *prajñā*.
*Dhyāna* is essence,
*Prajñā* is function.
When both are complete,
They never wane day by day.

**On Serenity**

To love broadly is to be muddled—
Who can cherish purity?
Entangled in myriad cares,
I alone keep one life serene.
Break free from the deepest chains,
Ever dwell in tranquility;
Avoid the gnats and flies’ snares,
Awaken to luminous clarity.

The ancients said:
*Cut all worldly ties,
Uphold the primal order.*
To play in the boundless void of Great Purity,
One must root deeply and stand firm;
To dwell in true simplicity and leisure,
One must rejoice in eternal life and keen vision.

When this truth is known,
The heart becomes clear as autumn water;
All movements in time
Are subtle as spring winds rising.

Standing alone, yet upright—
Silent, yet present.
Unblemished yet not rigid—
Like a mirror revealing beauty and flaw;
Luminous yet without favor—
Like the moon illuminating heaven and earth.

Upright in singular nature,
Calm in the Six Roots.
Numinous purity stands aloof,
Like pine and cypress in virtue;
Lawful vastness unfolds,
Beyond the gate of the Mysterious and Primordial.

In the world, the body returns to the lone cloud,
Emotions rise like wild cranes.
Subtle and wondrous, it hides mountains in marshes;
Beyond thought, it buries elixir in valleys.
Pure and transparent, boundless and free—
The spirit soars to Guishan’s realm;
Self and objects forgotten,
The steps tread the void’s expanse.

Ultimately, this is not the private domain of the Sage—
It is what one makes of it.
If one does not abandon name and gain,
How can one awaken to the rare and lofty?

The great sage speaks leisurely,
Echoing the South Mountain’s words;
The petty man frets endlessly,
Hearing Confucius’ teachings in vain.

As for those who practice Chan amid desire,
Carrying their families’ burdens while preaching subtlety—
They must earn the respect of the lowest fool,
And avoid the scorn of the virtuous.

One must only quietly cultivate,
Turning toward leisure’s reflection.
To exhaust emptiness and uphold stillness firmly—
This is Laozi’s family tradition;
To discard limbs and abandon cleverness—
This is Yan Yuan’s essential key.

When heart and method both vanish,
Life and death are cast aside.
Through pure refinement, the Dao is perfected;
Through empty leisure, the Mysterious is pierced.

Having abandoned the causes of defilement,
The universe grows desolate;
Sealing the breath of non-action,
One laughs among the clouds.

Strange—
Ants toil for food, moths perish in flame.
Why cling to this sinking suffering?
Who would perfect virtue’s nature?

Alas—
Better to hear early of leisure and purity,
And return to the Celestial Metropolis to worship the Emperor.

**On Perfect Truth**

Divine and saintly grace descends,
Mercy spreads universally.

**On the Dao of Perfect Truth**

Having embraced the vast expanse of the Mysterious Teaching,
I now reverently uphold the Dao of Perfect Truth.
Who would have known that the tenfold heights of the High Immortals
Descend to wander in this mortal world;
That the Great Explication of the Three Sovereigns’ ancient Way
Harmonizes with the transformations of humanity?

The roots of virtue permeate all schools,
Yet the heart returns to the One Rectitude.
Those who abandon the secular world sever ties with kin and love;
Those who endure hardship rejoice in Heaven’s decree and accept fate.
Thus, Perfect Truth is both learning and refining the nature.
Worldly fame and wealth, sensual pleasures—
View them as floating scum upon water;
Wisdom and insight—
Hold them sacred as the foremost saints of the Teaching.

For indeed, learning is not a rigid possession,
But a quest for the Great Way.
Amassing abundant virtue,
One extends compassion through skilful means;
Deeply cultivating and preserving,
One attains inner success.
To dwell in non-action’s clarity,
To seek the Way’s unity—
Objects are distinct as the bright moon in a clear pool;
Each response appears as the gentle wind through swaying grass.
All must be discerned in high and low,
And lifted in full awareness.
Learners have causes and fruits;
Those who realize transcend birth and death.
In utmost stillness and harmony,
In utmost firmness and purity—
Unifying the myriad virtues to interact with the world,
Never forsaking mercy;
Proclaiming the Three Teachings to awaken the lost,
Still honoring the wise and virtuous.
In essence, begging is no shame,
Nor is utter poverty a sorrow.
Bending oneself to benefit others,
One bestows kindness upon the aged and destitute;
Upholding lofty resolve and integrity,
One scorns kings and nobles with laughter.
This is the Perfect Truth’s heroic sage,
The Dao-realized Immortal stream.

Sudden enlightenment to Heaven’s mechanisms,
Broadcasts the Mysterious Wind through the Sacred Realm;
Widespread offerings of fragrant bait,
Universally seeks the knowing companions for the journey to the Isle of the Sea.
Thus, seeing clearly into things awakens the heart,
And knowing emptiness realizes the Dao.

**[Learning] the Perfect Truth’s Dao and methods,**
One must adhere to the teachings of Zhong and Lü;
**[Taking] the Great Way’s Mysterious principles,**
One must strictly follow the doctrines of Huang and Lao.
In pure stillness and simplicity,
Refining the Vermilion Elixir to extract Silver Threads;
In pristine subtlety,
Forging the Golden Treasure in the Cinnabar Cauldron.
Discarding false pretenses,
Revealing the natural.
Attaining the ever-more-wondrous essence of reality,
Obtaining the utterly complete True Function.
Five paths of silver clouds pierce the celestial vault,
One radiant wheel of moon illuminates the sky.
With crane’s carriage and golden scriptures,
One ascends to the Nine Yang Palace;
With peach wine and jade nectar,
One takes seat among the Ten Thousand Saints.

Alas—
Some remain in foolish delusion,
Engaged in petty disputes of self and others.
Those who declaim scriptures and proclaim the Teachings,
Do they truly grasp the Mysterious?
Those who deceive the middle and lower ranks,
Do not understand cause and effect.
One must depart the Fire Hall’s favors and the Mountain of Merit,
And withdraw from the bonds of name and gain.
Truly, if one wishes to know Perfect Truth’s essence,
Sudden enlightenment to emptiness is the path.

**The Emperor’s Ode to the Dao**

Within the Three Teachings, the Dao alone is most exalted.
Above, it does not bow to the Son of Heaven;
Below, it does not pay respects to ministers and officials.
Avoiding the secular world, it hides its traces;
Escaping the worldly net, it refines the True.
Scorning the forests and streams,
It rejects fame and profit;
Rejoicing in the mountains and valleys,
It forgets disgrace and glory.
Crowning with the Star Cap, it blazes like the sun;
Wearing coarse hemp robes, it nurtures eternal spring.
Some shave their heads and bare their feet,
Others tie their hair in a knot and wrap it in cloth.
Plucking Immortal flowers to weave hats,
Folding wild grasses to spread mats.
Drinking from the Sweet Springs to rinse the teeth,
Feasting on pine nuts to prolong life.
Singing with hand-drums, dancing until clouds gather—
With mountain companions, sharing tea in friendly conversation;
By riverside gatherings, lifting cups to discuss ancient texts.
Laughing at the vulgarity of lavish wealth,
Rejoicing in the ease of humble poverty.
Not a single hair’s obstruction,
Nor a speck of entanglement.
Some gather in threes to seek the Mysterious and inquire of the Dao,
Others converse in pairs on past and present.
Discussing past and present,
They sigh over the rise and fall of ancient worthies;
Seeking the Mysterious and inquiring of the Dao,
They clarify the essence of their own True Nature.
Enduring the shifts of cold and heat,
Completing the nine revolutions of the celestial tortoise and hare.
Graying hair returns to youth,
White hair turns green.
Carrying a bamboo lunchbox, they enter markets to beg for meals;
Gathering herbs to heal the world and aid humanity.
Some relieve suffering and benefit beings,
Others restore life from death.
Those who cultivate the Immortal Way have bones of utmost firmness and refinement,
Those who attain the Dao have spirits of peerless luminosity.
Forecasting fortune and misfortune, directing strange omens,
Determining calamity and blessing through subtle investigation of human affairs.
Expounding the Dao and elevating the Supreme Sage’s orthodox Teaching,
Applying talismans to dispel the world’s malevolent influences.
Subduing demonic forces with a wave of the hand,
Displaying *qi* at the Gate of Thunder.
Knocking upon Heaven’s gate, the True Immortals gather;
Striking the earth’s threshold, the myriad spirits respond.
Sitting in silent contemplation of the True,
Storing the spirit in a still chamber.
Seizing the refined *qi* of Heaven and Earth,
Extracting the luminous essence of sun and moon.
Harmonizing yin and yang to refine the nature,
Adjusting water and fire to form the embryonic essence.
When the two eights of yin dissipate,
It seems as if lost in a dream;
When the three nines of yang flourish,
It vanishes like the distant night.
Adapting to the four seasons in gathering,
Nurturing the nine transformations to complete the elixir.
Riding the Azure Crane to ascend the Purple Palace,
Mounting the White Crane to pay homage to the Jade Capital.
Drawing upon Heaven’s refined *qi*,
Manifesting the Dao’s utmost devotion.
Compared to Confucianism,
Its officials hold high rank and splendid titles—
Wealth and honor are fleeting clouds.
Compared to Buddhism,
Its joy is in quiescence and extinction—
Yet it does not escape the secular dust.
I observe the Three Teachings,
And find the Dao alone most exalted.

**Record of the Ancestral Court**

The Ancestral Court once had no trace in Japan,
But Master Zhongyang illuminated and expounded the Mysterious Way.
His native home was in Chang’an, the capital of Jingzhao Prefecture,
And his ancestral residence was in the Taizi Village of Liquan.
Heaven sent down the Celestial Diagram, and Immortals descended;
Earth emitted auspicious light, and purple *qi* ascended.
His mother bore an Immortal embryo for two years,
And he was born in the fortunate era of Emperor Huizong of Song.
In the second year of Zhenghe (壬辰), the twelfth month, on the twenty-second,
The Emperor was born.
The Ancestral Master’s parents bore three sons,
And Master Zhongyang had two younger brothers.
As a child, he entered school to receive a sage’s instruction,
And mastered the Nine Classics and sacred texts.
At twenty-seven, he took the military examination,
And deeply understood the arts of war, drawing a hard bow.
With both literary and martial prowess,
He was feared by all.
The Song Dynasty hailed his virtue and might as a world-renowned hero.
His thoughts were clear as a mirror,
His words resounded like a bell.
Once at the Gansha River, he drank wine,
And there encountered two Immortal masters wrapped in coarse hemp robes.

「Five volumes of profound mysteries were received through direct transmission,
And seven orifices of spiritual insight revealed his merit.

Since drinking the waters of the Gansha River,
His heart opened vastly, and his faculties became clear.

At forty-eight, he encountered the True Teaching,
And abandoned the world to embrace the Dao, hidden within tombs.
He observed the inner landscape of reality,
And only then comprehended the Five Phases’ transformative power.

Piercing through the illusory and false forms,
He no longer inquired of mortal omens and portents.

Once again meeting the harmonious Li and dwelling in Liu Jiang,
The three of them resided together through three winters.

In thought, he reflected on the teachings of Qiu Liu, Tan Zhong, and Ma Yu,
And renamed himself as *Wang Haifeng* [王害风].

Fire consumed his thatched hut, and he left the land of Qin,
Departing the southeastern regions to descend to the east.

Three thousand miles away, he found a kindred soul,
And through nine transformations entered the Southern Capital.

The Master summoned his disciples with personal instructions:
“I shall return to the Pengleng [蓬瀛].”

In the tenth year of the Dading era (庚寅), at fifty-eight,
His lifespan ended.

At the *Cha Zi* [查子] shop, he ascended the path to Immortality,
Leaving behind the ancient traditions of the *Quanzhen* [全真] school.

Seven golden lotuses bloom at the hall’s entrance,
The *Changchun* [长春] and *Changjiao* [长教] lineages flourish within.

The teachings of *Quanzhen* [全真] in the *Qinghe* [清和] era are passed on,
And the *Hao* [浩然] sect thrives atop *Panshan* [盘山], south of the peaks.

*Dongzhen* [洞真], clad in white clouds, is the *Piyun* [披云] Master,
With boundless desirelessness, he ranks highest among all Immortal masters.

Eighteen senior masters gather here,
From the *Gengzi* [庚子] era, their deeds began.

Disciples from all under heaven come to lend their strength,
Daoists across the world contribute their efforts.

Heaven bestowed the craftsman *Cao Tidi* [曹提点],
And the halls were built in the *Shuizhu* [水竹] village.

Lofty and majestic, they rise a hundred feet high,
Jade-tiled roofs and tortoiseshell-like windows touch the heavens.

The southern mountain’s lion-like beast spits water,
Four beasts stand proud, their roars like winds of thunder.

Thousands of beams and arches arranged in the Eight Trigrams,
Five ridges and six beasts aligned with the Nine Palaces.

From afar, it resembles the summit of *Xumishan* [须弥],
And in the distance, it mirrors the grandeur of *Taihuafeng* [太华峰].

Above, it connects with clouds and the Northern Dipper,
Below, it descends to the Nine Abodes and Nine Springs.

〔Missing verse〕 The eight rivers behind the ridge all flow east.
A thousand rays of dawn enshroud the precious halls,
A thousand wisps of jade mist veil the ornate palaces.

Once, he saw cranes and phoenixes dancing in the sky,
And heard celestial music resounding from the Heavenly Palace.
All manifestations gathered to pay homage to the Jade Emperor,
The saints and Immortals presented offerings to the Three Pure Ones.

Deep within the crimson glow and violet mist, sealed tight,
White clouds and auspicious *qi* [气] are firmly locked within.

Scattered red peach blossoms and green bamboo intermingle,
Thousands of verdant trees and azure pines stand in harmony.

He wandered the boundless realms of heaven and earth,
And found no place more rare than the *Wang Zhongyang* [重阳] *Wanshou* [万寿] Palace.

At the hall’s entrance, *Zhao Zhenren* [赵真人] speaks:

*"The True One of the Primordial Dao,
Opens wide the gate to all marvelous mysteries.

The *Quanzhen* [全真] Way is fully realized,
And its teachings universally benefit all beings.

The fairy maidens of the *Yaochi* [瑶池],
The golden lotuses of *Wang Zhongyang*—seven blooms.

The *Langyuan* [阆苑] and *Jingong* [璚宫],
The *Changchun* [长春] lineage’s jade flowers—ten thousand leaves.

Though branches may diverge in detail,
All paths ultimately return to the root.

Though sects may vary in flow,
All rivers eventually merge into the sea.

He sets forth teachings in every direction,
Gathering clouds of friends from the four seas.

He sparks the *yuan* [缘] of the Dao in every place,
Summoning the misty companions of the Three Mountains.

Thatched huts and humble dwellings,
All become adorned with precious halls and ornate palaces.

Rough hemp robes and coarse attire,
Are graced with star-crowned caps and moon-trimmed cloaks.

It can be said that humans can magnify the Dao,
Expounding the rules of the ancient sages.

The Dao’s methods naturally align with humanity,
Opening the eyes of future generations.

At the *Liao Zhen* [了真] Hall, no trace of worldly attachment remains;
Under the *Wanxing* [万行] banner, all are urged to exert their efforts.

Those above must act with boundless compassion,
Those below must always hold reverence and obedience.

Worldly disputes cloud the mind,
And fail to grasp the essence of the *Quanzhen* [体玄] Way’s tradition.

Daoist insight unites in harmony,
Following the ancient practice of refining the *Danjiao* [丹肠].

From early times, he was a transcendent Immortal,
Now he serves as the Master’s *fahuai* [法眷].

Do not linger in the fleeting dust of mortal concerns,
Nor mock the precious pearls of a thousand sages.

In life, he shared in cultivating the Dao’s fruits,
And together ascended to transcend the mortal ranks.

The *Chujia* [出家] scholar, with clear vision, delves into the depths.
The *Licheng* [离尘] warrior, with pure heart, illuminates the path.

I humbly pray for your revered care.

*Feng Zunshi* [冯尊师]’s second verse:

The Supreme Dao is boundless and profound,
The wondrous Dao is rare and elusive.
Before heaven and earth, it was already present,
Not confined to words or texts.

Its light is luminous and void-pervading,
Filling all ten directions.
Its purity is clear and spiritually resonant,
Flowing through the Three Realms.

In endless transformations and changes,
It encompasses and governs yin and yang.
Its essence and function are eternally true,
Limitless and beyond measure.

Yet how can mortals, ensnared by heavy veils,
Bear its weight?

Valuing the ancient while scornful of the present,
They fabricate knowledge and understanding.
They debate the *Dharma* [法] and practice Zen,
But only open side doors to the Way.

From then on, the *Taiji* [太极] Primordial simplicity was lost,
And the teachings were divided into three gates.
Within the realm of emotions and perceptions,
They could not return to the origin.

To see these people thus,
One must deeply pity them.

Therefore, the Master widely opened the *fangbian* [方便],
And broadly spread the *cihang* [慈航] of compassion.

He universally rescued beings from suffering,
Freeing them from the six realms of transmigration.

He guided them back to the True Path,
And let them revel once more in the *Hongmeng* [鸿蒙] of primordial simplicity.

He broke open the gate of serene detachment,
And wandered freely through the *Qingdu* [清都] and *Jianguo* [降阙] of the celestial realms.

On the Five Clouds Platform,
He clearly transmitted the *Shuimi* [黍米] and *Xuanzhu* [玄珠];
Beside the Nine Luminaries Tower,
He raised high the *Han guang* [含光] treasure sword.

In boundless expanse, he moves with effortless freedom,
Pure and unobstructed, like the void itself.

In action and stillness, he transcends *wuwei* [无为],
Merging into the undifferentiated essence.

Thus, he can sweep away the *Sadā* [萨埵],
And playfully engage with *Bodhi* [菩提].

Neither death nor birth remain,
No excess, no deficiency.

Both saints and mortals are released,
Embracing the vastness of emptiness and form.

Even if the *nirūna* [泥牛] bellows at the moon,
Or the wooden horse whinnies in the wind,
Or the *lòutòu* [漏透] snares the mind,
Or the *jiāxiào* [作家] becomes a laughingstock—

With fiery words, he scolds the blue-eyed barbarian monks;
In silent illumination, he shatters the golden-maned lion.

The Five-Leaf Flower blooms in full,
And the Three Mysteries are gently brushed aside.
He frees the *Yuanshi* [元始] from its constraints,
And withdraws the *Muni* [牟尼]’s artifices.

He unfurls the *xiàngwàng* [象罔],
And tramples the *nièpán* [涅盘].

He severs the *Caoxi* [曹溪] lineage,
And leisurely resides in *Zhengpu* [郑圃].

Before *Dàmó* [达磨] and *Luóshì* [罗什] were born,
The *Nanhua* [南华] teachings already repelled *Qùkè* [御寇].

Alas, how scholars forget their roots and chase after branches,
Abandoning their own to favor outsiders.

They do not knock at the *Chōngxū* [冲虚] gate,
But cling to foreign *Dharma* [梵语].

Their homeland is secure,
Yet they seek validation in the West.

In vain, they wear out their straw sandals,
Searching for what, exactly?

The stone lion’s heart has been gouged out,
And the wild fox’s drool seeps into the marrow.

」

「When one seeks to practice *chan* and aspire to buddhahood,
Boasting in riddles like *ge teng* vines—
Who dares to deceive others?

Such a gentleman—how then does he guide others?

Now, I casually cast forth the *Dharma* elixir,
Hurling it into the mortal world,
Offering this *tiánhú* [醍醐], benefiting the noble ones.

I uplift the authentic Daoist life,
Revealing their true nature before them.

I disclose some clues,
Entrusting them to kindred spirits—
This family tradition, what melody does it sing?

Not bound by *lǜlǜ* [律吕], yet transcending mortal *yangchūn* [阳春],
A stringless *qin* [琴], yet blowing the *tiānlài* [天籁].

No need for jade threads and gold needles,
To embroider *nícháng* [霓裳] or phoenixes.

Those who grasp this truth—
Returning home, they ascend the eternal gathering,
Where the moonlit towers never sleep.

A bottomless basket draws water,
A rootless iron tree blooms.

This grand design—
How shall it be sealed with official insignia?

At the borders of *Húnlún* [浑沦], no negotiation allowed.
Before the *Língbǎo* [灵宝] peak—who dares set foot?

Only be unrestrained, not entangled in confusion.
Instantly awakening to the Dao’s wind,
Roaming the cosmos in ease,
Long awaiting the celestial ranks—
I humbly implore, hold this in reverence.

---

**The Third [Section]**
*Qín Zhēnrén* [秦真人]

A hundred years of life—
Swift as flowing water,
A lifetime’s deeds—
Empty as floating bubbles.

Yesterday, peach and apricot blossoms on your face,
Today, frost and snow break through your hair.

*Sū Xīnggōng* [苏相国], though bearing six seals of office,
Could not escape the *wúcháng* [无常];
*Guō Zǐyú* [郭子仪], though rising to the *sāngōng* [三公],
Still met the *dàxiàn* [大限].

The white ants’ battlefield crumbles like a dream,
The *zǐguī* [子规]’s cry urges you to return.

Do not wait for calamity to strike—
Only then will you know it was all illusion.

Gold and jade fill the halls—
How can you guard them,
When your children stand before you,
And you sigh in vain?

Red towers, emerald pavilions, high white walls—
None concern you;
White horses, red wheels, golden bells—
All belong to others.

In vain you bind your wounds—
Unnoticed, time’s finger ticks away.

The *guǐshǐ* [鬼使者] do not bend to favors,
*Yán Lǎozi* [阎老子] cares not for human sentiment.

A thousand tears fall—
What use is regret now?

The intestines split into nine—
Who else is there to blame?

At this juncture, rest or not—
Only then do you know the myriad errors.

Melancholy as falling flowers and flowing water,
Powerless to bear;
Desolate as withered grass and autumn winds,
Unbearable to recall.

Yet the wise and resolute—
Plunging into all things, awakening in an instant.

Gold is dung, jade is dust—
To buy the Dao;
Heaven and Earth are turned—
By the hands of the sage.

No more calculating gains and losses,
Measuring dawn and dusk.

Backbone like steel, heels like iron.
Why bother refining elixirs or alchemy,
To return to the *Sāndǎo* [三岛]?
No need for furnaces or cauldrons—
Directly ascend to the *Shízōu* [十洲].

*Xǔ Jīngyáng* [旌阳] lifted his home to the heavens—
Thus it was.
The *Huáinán Wáng* [淮南王]’s entire family escaped—
No other way.

Better to be a high one,
Creating cosmic upheavals,
With ancient-leaping, modern-soaring prowess.

Heart and mouth in harmony,
Mouth and heart as one.
Your name is inscribed at the *Dāntái* [丹台],
Your merit destined for the *Zǐfǔ* [紫府].

If this is mere saintly fabrication,
How pitiful to deceive the virtuous!

I am ashamed of my clumsy words,
Dare not speak further.

Long standing among the celestial guests,
I humbly implore, hold this in reverence.

---
**Tea Ode**

I have heard—
A single thunderclap shakes loose
The fragrant essence of all grades.

Phoenix cakes, dragon clusters—
Manifesting the *zhìzhēn* [至真]’s rare wonder.

Nourished by *yīnyáng* [阴阳], flourishing,
Heaven and Earth in misty fusion.
Drawing the *zhèngqì* [正气] of the four seasons,
Surpassing the *qīngwèi* [清味] of the five phases.

Before spring’s garden, it grows as precious jade,
Before the snow-laden peak, *Zàohuà* [造化] crafts the sacred bud.

The immortal hands pluck it—
Timely use revealed.
Ground in the golden mortar, its aroma assaults the nose;
Boiled in the stone kettle, its blossoms dance in waves.

*Lú Quán*’s seven bowls—
Washing away the six desires’ delusion;
*Zhào Lǎo*’s three cups—
Cleansing all beings from their dreams.

Those who love it find their spirits refreshed,
Those who awaken find their hearts serene.

Do not say this is the *shìzi* [释子]’s tradition—
Truly, the Daoists benefit from it.

Casually sharing this one essence,
I bestow it upon all—
Returning with joy, I humbly implore, hold this in reverence.

---
**Seven True Ones’ Chan Praises and Preface**

*Pīyún Zhēnrén* [披云真人]

The *Quánzhēn* [全真] Dao—
Its origins stretch far back.
Though *Zēng Zǐgǔ* [曾子固] spoke of it in detail,
Later scholars still deemed it obscure.

For *quán* [全] means all things are whole,
And *zhēn* [真] means every thought is true.
All things whole—
Nothing is lacking, nothing incomplete.
Every thought true—
No moment untrue.

Yet to say all things are whole is not yet *quán* [全],
To say every thought is true is not yet *zhēn* [真].
For the *quán* in *quán* is not *quán*,
And the *zhēn* in *zhēn* is not *zhēn*—
Yet nothing is un-*quán*, nothing un-*zhēn*.

When one reaches this stage,
*Quán* and *zhēn* become a single thread—
Yet ten thousandfold, they remain unattained.

Thus they can traverse mountains and rivers,
Move cities, tread fire and water,
Enter metal and stone,
Roam freely, transform endlessly.

This teaching originates from *Tàishàng* [太上],
Transmitted to *Dōnghuá* [东华].
*Dōnghuá* passed it to *Zhèngyáng* [正阳],
*Zhèngyáng* to *Chúnyáng* [纯阳],
*Chúnyáng* to *Chóngyáng* [重阳].

Before *Chóngyáng*, the Dao’s seed was just sprouting,
Few believed in it.
After *Chóngyáng*, its influence spread—
Seven generations have flourished since.

His disciple, *Dōnglái Pīyúnzǐ* [东莱披云子],
After strict fasting and purification,
Composed these *Seven True Ones’* praises.

The verses read:

The teaching’s ancestor, *Zhòngé* [重鹅],
Boldly shed his golden seals.
He bore *Dòngbīn*’s [洞宾] secret precepts,
Drank the *Gānhé*’s [甘河] sacred draught.

Ascending the highest steps,
Entering the *Xuánxuán Táng* [玄玄堂].
He gathered the four friends from the Eastern Sea,
Led the assembly of immortals in the Upper Realm.

The golden lotus bloomed for ten thousand ancestors,
The jade leaves passed on nineteen generations’ grace.
Since the master departed,
The *Zhōngnán* [终南] still holds its fine winds.

---

**The Second**
Leaning on *Dānyáng*’s peak, his triple braids swayed in dance.
Secretly seizing the *Cìyù*’s hidden thread,
Awakening to the *Fēnlí*’s parting words.
He cast aside half a realm’s old possessions,
Answering the *Sānqīng*’s celestial selection.

Before the *èrqì* had yet divided,
He moved where the *wǔxíng*’s reach did not extend.
A thunderclap—he turned and returned,
Laughing, clapping hands as petals rained.

**The Third**
Bowing to the *Chángzhēn*’s lofty truth,
Unbound by petty conventions.
His courage chilled autumn’s breath,
His stance firm as iron.

He cast off worldly ties with bold resolve,
Entered the Dao’s gate with unyielding will.
He inherited *Lǎngránzǐ*’s nine-fold transformation,
Received *Chóngyáng*’s four-word precept.

Transcending *yīnyáng*’s refining,
Unlocking *Zàohuà*’s binding knots.
For ten years, he savored *Luòyáng*’s spring—
Yet casually dismissed the east wind’s tale.

**The Fourth**
Magnificent, the *Chángshēng*’s bearing stood apart,
His elegance unmatched.
Disgusted by dust’s cloying stench,
Awakened to the *Zōngfēng*’s subtle currents.

His heart roamed beyond the world’s mists and clouds,
His traces mingled with the market’s drums and pipes.
His flower-pin adorned *Làngyuàn*’s crimson,
His peach-cheeks tasted *Pénghú*’s jade-green.

Soaring above the surging waves ten thousand feet high,
A spark of numinous light—yet none could see.

**The Fifth**
Truly great, the *Chángchūn*’s virtue shone early,
His youthful purity unmatched.
Alone, he crossed the *Hángǔ*’s winds,
Seven years seated by *Pánxī*’s moon.

Six times summoned by imperial decree,
Four audiences at the imperial court.
His teachings transformed tens of kingdoms in *Xūjìng*,
He did not shrink from wind and snow across thirty thousand *lǐ*.

On *Bǎoxuán* Terrace, he dreamed of immortals—
Dew dripped from pine needles, revealing his return.

**The Sixth**
Called *Cìtǐ Xuán*, he held true essence naturally.
His given name split from the □-bamboo,
His station fixed by the golden lotus.
In June, he stood welcoming the sun,
In winter, he embraced snow in tranquil rest.

Though the rooster was cooked, he sang again,
Though the poison was drunk, his life extended.
He received the *Jīnguó*’s four edicts,
Bowed to the *Yùhuáng*’s two proclamations.

Ask the moon beneath *Tiězhí* Mountain—
Would it share its secrets with mortals?

**The Seventh**
In the *Tàigǔ*’s prime, fortunate to meet *Chóngyáng*,
Rising beyond mists and clouds,
Far beyond fame and gain’s arena.
At *Nínghǎi*’s market, he turned back sun and moon,
Beneath *Zhào Zhōu*’s bridge, he sat unyielding through frost.

Refining the *wǔxíng* into marrow,
Boiling the *Bāguà* for sustenance.
Eighty-four years—his debt repaid,
East wind turned, gazing back at his homeland.

Someone asked: *"Has the Dao of the Seven True Ones ended here?"*
He replied: *"Not yet."*

**The Eighth**
Is this like chasing the fading traces of a swift steed,
Or gathering the fallen feathers of a phoenix,
And claiming them as the whole of horse and phoenix?
Is that possible?

Some may laugh and bow in reverence.
Only the sage knows the sage,
Only the true knows the true,
Only the phoenix knows the phoenix,
Only the *lín* knows the *lín*.

Only the aged Daoist of the Cloud-Cloak,
With his wondrous years entering the Way,
Has served the Eternal Spring for over forty seasons of frost.

He has received the most refined essence of the Seven True Ones.
In his revealed divine treasury of the Dao,
I have heard and seen its depths.

His words flow as praise,
Each utterance divinely resonant,
No idle speech, no empty rhetoric.
If scholars of the world read this,
They will find it a trustworthy foundation without doubt.

**The "Adrift and Free" Ode**
In harmony’s ease, drifting free and unbound,
Preserving life while avoiding worldly clamor.
Familiar with seagulls, swimming in boundless shallows,
Strumming the *sè* while gathering fishermen and woodcutters.

Aiding the *kuī* without shame,
Honoring glory yet unconcerned with high status.
Withdrawing to late fishing, trusting steps with spring’s play.

His robes complete, his silk refined,
His virtue overflows like dew on the *liáo xiāo*.
The *Huángtíng* dispels all cares,
The *Zǐyù* awaits the final dawn.

There, he opens the three paths,
Riding the *fúxiáo* to sport in the nine heavens.
His emotions flow across a short flute,
His firm grasp returns to youthful vigor.

No favor sought, no reliance on rank,
Contentment and leisure suffice for wealth.
He fulfills others’ tasks with borrowed ink,
Yet alone appreciates the *shān láo*’s worth.

Thus, he bathes in the waters of *Yí*,
Rejecting the noise of *Xǔ*’s jug.
With empty heart, he accepts the *zhuó zhuó*’s chisel,
Mingling with the coarse yet unyielding.

When times are adverse, he knows to halt,
In winter’s chill, his resolve never fades.
With nine thoughts at the *jié yī*’s bow,
Five willows left to their wild state.

His partner may till the fields,
He rests, too lazy to bend his waist.
Irrigating the ridges, he gladly embraces the jar,
Forgetting taste, delighting in the *sháo*’s song.

Removing harm weighs less than gold and jade,
He devotes himself to brightening ancestral halls.
His lofty strides outpace the swiftest steed,
With wings raised, he laughs at the sparrow’s flight.

Cutting off learning, he wanders the *xián pǔ*’s mystery,
Singing praises to the sacred age.
Watching the *yú* at the curved pond,
Covering the deer with withered bananas.

Blocking the *duì* is futile in truth,
Deep roots need not be pulled like seedlings.
Unraveling disputes requires steady discourse,
Nurturing simplicity finds joy in boundless ease.

Hiding in seams of profound subtlety,
Like the foolish, he conceals his radiant virtue.
Entering Zen, he kneels at the *jú lóu*,
Scratching tiles with skillful *líng cháo* waves.

Equalizing all things—what true gain?
Sealing the *róng*—can the world be transcended?
Ah, the race of snails in vain,
While crows ascend the lofty trees.

But look at the plowman in common toil,
How could he bow to lesser ranks?

The phoenix’s *shēng* sounds beyond the clouds,
Spring’s hues are teased with a staff’s tip.

Who sets free the carved *yuān*?
The unstrung *qín* self-tunes.
Returning to emptiness at day’s end,
No need for imperial carriages.

**The Hall’s Precepts**
**The White Jade Rabbit**
Heaven, Earth, gods, spirits, and the Five Daoists,
All follow rules to define square and round.
Go against, and paths lead to chaos and confusion,
Follow, and all aligns with nature’s flow.

The Dao has existed since antiquity,
This Hall’s rise is recent.
A nurturing chamber for the Daoists’ refined essence,
A place where the sages’ burdens are cast aside.

Morning and evening, incense burns,
Praying for the longevity of the Celestial Kings and Saints.
Dawn and dusk, scriptures are expounded,
Guarding the *tánnà*’s families in peace and fortune.

Thus, hidden and revealed are beyond measure,
The common and the sage dwell together.
With only a hat and a meal in a gourd,
Living as a *húzhōng*’s humble craftsman;
Alone as a wild cloud or heron,
A man of leisure beyond worldly ties.

Free and unconstrained, drifting effortlessly,
Awakening from the *huángliáng* dream in a single pillow of clear wind;
The *jīn gōng* furnace opened, half the window bathed in silent moonlight.

When deeds are fulfilled and the Way complete,
His body’s subtlety merges with spirit’s essence.
Lying low as dragon and tiger,
He emerges from the muddled streets,
Riding *luán* and *hè* to return to the cavernous halls.

Some may first escape worldly snares,
Suddenly enter the mysterious gates,
Yet their innate nature remains unclear,
Their heart’s foundation still in doubt.

They must diligently follow the guiding principles,
Long practice will not stray from the model.

Serving teachers, respecting friends,
Remembering the Dao, pondering the true.
Always focus on life and nature’s core,
Never let ambition for fame or gain take hold.

Walk with measured steps,
Speak without clamor.
Do not sing of youthful allure,
Nor discuss matters of right and wrong.
For public or private errands,
Lights must not be seen before returning;
Silent meditation, speechless,
Rise only when the bell tolls.

Arriving, clearly state your belongings,
Departing, hand in your items to the assembly.
Any transgression will be met with punishment.
Minor offenses: incense, oil, tea, and cakes,
Severe crimes: exile to the bamboo groves below the mountain.

Theft of even a single coin,
Destruction of robes or alms bowls,
Drinking or gambling—
These are forbidden in the Hall.

Failure in duties shall be doubly penalized.
Thus, these precepts are proclaimed,
Let all know them well.

**Ode of Praise**

The Five Lakes’ clouds and waters,
Mingle within one hall.

Since gathered are the disciples,
Must be made clear the precepts’ framework.
Some are ordinary, some sages—
At times concealed, at times revealed.
Divine transformations are boundless,
The Dao’s rules are ever constant.
In quietude, one may tread—
Yet trust in life’s fate or Heaven’s decree.
No man shall drag you down,
No matter shall arise by chance alone.

Heaven gave birth to me,
Heaven shall take me back.
To heed Heaven’s will—
What could be more fitting?
Times must be discerned,
Things wax or wane.
Man flourishes or declines,
Affairs rise or fall.
Dragons do not leap in winter,
Fireflies soar when night descends.
Noble and ignoble alike—
Each has its season.

Master Kong pondered twice,
Zengzi reflected thrice.
Who am I, then?
Dare I not refine myself?

Words are bonds of trust,
Sun and moon are bright.
Ceasing war is strength,
Lamb’s fat makes fine broth.
Men are wise or foolish,
Matters great or small.
Gain comes not by hardship,
Loss is ever swift and easy.
Doubt not when resolved,
Delay not when decided.
To hesitate when cutting—
Only brings disorder in return.

When others are good, do not seek to follow,
When faults are your own, do not let them linger.
This is called knowing the Dao—
Is it not difficult indeed?

Precious as gold and jade,
Heavy as hills and mountains.
Grace like the phoenix and crane,
Fragrance like orchids and osmanthus.
Spring comes but once,
Flowers bloom but once.
Youth fades never to return,
Time passes never to come again.

The lingering notes of the crane—
Roll them into the ninth stanza.
